Report on the results of parallel checks on the management of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The submitted material informs about the progress and results of parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the NajA Supervisory Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of value added tax management and the use of the VIES information system (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so revenues from value added tax affect not only the state budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
Parallel control actions were aimed in particular at checking the procedure of the tax authorities in examining the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions carried out between individual Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of the VIES system enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of VAT payers in individual Member States of the European Union and on commercial transactions carried out by these payers.
The mismatch between the VIES data and the data in the VAT return submitted by the payer should alert the tax authorities to suspicious cases and allow the detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefits of the parallel checks carried out consisted not only in the exchange of information on the progress of financial or tax authorities in the management of value added tax, but in particular in examining the use of the VIES system in checking the application of the right to an exemption from value added tax in intracomonality transactions.
The lessons learned in the implementation of parallel controls are beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in carrying out further parallel controls in cooperation with the control institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel checks on the management of value added tax for the period from 1 January 2004 to 30 June 2005
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of scrutiny: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and fulfilment of roles under VIES for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO, the Czech Republic) and the Najvyšší Control Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO of the Slovak Republic) concluded the Cooperation in Control Activities on 12 December 2005.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implemented parallel control actions of the "Value Added Tax Administration", included in the control activity plan of the SAO, the Czech Republic for 2005 under No 05/19 and "Control of the procedure of the tax authorities in spiral, control and recovery of dane from the pridé value and pleneni roles within the VIES system on the fabric of information media by the member regions of the ECO", included in the control activity plan of the SAO SR SAO under No 22/2005.
Parallel control actions carried out were in the nature of coordinated checks.
The outcome of the joint coordinated control was drawn up within the meaning of European Implementing Regulation No 31 for INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated check was to verify selected cases of delivery and acquisition of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Slovak Republic (SR).
The two parties have contracted to provide each other with information from public sources, the VIES electronic system (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and data on received and sent requests to investigate business transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial unions of Central Bohemia, northwest Bohemia, southern Bohemia, South Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited bodies were the Ministry of Finance and 12 Financial Offices: Financial Office in Mladá Boleslav, Financial Office in Cologne, Financial Office in Teplice, Financial Office in Karlovy Vary, Financial Office in Tábor, Financial Office Brno III, Financial Office in Znojmo, Financial Office in Zlín, Financial Office in Šumperk, Financial Office Ostrava I, Financial Office for Prague 7 and Financial Office for Prague 9.
The audit on the territory of the SR was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with Expoziturami SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on 9 selected tax offices: Tax Úrad Bratislava I, Tax Úrad Komárno, Tax Úrad Trenčín, Tax Office Prievidza, Tax Úrad Zvolen, Tax Úrad Dolný Kubín, Tax Úrad Košice II, Tax Úrad Košice V and Tax Úrad Michalovce.
Objective of checks:
The aim of parallel control actions was to examine the procedure of financial or tax authorities in the management of value added tax (VAT) after the integration of the Czech Republic and Slovakia into the single internal market of the European Union (EU) and to examine the use of the VIES electronic information system, in particular when checking the application of the right to VAT exemption.
The audited period for coordinated control was the period from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005.
Summary of the results and evaluation of parallel control actions In the EU Member States, an electronic VIES system is in place, allowing tax administrations to check whether the supplier has been entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and makes it possible to check in the country of destination whether the purchaser has properly admitted and taxed the acquired goods.
VIES is not centralised within the EU, each Member State is developing its own system.
The checks identified differences in the national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the following areas:
The recapitulative statements shall indicate the values of deliveries of goods to other EU Member States, the values of the services provided shall not be included in the recapitulative statements.
Data from recapitulative statements submitted by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the tax authorities, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States listed in VAT returns.
The tax authorities shall transmit the data from the recapitulative statements to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In Slovakia, data from recapitulative statements filed by Slovak payers at tax offices are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Slovak Tax Directorate (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of the supply of goods and the value of the provision of services to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT returns, which makes it possible to compare the values given in the recapitulative reports with the values of the supply of goods according to VAT tax returns and to identify their possible differences.
In the SR, the values of goods delivered and services supplied to other EU Member States are reported cumulatively on the common row of the VAT return.
As a result, the system does not make it possible to automatically identify differences between the values of the supply of goods under VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
Separate reporting of the values of the supply of goods in VAT tax returns makes it possible to use the results of the comparison of data when checking the exemption of goods to the EU from VAT.
The supplied data from the recapitulative statements submitted by the payers in other EU Member States are processed into the CLO and compared with the value of the acquisition of goods mentioned by the payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia in VAT tax returns.
In the SR, these figures are sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities themselves decide which cases of differences to examine.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) will determine the quantified differences between the values of delivery and the acquisition of goods must be examined by the tax authorities, and hand over a list of these cases to the locally competent tax authorities.
This ensures that for the most significant derogations, it will be examined whether VAT has been awarded at the correct amount when acquiring the goods.
The audit also highlighted some of the problems in the VAT management system of the complications caused by the different reporting of intracomonality transactions (i.e. the supply and acquisition of goods made by payers from different EU Member States):
Summary reports are made in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum time limit for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
Reducing the period for which recapitulative statements are made for one month, together with the shortening of the deadline for processing them, would allow earlier access to the VIES data.
Tax administrators would thus be able to examine more effectively whether VAT was awarded at the correct amount in intracomonarian acquisitions.
At the same time, filing VAT returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax year (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer has reported the same values of the supply of goods to the EU in the recapitulative statement as well as the VAT return.
The differences between the values of delivery of goods reported by EU payers and the values of the acquisition of goods reported by payers from the Czech Republic or SR were due, among other things, to different reporting of data on intracomonality delivery and acquisition in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the inclusion of received advances in the recapitulative reports, or the reporting of intracomonant supplies in the supplier's recapitulative statement in a quarter other than intracomonality acquisitions in the tax return on the purchaser's VAT return.
A unification of the conditions for reporting these data within the EU would lead to streamlining the control activity of national tax administrations.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was also aimed at examining selected intracomonality transactions carried out between the two states.
Together, a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions carried out between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined, for which there were doubts about their realisation or suspicion of tax evasion on VAT.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the SR found, among other things, the following facts:
the tax authorities have declared in their VAT returns in order to unlawfully obtain excess VAT execution of intracomonant transactions which have not actually been carried out;
tax entities reported intracomonality supplies in carousel transactions in which there was a deliberate multiple reduction in the value of supplies in order to draw on excess VAT deductions;
the suppliers reported in their VAT tax returns and recapitulative statements the intracomonality supply of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare the tax on the goods acquired;
the suppliers made an intracomonality supply of goods exempt from VAT for tax entities that were not registered for VAT in another Member State.
In such cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been subject to tax in the supplier's country;
suppliers reported intracomonality supplies in their VAT tax returns at a higher value than those declared by the purchasers of the intracomonality acquisition, in some cases the VAT was declared in the wrong amount.
The findings of the inspection showed that the VIES system provides tax administrations with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracomonality transactions.
In particular, tax administrations should pay extra attention to the rigorous examination of the differences between the data reported by VAT payers and the VIES data and the use of all information in tax procedures.
The issue of value added tax after the entry of the Czech Republic and Slovakia into the EU
Value added tax
On 1 May 2004, the Czech Republic and Slovakia became members of the EU.
After joining the EU, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within EU territory were abolished.
The VAT administrator was the relevant financial or tax office until 30.4.2004, with the exception of the import of goods and occasional bus transport in the Czech Republic, where the tax administrator was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Law No. 235/2004 Coll.), or Act No. 222/2004 Z. z., on Pridanej Value Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 222/2004 Z. z."), the VAT administration switched the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU Member States from customs offices to financial or tax offices.
The delivery of goods in the Czech Republic under the provisions of Section 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of the goods as owner.
The delivery of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is the delivery of goods that have actually been shipped or transported to another EU Member State.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 64 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., it is an exempt taxable transaction with a right to deduct VAT if the goods are supplied to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The supply of goods in the Slovak Republic under the provisions of Section 8 of Law No 222/2004 Z. z. is considered to be the supply of tangible property in which ownership rights are changed.
The transfer of goods belonging to a taxable person from the country to another Member State shall also be considered a supply of goods if those goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
Under Paragraph 43 of Law No 222/2004 Z. z., the supply of goods from the country to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the person acquiring the person identified for VAT in another Member State is the person identified for VAT.
The acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic under the provisions of Section 16 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of the goods which are sent or transported by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer buys goods at a price without VAT and his obligation is to declare VAT in the Czech Republic under the provisions of Section 25 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., subject to the fulfilment of the conditions set out in Section 73 of this Act, he is entitled to deduct VAT.
By acquiring goods domestically from another EU Member State, in the Slovak Republic, pursuant to the provisions of Section 11 of Law No 222/2004 Z. z., the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of movable tangible property dispatched or transported by the purchaser by the supplier or the acquirer or on their behalf to the country from another Member State.
The tax liability in the SR arises to the payer when acquiring goods in the Czech Republic from another Member State under the provisions of Section 20 of Law No 222/2004 Z.z.
The payer may deduct VAT under the provisions of Section 49 of Law No 222/2004 Z. if the tax is applied by it when acquiring goods in the national territory from another Member State pursuant to the provisions of Sections 11 and 11a of this Act.
Trilateral trade means, according to the provisions of Section 17 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., or Section 45 of Act No 222/2004 Z. trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, where the subject of trade is the supply of the same goods between the three persons.
Intracomonarial transactions means the supply and acquisition of goods made between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intracomonality transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are shown in the following table.
VIES
In order to check the application of the VAT exemption entitlement to intracommunity supplies of goods, a VAT information exchange system has been established within the EU.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows tax administrations of EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and vice versa whether the acquirer duly admitted and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State shall develop its own VIES system.
National systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through the EU's common communication network, the so-called CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was linked to an automated tax information system (ADIS), in the Slovak Republic, with the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "APV DIS").
These systems use financial or tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in tax and fee management.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU member country receives information on tax entities that it would not have been able to obtain on its own without such cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax losses.
Pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State, within the internal organisational structure, provides for a central unit in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the administration of VAT, the so-called CLO (CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance – the Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the International Cooperation in the VAT Administration (MF CLO) was established.
The CLO function in the Slovak Republic is performed by the Slovak Tax Directorate, the International Administrative Cooperation Unit (DR CLO).
These departments inter alia communicate with EU foreign administrations, in particular in the area of exchange of information under the VIES system, the exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of EU tax administrations, the coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax controls, the verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as the VAT Code) of persons registered for VAT in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to examine a certain intracomonality transaction or to obtain other information relating to a particular tax entity, the financial or tax authorities shall send requests for information to the EU via the IF CLO or DR CLO to the EU.
Through these applications, they obtain from the requested Member States information which they can use to correctly determine VAT.
Requests for information are mostly sent between the CLO of EU Member States in electronic form, using the standardised SCAC form.
Selected control findings when verifying commercial transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic was aimed primarily at examining selected intracomonality transactions carried out between the two states and on the level of use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation obtained in the form of international cooperation by financial or tax authorities.
The SAO, the Czech Republic requested the SAO of the SR to examine in 30 cases the commercial transactions carried out between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
The SAO SR requested the SAO, the Czech Republic to examine in 10 cases commercial transactions carried out between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
Examination of intracomonial transactions was found, among other things:
o
The SAO, the Czech Republic has asked the SAO of the SR to examine the procedure of the tax administrator, to whom a response to the request for information was sent.
The Slovak Tax Office applied via the SCAC form to examine the delivery of goods (footwear) in the 3rd quarter of 2004 from a Slovak payer worth 2 847 thousand Sk.
The Financial Office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer had stated the acquisition of goods of this value only in an additional VAT return and had delivered the same goods back to Slovak tax entities worth CZK 2,550,000 by the end of 2004.
Based on the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the locally competent tax authority recognized the Slovak contractor in full the right to excess VAT deduction incurred, among other things, on the basis of this supply.
This tax office did not provide information on suspicion of reexport to tax authorities locally competent customers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
These will trigger further screening of trading activities in relation to possible carousel fraud.
o
The Czech tax administrator applied through the SCAC form to examine the delivery of the technological line to SR worth CZK 4,850 thousand in the 2nd quarter of 2004.
The tax procedure carried out in the SR showed that only part of the technological line was delivered, components worth CZK 3,395,000 were not delivered.
When examining this case, the SAO of the SR found that VAT on the taxable transaction carried out was granted by the Slovak tax entity on the amount of CZK 4,850,000 in the VAT return (hereinafter referred to as "DAP") for the tax period 7/2004.
The SAO, the Czech Republic further found that the Czech payer reported an excessive VAT deduction of CZK 655,000 for that quarter in his DAP, which was created by applying a VAT deduction on the purchase of this technological line from another domestic payer.
Based on the results of the investigation, the Czech Tax Office concluded that the Czech and Slovak tax entities had created a commercial relationship in order to improperly obtain an excess VAT deduction, questioned the execution of the taxable supply and did not recognise the Czech payer part of the right to deduct CZK 647,000.
o
The Slovak tax administrator applied in 2004 via the SCAC form to examine the supply of goods (copiering machines) to a Czech payer worth 24 246 thousand Sk made in December 2002.
The Slovak payer purchased these goods in November 2002 in SR from another tax entity worth 29 667 thousand. Sk and subsequently sold it to the Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity applied an excess VAT deduction for the relevant tax year.
In a tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic, it was found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not file DAP for the 4th quarter of 2002 or for the period following.
The SAO of the SR found that the Slovak tax administrator, on the basis of the result of the tax audit, did not recognise the right to an excess deduction of 5 541 thousand. Sk applied in DAP for the month 11/2002 and set the tax liability in the amount of 1 750 thousand Sk.
At the same time, that taxpayer was not granted an exemption from VAT on the export of goods in December 2002.
o
The Czech tax administrator received an order from MF CLO to verify the value of the acquired goods for the 3rd quarter of 2004.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer was to acquire goods (director) from SR worth 3 767 thousand Sk.
This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, DAP did not serve and VAT for the months 7 to 12/2004 was assessed ex officio in the amount of CZK 0.
The Czech tax administrator asked, via the SCAC form, to check whether deliveries of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic were made, in what quantity and price (according to invoices).
In reply, the Slovak local tax authority sent a copy of the invoice, bills and a notice to pay the invoice.
The SAO of the SR found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with a VAT deduction claim for this supply.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that the Czech tax administrator assessed the response to the request for information received from the SR as evidence proving that the company had acquired goods from another EU Member State.
On the basis of further investigation, the Financial Conduct Authority in the Czech Republic will request a review of the tax liability.
o
The Slovak company supplied goods (wooden products) including to an American company that stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free zone.
The operator of that free zone was listed on the invoices as the recipient of the goods.
In 2004, for example, an American company purchased chipboard cladding worth USD 57,600 from a Slovak payer (at a unit price of USD 100/piece) which it placed in a free zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred the property rights to the Swiss company, worth USD 14,400 (unit price USD 25/piece) and the goods were exported back to the Slovak Republic.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the free zone area on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator initiated tax inspections of individual tax years 2004 and 2005 from the supplier of goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
Examination of the transactions carried out was requested by the Czech locally competent tax authorities through several forms of SCAC.
Individual answers gradually created a picture of the shops and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from Slovakia and the Czech Republic in carousel shops.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO SR, found that there was deliberately a gradual reduction of the value of goods in these trade relations.
On the basis of the information obtained, the SR Tax Directorate concluded that in this case the carousel trade is free pricing (i.e. the import of undervalued goods and its overvaluation by domestic companies located in the chain between the importer and the exporter), which is not a breach of the VAT Act in the SR.
In the current legislation, the payment of excess VAT to export companies cannot be prevented as they meet all the conditions of the VAT exemption law.
o
The Czech payer's VAT registration had been revoked on 12 July 2005.
On 27.10.2005, that body became a taxpayer again on the basis of a voluntary VAT registration application.
The Czech tax entity entered into DAP for the month 8/2005 (i.e. the period when it was not the VAT payer) the value of the purchase of goods (a polygraphic printing machine) from the Slovak Republic in the amount of CZK 1,174,000 and claimed the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to the supply of goods from the Slovak payer in the amount of 1 530 thousand Sk, which the Slovak payer listed in DAP as a supply of goods to another EU Member State entitled to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator asked to verify the mentioned delivery using the SCAC form because the Slovak supplier did not prove how he acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that the Czech taxpayer does not cooperate with the tax administrator and does not reside at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the locally competent tax administrator for the purpose of examining the data.
o
The Slovak payer entered the summary report for the 3rd quarter of 2004 a supply of goods worth 956 thousand. Sk to a tax entity from the Czech Republic.
The VAT number of the Czech entity was identified by the VIES system as erroneous.
By verification in the payer database, it was found that such a DIČ was never assigned in the Czech Republic.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was a performance of electrical works on real estate in the Czech Republic, it was not a delivery of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic, but a service provision.
The services were invoiced without VAT, as the Czech entity told the Slovak entity that it was registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax administrator asked to verify these facts by means of the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, by asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that the tax entity listed on invoices as a customer was never registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, did not acknowledge the tax on the services received from the Slovak entity and did not acknowledge the tax on the acquisition of the goods.
Local investigations and tax inspections have not been carried out with the Czech entity, his current stay is unknown.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity had become the adoption of the service as a VAT payer by law.
The Slovak tax entity will be subject to a tax audit for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2004.
o
The Slovak payer entered the summary report for the 3rd quarter of 2004 delivery of goods worth 1 055 thousand. Sk to the Czech payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was a performance of electrical works on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not about delivering goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic, but about providing services.
The Slovak tax administrator asked to verify these facts by means of the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, asked by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of the supply and a local investigation was carried out with it in order to examine the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
On the basis of this local investigation, it was found that it was indeed not the acquisition of goods in the present case, but the acquisition of services, which was also reported by the Czech entity in a regular DAP.
The tax office further found that the Czech entity, as a result of a poor procedure in calculating VAT, did not pay VAT at the correct amount for the 3rd quarter of 2004 tax year.
The taxpayer shall submit an additional DAP.
Asked by the locally competent tax authority, the SAO of the SR found that the Slovak payer had misstated the provision of the service in the recapitarian report and would be subject to a tax audit for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2004.
o
The Czech taxpayer voluntarily registered as a VAT payer from 10 March 2004.
For the first quarter of 2004, DAP submitted with a high turnover on both entry and exit.
The tax administrator of the locally competent tax administrator initiated the tax proceedings, the entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, so due to the suspicion of involvement in the carousel trade, he was assessed in VAT amounting to CZK 0.
Another DAP has not filed this payer.
Due to the failure to comply with his obligations under the law, his VAT registration was revoked on 4 January 2005.
According to data from the VIES system, the entity was to acquire goods worth 7,846,000 from the Slovak payer in the 3rd and 4th quarters of 2004.
In order to examine the execution of these deals, the Czech tax administrator sent two requests for information to SR.
When asked by the locally competent tax authority, the SAO of the SR found that the manager of the Czech company in the witness statement denied carrying out the transactions examined and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
On the basis of the tax procedure carried out in the Slovak Republic, the intracomonality delivery to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer was questioned.
The payer will not be entitled to an exemption from VAT and will be charged with VAT on the amount mentioned above.
o
According to data from the VIES system, the Czech payer was to acquire goods (workwear) from SR in the first quarter of 2005 with a total value of 39,970,000 Sk.
The Czech payer reported the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in this quarter only in DAP for the month 3/2005, worth CZK 11,292,000.
The locally competent tax authority carried out a local investigation with the entity to examine the data in this DAP.
As the company did not produce any documents, nor otherwise substantiated the execution of taxable transactions, on 9 June 2005 the tax administrator assessed the VAT in the amount of CZK 0.
Due to doubts about the acquisition of the goods, the tax authority sent two requests for information to the SR in May 2005.
According to the reply to requests for information, the tax administrator in SR had doubts about the execution of business cases as well as the implementation of the payment.
The SAO of the SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous checks with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which would be carried out with the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated control, the locally competent tax administrator carried out further investigations concerning the Czech entity in the Czech Republic and at the same time an investigation by the Police of the Czech Republic was ongoing.
o
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of being involved in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (working clothing) were made between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the 4th quarter of 2004 and 1st quarter 2005.
Slovak payer No.1 supplied goods to Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered it back to SR to payer No. 4 (see diagram No. 2).
A)
Czech payer No. 2 was to purchase goods (workwear) worth CZK 4,847,000 from Slovak payer No 1 in the 4th quarter of 2004 and goods worth CZK 17,050,000 in the first quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the locally competent tax administrator sent a request for information to the SR on 25 May 2005.
In response, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the execution of business cases as well as the implementation of the payment.
On 8 June 2005, a request for information was received at MF CLO from SR concerning goods worth 16 575 thousand. Sk, which was to be delivered in December 2004 by Slovak payer No. 1 to Czech payer No. 2.
The Slovak side demanded to check whether Czech payer No 2 had actually accepted the goods, admitted it in DAP and paid VAT.
An official record drawn up by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that Czech payer No 2 has not been stationed at an address registered in the Commercial Register for a long time.
Although they were VAT payers with a monthly tax period, they served the DAP for a quarterly tax year.
In view of this fact, the Czech tax administrator could not assess VAT.
The realisation of the taxable supply between Slovak payer No 1 and Czech payer No 2 mentioned in the application in the amount of 16 575 thousand. Sk could not be verified due to the above facts.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel trade in order to draw an excess VAT deduction.
B)
Czech payer No 3, engaged in the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed a DAP for the tax period of the months 1 and 2/2005 in which he reported delivery of goods (workwear) to the Slovak payer No 4 with a total value of CZK 21,935,000.
These working clothes were to be purchased by Czech payer No 3 from Czech payer No 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The locally competent tax authority sent a request for information to the SR, which was mainly to verify whether Slovak payer No 4 had purchased goods worth CZK 1,025,000 from Czech payer No 3 in December 2004 and CZK 21,935,000 in the first quarter of 2005.
The reply to this request for information received from the SR showed that in DAP for month 12/2004 Slovak payer No 4 stated the zero value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in DAP for months 1 and 2/2005 stated the value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the amount of only 1 193 thousand Sk.
The invitation to submit tax documents for the tax period of the months 10/2004 to 3/2005 did not respond to Slovak payer No 4.
In the local investigation carried out in SR, it was found that the company was not at the address mentioned in the Commercial Register.
The reply further stated that this payer fulfils all the characteristics of the so-called "lost society" and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO of the SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent DR CLO an initiative to carry out simultaneous checks with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which would be carried out by the participating tax entities.
During the coordinated check, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or refute the existence of the goods.
VAT will be measured against the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also being handled by the Police of the Czech Republic.
The course of the inspection
As part of the preparation of parallel control actions, a coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic with representatives of the SAO, took place in the first half of July 2005.
Participants in this meeting became aware of the VAT legislation in both states and the integration of the VIES electronic system into national databases.
The result of the negotiations was a specification of the scope of cooperation and the setting of conditions for the selection of control samples.
The two parties agreed that the cooperation will focus on the following areas: (a) verification of the validity and correctness of VAT officers registered in the Czech Republic or SR for intracomonality supplies; (b) verification of data on intracomonant acquisitions listed in the DAP by payers in the Czech Republic using information from recapital reports (hereinafter referred to as "SH") of SR payers contained in the VIES system; and vice versa; c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and in the Slovak Republic on commercial transactions carried out.
It was also agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection would be carried out following the volume of intracomonality deliveries between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and according to the number of applications for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and Slovakia via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intracomonative transactions
The process of processing information by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia in intracomonial delivery and acquisition of goods illustrates the following diagram.
5.1.1 Intracomonant delivery
If the VAT payer makes an intracomonality delivery, he is obliged to file SH until the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic gives in SH summary information about the supplies of goods made by him to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The Slovak payer is obliged to indicate to SH the value of goods that have been exempt and delivered from the country to other EU Member States for the calendar quarter period.
Data on the value of the delivered goods are always shown in SH in the Czech or Slovak currency, broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their VAT number under which they were registered in their country.
Data on services are not included in SH.
If a payer in the Czech Republic finds that he has given erroneous data in SH, he is obliged to submit subsequent SH.
In the event that the payer in the SR finds that the data referred to in SH were incomplete or incorrect, he shall lodge a corrective SH before the expiry of the deadline for the submission of SH, after that period he is required to submit an additional SH.
VIES allows the exchange of information on VAT registered users' registration data in EU Member States.
Payers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia can check whether the VAT number of the relevant acquirer is registered in a given EU Member State.
Data from the submitted SH are grouped on MF CLO or DR CLO by the VIES system according to the individual VAT number of the purchasers.
The aggregate value of all deliveries for each DIČ of the acquirer and the code of the method of performance from all its Czech or Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files, will be created.
Data from the L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intracomonality transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia (from L1QD files) is given in the following table.
If the VIES system in another Member State detects the erroneous TIN of the maker in the L1QD files sent, it generates the so-called O_MCTL message, which contains all the faulty VAT number indicating the type of error.
This message is then sent to MF CLO, respectively DR CLO.
The O_MCTL report may contain 4 types of errors: formally erroneous VAT number, VAT number is not registered in that state or has never been allocated, the customer with a particular VAT number was not a VAT payer in the given quarter, the VAT registration of the customer was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, MF CLO transmits data from received O_MCTL reports to the tax authorities.
If the wrong EU payer's VAT number is used in one of the SH or subsequent SHs sent lines, the so-called "Notice on the VAT ID" is generated at the relevant tax office by ADIS.
The tax office will examine whether the delivery to the VAT registered payer in another EU Member State has actually taken place and will record the result of the verification in the system.
In the SR, DR CLO will process all O_MCTL messages in VIES and electronically send them to the locally competent tax authorities together with the identification of tax payers who have reported the wrong VAT number in their SHs.
Tax authorities subsequently call on the payer to file an additional SH and give a valid VAT number, or the tax office, when reporting an invalid VAT number in the filed SH, will examine the delivery of the goods at the relevant payer.
Data on the number of erroneous DIČs relating to intracomonality transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are given in the following table.
Of the total number of 41,728 VAT number of Czech payers, listed in SH Slovak payers between the 2nd quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005, 929 were erroneous DIČs, i.e. 2.23%.
Of the total number of 62 997 VAT number of Slovak payers listed in SH Czech payers in the same period, 416 were erroneous DIČ, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intracomonality transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, Czech VAT payers reported on average fewer erroneous VAT numbers in their SH than Slovak payers.
When examining the activities of financial or tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of tax entities in all cases.
E.g.:
- Although, when asked by the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax entity in Q4 2004, the O_MCTL report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the registration of the payer in this quarter.
The investigation revealed that the end of the marketing authorisation did not take place until 1 January 2005;
- The SAO of the SR further found that 6 tax entities were submitted by SH, which reported the wrong VAT number, but the O_MCTL reports did not contain this VAT number.
In the SR, the submitted SHs shall be transferred to the tax authorities in electronic form and the data from them shall be sent to DR CLO.
Following the subsequent processing of these data in the VIES system, DR CLO will send to the relevant tax authorities so-called breakdowns of errors in SH submitted by tax entities for the relevant quarter.
The SAO of the SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in SH as of 26 July 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the inspection procedure) and to 2.2.2006 (i.e. data processed after the end of the inspection procedure).
The data comparison is provided in the following table.
From the above data it can be seen that the audit of the SAO of the SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SHs with the wrong VAT number (average by 199 SH per quarter), but also on the reduction of the number of unrepaired errors in SH (on average by 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intracomonant supplies listed by the payer in the respective DAP lines is compared at the tax authorities with the intracomonality delivery value given by this payer in the quarterly SH.
ADIS automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should examine the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the data obtained to determine the tax liability.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that the audited tax authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The overall difference between the values shown in SH and DAP was CZK 537,231,000 in these cases.
Since the 3rd quarter of 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values shown in SH and DAP of up to 0.5% of the total value of intracomonarian supplies according to SH as a match and set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intracomonality deliveries for one quarter, 0.5% of the value represents a not insignificant amount, therefore tax administrations should not set the compliance of SH and DAP in these cases without clarifying the causes of the differences.
For example, the tax administrator without verification set the match in case of a difference of values in the amount of CZK 1,561,000.
The examination of differences in the Czech Republic and Slovakia was complicated by the fact that SH was administered by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter for each calendar quarter.
For taxpayers with a monthly tax period at the time of DAP's submission for the first two months of the calendar quarter, tax administrators could not compare the intracomonal delivery values given in these DAPs with those according to the SH.
In these cases, the tax administrators only became aware of any mismatch of the data in the DAP and SH when the tax liability or excess VAT deduction was assessed or refunded.
5.1.2 Intracomonity acquisition
The VIES system provides, inter alia, information on the values of intracomonality transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, data delivered from SHs delivered by payers from other EU Member States (delivered L1QD) are processed by MF CLO.
During processing, the data are recalculated by the Czech National Bank's minimum and maximum daily exchange rates for the relevant period and are then compared to the acquisition value given by Czech payers in DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods recognised by the payer in DAP should be within the minimum and maximum recalculated value of L1QD (L1min and L1max values).
If the value shown in the DAP is less than L1min, the so-called verification order is generated for the payer with the most significant irregularities.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax entities and are transmitted to the locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of authentication orders relating to the audited tax authorities in the Czech Republic is given in the following table.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that the audited tax authorities in 33 cases did not examine irregularities in the values of intracomonality acquisitions to which the audited orders were pointed out.
The overall difference between the values shown in SH payers from other EU Member States and DAP of Czech payers was at least CZK 148,319,000 in these cases.
The SAO, the Czech Republic has selected 533 files of tax entities for inspection, for which the audited tax authorities received a verification order from the I.F. CLO.
The inspection identified the following most common causes of differences between the values given in the DAP of the acquirer and in SH of the supplier: on the side of the acquirer (Czech payer) in 263 cases the acquirer did not indicate the acquisition of goods in regular DAP, in 93 cases the payer admitted the acquisition of goods in a different tax year than in which he was liable to declare the tax, in 6 cases the acquirer stated the value of the acquired goods in the incorrect line of DAP, on the part of the supplier (the EU payer) in 88 cases the payers from the EU in their SHI included the values of the services provided to the Czech payer, of which in 54 cases were the supplier from the SBCs, in 88 cases of the supplier in the Czech Republic, the supplier from the Czech Republic included the values of the services provided to the Czech payer in the Czech Republic, of which in 54 cases were the payers from the SR, included the supply of the goods in the SBCs in 88 cases of the supplier
On the side of the payers from the SR, the value of the services provided in SH was most often incorrectly included.
54 such cases were found at the audited tax offices.
For example, when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974,000 arose from the Slovak payer introducing the provision of services to SH for the first quarter of 2005 (construction work and delivery of goods, including assembly on the territory of the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of accepted advances into SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers gave in SH the advances received from Czech payers, resulting in a command to verify the difference of CZK 3,580,000.
Orders to verify goods acquired are generated only once in one quarter.
In cases where data from SHs are subsequently changed in EU Member States, such as a change in the customer of goods in the Czech Republic or the increased value of deliveries of goods to the Czech Republic, new authentication orders are not generated.
As the VIES does not automatically draw attention to these changes, the locally competent tax authorities need not know the purchaser of the goods without any other complaint about the facts relevant for the correct determination of the tax liability on the goods acquired and there is a strong likelihood of VAT evasion.
An audit of the SAO, the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
The Slovak payer gave the value of the supply of goods to the Czech payer in SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 in the amount of 1 504 thousand Sk.
On 1 February 2005, the tax office sent a request for information to the locally competent Czech payer to the SR, as the Czech payer admitted the acquisition of the goods only in the amount of CZK 425,000.
On the basis of the tax proceedings, the Slovak payer filed an additional SH on 1 January 2005, correcting the data on the supply of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the supply for the originally listed Czech payer to 538 thousand. Sk and increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from the sum of 194 thousand Sk.
Four Slovak payers reported intracomonarian delivery to payers from the Czech Republic totalling 10,24 thousand Sk (i.e. CZK 8,183,000) in their SH for the second quarter of 2004.
However, Czech buyers did not report intracomonarian acquisition in DAP.
Based on the international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer, which was not mentioned in SH submitted by Slovak payers.
During the first quarter of 2005, Slovak payers in additional SHs related to the 2nd quarter of 2004 increased the value of intracomonant delivery for this Czech payer by a total of 10,24 thousand Sk.
In view of the above, the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data in the submitted DAP for the second quarter of 2004, even though the actual acquirer did not comply with the obligation to grant an intracomonality acquisition for this quarter.
The SAO, the Czech Republic found that, on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the aforementioned Czech taxpayer was additionally charged VAT for the tax period 5 and 6/2004 in the amount of CZK 3,640 thousand and for the 3rd quarter of 2004 in the amount of CZK 3,305,000 from the goods acquired in these periods.
From the above, it can be seen that tax authorities had to examine in tax proceedings not only the differences caused by errors in the DAP of the purchaser, but also the differences caused by the different reporting of intracomonality and acquisition data in individual EU Member States.
A unification of the conditions for reporting these data would lead to a streamlining of the control activity of tax administrators.
Acquisition of goods in SR
In the SR, APV DIS makes it possible to compare data on the value of goods acquired through the VIES system from other EU Member States with those listed in the DAP of Slovak buyers.
The method by which data is compared is called "Method MIN-MAX".
This method will recalculate the value of deliveries of goods listed in SH payers from other EU Member States with a minimum and maximum exchange rate for the relevant quarter.
There will be an MIN-MAX interval, which is used for comparison with the purchase values of goods listed in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DR CLO will send the tax administrators information on the intracomonality acquisition values set out in the DAP and the values of the delivery from the EU in VIES.
The tax administrator will decide for which VAT registered persons the difference will be examined, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
On the basis of data provided by DR CLO, the SAO SR selected 57 files of Slovak purchasers of goods for inspection at audited tax offices, of which 25 were also purchased by goods from the Czech Republic, for which the highest differences were found between the values of acquisition obtained from the VIES system and the values declared in DAP.
The SAO audit of the SR SAO confirmed the fact that the tax authorities did not consistently examine the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and did not check the accuracy of the data listed in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
As part of the audit, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations with specific tax entities.
During the SAO's audit at tax offices, 31 local investigations were terminated.
For Slovak companies, to which the VIES system showed significant differences in MIN-MAX values when acquiring goods from EU Member States, the following facts were identified, among other things:
In DAP for the fourth quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer did not disclose the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The tax office found that the company from the Czech Republic accidentally listed this payer's VAT number in SH for the 4th quarter of 2004, while it actually delivered the goods worth CZK 19,184,000 to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, the Slovak company was to purchase goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria in the 4th quarter of 2004 worth MIN 682 692 thousand. Sk and MAX 715 105 thousand Sk.
This company submitted the DAP for the periods in which it stated the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU only amounting to 480,599 thousand Sk.
The tax administrator conducted a local investigation, finding that the tax entity purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP intracomonarian deliveries did not state according to the date of invoice issuance, but according to the date of delivery.
In view of other irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU states, the tax administrator will request an examination of the value of the delivered goods through the SCAC forms.
The acquisition of goods from EU member states in the 4th quarter of 2004 did not mention the Slovak payer in DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer was to purchase goods worth MIN 11,286 thousand Sk and MAX 11 845 thousand Sk.
The tax office carried out a local investigation, the inspection showed that the tax entity did not acquire any goods from EU member states in the 4th quarter of 2004.
The SAO SR recommended that the tax authority request to examine the delivery of goods from EU Member States via the SCAC form.
The VIES system reported delivery of goods to a Slovak customer worth MIN 557 thousand. Sk and MAX 565 thousand Sk.
In the DAP for the tax year 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not show any acquisition of the goods.
A local investigation by the tax administrator found that the tax entity received an invoice from a supplier from the Czech Republic on 10 December 2004 for the material consumed in repairing the hydraulic loader.
The SAO SR recommended carrying out a tax audit on the payer.
During the audit of the SAO SR in 16 cases, the tax authorities did not terminate the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the SAO SR asked the tax administrator to carry out a tax audit on tax entities.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax inspections will be filed by the tax authorities after they have been carried out by the SAO SR.
These were, for example, the following cases:
The Slovak acquirer did not declare in DAP for the fourth quarter of 2004 the acquisition of goods from EU Member States and did not grant any tax for the tax period of the months 10 to 12/2004 and claimed a refund of the excess VAT deduction in the total amount of 1 236 thousand Sk.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation, which showed that the tax entity had purchased goods worth 683 thousand euro (approx. 27,080 thousand Sk) from the Czech Republic.
These goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to customs in Čiernej nad Tisou, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak customer payer in the Russian Federation issued an invoice for the amount of EUR 683 thousand, which he did not mention in the filed DAP.
For the tax entity, the tax administrator carries out a tax inspection.
The difference between the acquisition data reported in the Slovak payer's DAP for the 3rd quarter of 2004 to Q1 2005 and the delivery data reported by EU Member States in each quarter was a total of 4,800 thousand Sk.
The tax office found that the tax entity purchased goods from suppliers from the Czech Republic and Belgium and subsequently sold these goods to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by the export uniform customs declarations.
The acquisition of goods in the DAP was not reported by the tax entity, according to the company's manager, the goods under the transit procedure were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine.
The taxpayer did not submit any VAT records in respect of the local investigation.
Tax control was initiated at the payer.
5.2 International exchange of L3 Level Information
The exchange of information at L3 level is initiated by the locally competent tax authorities, who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as the SPI) or spontaneous information (SPI) relating to a particular tax entity or transaction, by means of MF CLO or.
DR CLO to another EU member country. The aim of the ŽOI is, for example, to prove the execution of a given transaction within intracomonality transactions, verification of a particular VAT number, etc.
In the case of the SPI, it is a communication of information relevant to tax administrations in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to the ROI was set in Article 8 of this Regulation for 3 months.
The conditions for admissibility of applications are governed by the Decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15.11.2004, which provides that, unless the participating States agree otherwise, the RHI must relate to commercial transactions worth at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
Where the ROI relates to a commercial transaction of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to respond in view of its workload.
The procedure for processing received ŽOI by the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including the indication of internal time limits set for processing at individual organizational levels, illustrates the following diagram.
In the SR, the deadline for the processing of ŽOI by the tax authorities was set internally for 2 months so that the three-month period under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 could be met.
MF CLO received a total of 29 ŽOI and 3 SPI from SR from 1 May 2004 to 30 June 2005.
Of the 29 ŽOI received, 26 (i.e. 89.7%) were processed within the time limit of 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10.3%) were dealt with after that period.
In the same period, DR CLO from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 ŽOI received, 64 (i.e. 90.1%) were processed within the deadline of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were dealt with after that period (for the other 2 cases, it was not possible to determine the processing time from the submitted materials).
More detailed data on the time of processing of ŽOI received MF CLO or DR CLO contains the following chart.
The reasons for sending the ŽOI, given on the SCAC forms, are provided in the following table.
Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT has been examined, as well as the use of the VIES system to exchange information between EU Member States, in particular when checking the application of the right to VAT exemption.
International cooperation made it possible to examine selected intracomonality transactions carried out between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
By examining the selected transactions, it was found that, on the basis of an international exchange of information, the tax administrations of both countries revealed cases of companies that carried out fictitious intracomonal commercial transactions to obtain excess VAT deductions, as well as cases where the purchasers did not declare VAT on the received supplies of goods at the correct amount.
Furthermore, the checks identified differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of both countries.
The audit also highlighted the problems caused by different reporting of data on intracomonality deliveries and purchases of goods in individual EU Member States.
A unification of the conditions for reporting these data within the EU would lead to streamlining the control activity of national tax administrations.
By examining the procedure of the financial or tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system, it was found that the financial or tax authorities did not sufficiently use all the possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal permissions.
Furthermore, it was found that the VIES did not provide up-to-date information on the supply of goods and the validity of the VAT registration of tax entities in all cases.
The SAO SR compared data on the occurrence of erroneous data in SH, processed before the start of the inspection performance, with data processed after the completion of the inspection performance.
It was clear from the comparison of these data that the audit of the SAO of the SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SHs with the erroneous VAT number, but also on the reduction of the number of unrepaired errors in SH.
In the case of irregularities in the reported data of the SAO SR, it asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations or to carry out tax inspections.
The SAO, the Czech Republic did not have such an option under the current legislation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the control actions obtained showed that the VIES system provided tax administrations with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracomonality transactions.
As there continues to be scope for tax evasion in this area, there is a need for increased attention to intracomonality transactions in the VAT administration.
Communications
This report was prepared in the Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the chairman of Najýššie's control department of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duty between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material gives an overview of the progress and results of parallel control actions carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Najk control úradom of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the management of value added and excise duties.
Cooperation between the highest control authorities of both countries was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement in control activities concluded in February 2004.
The subject of parallel control actions has been selected in view of the fact that indirect taxes account for a significant contribution to the revenues of the two countries' state budgets.
The design of value added tax, allowing the refund of excess deduction, provides scope for tax fraud or evasion.
High excise duty rates, especially for tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation by illegally selling these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other European Union countries.
Due to the need to address this issue comprehensively across the European Union, the highest control institutions of the European Union Member States have been set up by the VAT Working Group, in whose activities the highest control offices of both countries are actively involved.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in a joint effort to identify problem areas of indirect tax administration in order to limit the scope for tax evasion.
The experience gained and knowledge will be used in the framework of planned indirect tax inspections, mainly aimed at involving both Member States' tax administrations in the VIES system, to control the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the control of the management of value added tax and excise duties for the period 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject-matter of the inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duty
(SK) Control of the procedure of the tax administrator in the administration, control and recovery of value added tax and excise duty
On 11.2.2004 the Cooperation Agreement was concluded in control activities between the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the Najvyšší audit úradom of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO of the Slovak Republic"). The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implemented parallel control actions "Value added tax and excise duty tax", included in the auditing plan of the SAO for 2004 under No 04/07 and "Control of the procedure of the administration dane pri správe, control and recovery of dane from the pridé value and spotreb taxes", included in the control activity plan of the SAO SR under No 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent provided for in the contract and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
In the contract, the two parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the customs administration database and from the files of tax entities held by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the contracting parties were unable to obtain when checking the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the relevant state.
The checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
In the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic), the inspection was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial unions of southern Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected Financial Offices: Financial Office for Prague 1, Financial Office for Prague 3, Financial Office in České Budějovice, Financial Office in Frýdek-Místek, Financial Office in Hodonín, Financial Office in Jihlava, Financial Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, Financial Office in Kroměříž, Financial Office in Písek, Financial Office in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, Financial Office in Velke Meziříčí.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SR") was carried out by the Section of Tax and Customs Administration of the SAO of the SR in cooperation with Exposituras of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
Tax Úrad Bratislava pre selected tax entities, Tax Úrad Bratislava III, Tax Úrad Trnava, Tax Úrad Pú-chov, Tax Úrad Banská Bystrica I, Tax Úrad Liptovský Mikuláš, Tax Úrad Žilina I, Tax Úrad Žilina I, Tax Úrad Žilina II, Tax Úrad Košice I and Tax Úrad Košice IV.
Objective of control
The aim of the control actions was to examine the fulfilment of the obligations of financial or tax authorities and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise duty, with a focus on the collection of these taxes on the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the customs database of the Czech Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns at the relevant financial or tax offices.
The audited period was 2002 and 2003.
2. Recapitulation of control results
2.1. 2.1. General evaluation of control activities
As part of the SAO's international cooperation, the SAO of the Slovak Republic handed over 22,206 items of uniform customs declarations (hereinafter referred to as "JCD") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, and vice versa, the SAO of the SR, handed over 30 221 JCD items from the SR customs database.
A comparison of the drafted JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic was made.
Of the 5 883 selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic, a total of 43% of the related JCD items were assigned.
Of the 12,343 selected JCD items from the SR customs database, a total of 26% of the related JCD entries were assigned.
Based on the unassigned JCD items, financial or tax offices selected files of tax entities for which reported imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Based on the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak and financial or tax authorities, the implementation of reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia was verified on the territory of the second state.
The SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic carried out a joint pilot inspection at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma, in which the two interested parties cooperated closely in verifying the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The inspection did not identify deficiencies in the register of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine trade transactions carried out between trading partners from both states and pointed to shortcomings in the import and export records.
2.2. Summary of the results of the inspection
Control of the SAO and SAO SR in the field of international cooperation focused on imports and exports of spirits and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, and possibly other types of goods.
On the basis of an examination of the files of tax entities at selected financial or tax offices, the SAO asked for verification of the implementation of exports of goods declared at 40 JCD with a total statistical value of CZK 15,010,093 and the SAO SR to verify exports at a statistical value of 56 989 Sk.
The SAO and the SAO of the SR found, among other things, the following facts:
- trade transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the SR customs database,
- the error rate in entering data in customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- for some exports from the Czech Republic, corresponding imports into the Slovak Republic have not been demonstrated.
In such cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of unauthorising application of value added tax deductions,
- Tax entities did not comply with certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- deficiencies were identified in the activities of financial or tax authorities in the management of value added tax and excise duties and in their interaction with the customs authorities.
In the area of value added tax and excise duties, attention will continue to need to be paid to international trade in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activities of tax administrators in the exercise of value added tax administration.
The basis for effective control of excise duties is to check the circulation of documents, systematic physical control of goods and the mutual exchange of information on the import and export of goods.
3. Description of the state of value added tax and excise duties
Value added tax
Value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") was levied by financial or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out domestically and by customs authorities on the importation of goods.
Tax revenues for financial or tax authorities were determined by the difference between the collected own tax liability and the excess VAT deductions returned.
The VAT revenues at the customs offices were due to the amount of tax collected by them.
The tax collected by the customs authorities, in accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, was reflected in the tax deductions applied to financial or tax authorities.
For most financial or tax authorities, excess VAT deductions exceeded the tax liability.
VAT is one of the core taxes in terms of state budget revenues, as it accounted for around 31% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic in 2003 and approximately 42% in the tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic amounted to CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The financial and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions refunded totalled CZK 231.4 billion.
Total VAT collection in the SR amounted to 83.8 billion Sk in 2003.
Tax and customs authorities collected CZK 187.0 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions refunded amounted to a total of EUR 103.2 billion.
Excise taxes
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as the SpD) was made by the relevant financial or tax authorities and on imports of products subject to SpD by the customs authorities.
SpD's share of state budget tax revenues in the Czech Republic was approximately 16% in 2003 and around 19% in the Slovak Republic.
The total collection of SpD collected in the Czech Republic by the financial and customs authorities in 2003 was CZK 85.6 billion and in the SR amounted to CZK 38.0 billion.
4. The course of the inspection
Cooperation between the SAO and the SAO of the SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage a comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia was carried out, in the second stage the results of this comparison were used in mutual verification of the implementation of selected commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and in checks carried out on the territory of both states.
4.1.
Preparing a control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel VAT and SpD inspections was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic in April 2003.
In November 2003, a coordination meeting was held at which, inter alia, the selection of commodities - goods which represented a significant risk in complying with customs and tax legislation: - alcohol and spirits, tariff subheadings 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff subheadings Nos.2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, items and subheadings of customs tariff Nos 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff subheadings Nos 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
The two parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection would be made: (a) from the unassigned items found by the comparison of exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, (b) from entities carrying out imports and exports regularly or in one lump sum, (c) on the basis of the findings from the checks carried out by selected tax and tax authorities.
4.2. 4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
In the first stage, a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002 tested a mechanism for the mutual allocation of JCD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Subsequently, some exports from the Czech Republic were compared with imports into the Slovak Republic for 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
