In addition to the requirements of the European Directive, contracting authorities should replace the tenderers they invite to submit a tender.
It is also not permissible to limit competition from a regional point of view.
Contracting entities must document and justify the selection of candidates and the selection process.
Different provisions
In Germany, at least three candidates are required to be invited in the case of a restricted procedure and, in the case of a negotiated procedure, several suitable candidates.
Apart from two cases, the new Czech regulations do not allow the number of candidates contacted to be limited in the case of a narrower and negotiated procedure.
In Germany, the "four-ey principle" must be respected when selecting candidates.
While one worker proposes a list of them, another must substantially modify this proposal, e.g. by removing the proposed candidate or installing another.
This is intended to prevent a situation where an individual can definitively establish a range of candidates who take part in the procedure.
If such a provision is not in place, a far-reaching illegal agreement between the participants is allowed.
The list of tenderers who will be invited to submit a tender shall be confidential and shall not be divulged.
This is also indebted to authorized independent experts.
There is no similar measure in the Czech Republic, nor is there any measure for confidential treatment of the list of candidates.
Under German provisions, they may not designate candidates for external society, but may make proposals to the contracting authority.
There is no similar requirement in the Czech Republic.
Main control findings
BRH
Number of candidates
In addition to a few cases, the requirement to address the minimum number of candidates has been met.
An analysis of almost 7,000 terms of reference for works with a value up to the national limit showed that, in the case of limited procedures, contracting authorities called for an average of 6.6 potential bidders and, in the case of a direct negotiation procedure, an average of 4.4 bidders.
Changing suppliers and regional restrictions
The contracting authorities, especially in the area of building construction, did not change the circle of contacted bidders because they had had good experience with those with whom they had worked so far.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The contracting authorities argued that, in the case of a non-public procedure, they should guarantee that they would reach out to tenderers whose suitability they had already secured in advance.
Although there was no evidence for illegal regional restrictions, the range of candidates in the non-public procedure included a larger proportion of regional tenderers than in the case of public procedures.
Contracting entities explained this to the low amount of the contract compared to the public procedure and the high cost of travel for potential bidders.
Cross-check principle and proposals from self-employed professionals
For the most part, contracting authorities ignored the obligation to change the list of candidates proposed by self-employed professionals.
They argued, in particular, a lack of staff, time pressure or inadequate knowledge of a suitable candidate.
In many cases, it was not apparent from the records who had proposed the tenderer who had been asked to participate in the proceedings.
The check of some samples showed that the list of potential candidates was created by self-employed professionals and was accepted unchanged by the contracting authority.
Contracting entities did not adequately protect themselves from potential manipulation.
Confidentiality of handling lists of potential candidates
One contracting authority kept a list of candidates for invitations to the procurement procedure in a database to which all employees had access at any time.
This allowed the manipulation or unauthorised disclosure of the names of the presumed or accepted bidders, who could then agree on the price.
Documentation
The dossier referred to the reasons for the selection of candidates in only a few cases.
SAO
Criteria for selection of candidates
When constructing the ring road, those interested did not have information about what the data on their qualifications would be evaluated and how.
For actions related to the development and modernisation of waterways and ports in the announcement of the procurement procedure for participation in the restricted procedure, the criteria for limiting the number of tenderers have not been established.
All eight bidders met the qualifications, but this exceeded the number to which the contracting authority restricted participation in the procurement procedure.
The Commission then selected the candidates using the random selection method - drawing lots, which was legal at the time.
This procedure should have been mentioned as a criterion already in the contract notice.
Summary
In view of the high risk of manipulation in the selection of the winning bidder in restricted procurement procedures, both countries have introduced special measures to prevent illegal restrictions on competition.
The German rules limit such opportunities for manipulation by so-called cross-checking (the four-eye principle), by maintaining the confidentiality of the list of candidates and by prohibiting proposals to select candidates to external companies.
Czech rules aim to prevent potential restrictions with the aim of manipulation mainly by an unlimited number of applicants.
However, the inspection found that part of those rules had not been applied to a sufficient degree and that an inadmissible restriction of the circle of candidates had not been prevented in some cases.
Contracting entities are obliged to completely eliminate the aforementioned shortcomings.
Submission of bids
The procurement phase, in which potential bidders can draw up tenders on the basis of the tender documentation they have received, begins with the publication of information on the procurement procedure and/or a call to tenderers.
By the time the envelopes are opened, prospective tenderers can submit their bids to the contracting authority and thus apply for the award of the contract.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU law does not prescribe specific requirements at this stage of the procurement procedure.
The contracting authority must comply with the national rules governing this stage of management and prevent potential manipulation.
Those provisions shall relate in particular to organisation and control.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The principle is that the tender documents on the basis of which potential suppliers make their bids must always be sent by the contracting authority.
Projection offices involved in management should not fulfil this role.
The contracting authority must ensure that all candidates have received the same information during this procurement procedure stage.
In case of confusion in the tender documents or if further questions arise, information may be supplied to tenderers only by the contracting authority.
Projection offices responsible for drawing up the tender documents may not provide any information.
Throughout this phase, any contact between the design office and the bidders must be prevented.
They must remain anonymous throughout, as allowing contact with them can adversely affect competition.
Tenders sent by post or submitted directly must be submitted in a closed envelope.
Electronically submitted offers must be encoded.
Different provisions
In Germany, the contracting authority may entrust insured suppliers of external services with the printing and distribution of documentation, and their staff must be obliged to comply with confidentiality.
In Germany, tenders received must be marked, indicating the date of receipt and transmitted directly and immediately in their original state to the official responsible for safekeeping.
This worker must not be involved in the procurement procedure.
The offers received must be locked up until the closing date of the envelopes.
In the Czech Republic, the offers received are marked with a serial number.
The sponsor shall issue a report with the details of the competition, including the offer number and information on the preparation and receipt of the offer.
There are no specific provisions on the safekeeping of offers.
Main control findings
BRH
BRH checked the terms of the administration building.
Sending tender documents
The audited contracting authorities of the building administration sent out the tender documents either directly or entrusted its printing and distribution to an external firm.
Self-employed workers did not send any documentation.
Information provided to tenderers
For the part of the tender documents relating to the questioning and obtaining information, the contracting authority did not follow the decree for separate planning from the procurement procedure.
Contrary to the relevant regulations, he often did not mention in the documentation the names of his contact staff, but rather the staff of the project management department.
Some notices in the procurement procedure even included the names of firms or self-employed persons involved in the preparation of the tender documents.
In rare cases, tenderers who raised questions during the procurement procedure did not receive identical information.
Labelling of tenders
For the contracting authorities, all accepted tenders were stamped with a stamp and acknowledgement of receipt.
However, in some cases for the negotiated procedure, offers were accepted by self-employed professionals, violating the rule of one construction of corruption prevention.
Custody of the tenders
Once marked, not all tenders were passed on directly and without delay to the official assigned to them keep in custody locked the tenders in a steel cabinet.
For one contracting entity, the bids were temporarily placed in an open compartment of the mailroom to which all employees had access.
Another sponsor placed the box in the corridor without permanent supervision, and part of the bids thrown into the mailbox stayed there overnight.
The box opening was wide and unsecured, and was thus accessible not only to employees.
SAO
The SAO did not find shortcomings in this area.
Summary
Rules are laid down in both countries to prevent contacts, in particular between interested companies and design offices working together in procurement procedures, for the duration of the process.
Equal treatment is ensured by sending the same information to all tenderers.
For the receipt, custody and confidentiality of tenders, there are appropriate rules to prevent manipulation and corruption.
In Germany, the relevant requirements are somewhat more developed than in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the accumulated control register showed breaches of the rules in some areas.
These discrepancies can be easily corrected.
Opening envelopes
Opening envelopes
During the opening of the envelopes, the offers that have been closed so far are opened, their contents are read and published.
The period for which the tenderer is bound by his tender begins at the time of expiry of the deadline for submitting envelopes or opening them and ends with a deadline specified by the contracting authority.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
European legislation does not contain any specific provisions dealing with the opening of envelopes.
However, national rights and regulations contain extensive requirements for both the protection of tenders and competition during this sensitive phase of the entire procurement procedure.
The principles of "multiple eyes", the transparency and credibility of the envelope opening process are intended to prevent manipulations and modifications of tenders already submitted.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The opening of envelopes must be carried out by several persons appointed by the contracting authority.
The coincidence with the "more eyes" principle is intended to prevent individuals from having hidden manipulation of offers.
Candidates may be present when opening envelopes.
When opening, all envelopes must be placed before the chairman of the commission and are opened one by one.
The tenders received late shall not be taken into account.
In order to ensure transparency when opening envelopes, this phase, including the conclusions (results), must be recorded in writing. The entry must include, among other things, the names of the tenderers and the prices offered.
The minutes must be read and signed by the group manager.
The minutes may also be signed by the candidates present.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, a commission is being set up to open envelopes.
The participation of independent experts is admitted.
Members of the Commission may also be entrusted with discussion in the subsequent stages of the procedure, i.e. the evaluation of tenders.
In Germany, the opening of envelopes takes place in the presence of a manager and registrar.
The manager must be an employee of the contracting authority.
The manager and, in the case of building construction, the registrar may not be participants in the preparatory phase (making the tender documents), may not decide on the award of the contract and shall not be members in the subsequent processing (management) of the contract.
German regulations require that the entry from the opening of envelopes contains not only bidding prices, but also all information about discounts and special (unusual) symptoms, e.g. damaged envelopes upon receipt or late received offer.
In the Czech Republic, in addition to the bidding prices, there must be an indication of the language of the tender and the signature mandate of the tenderer in addition to the bidding prices.
German regulations require all parts of the envelopes opened to be marked to avoid subsequent changes.
Offers, usually marked in the form of perforation indicating the date, must be kept confidential (secret) at the end of the opening of the envelopes and may be made available only to persons who further process them.
There are no such measures in the Czech Republic.
If a single tender is received in the Czech Republic, the envelope may not be opened and the tenderer must be notified without delay.
They do not have this adjustment in Germany and if a single offer is accepted, it is open and evaluated.
Main control findings
BRH
Principle of cross-checking
During the opening of the envelopes, the contracting authorities adhered to the four-eyed principle.
There were always a leader and registrar who was not given a different role.
However, in rare cases, for small court proceedings, natural persons have opened up tenders that have been sent to them, without the involvement of the contracting authority.
The opening process of envelopes
writings from the opening of envelopes have not always documented the course.
In some cases, tenders submitted were not marked late and in some cases there were no signatures.
Labelling of received bids
The contracting authorities marked perforation offers with a date, which was in line with the requirements.
Some of them have mislabeled offers in the past, but have changed practice after warnings from BRH.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
SAO
Deadline for receipt of tenders
In road repairs, a bidder's bid was handed over a month late for one event, and he accepted it anyway.
Summary
Substantial parts of the provision when opening envelopes are identical in both countries to the principle of "multiple eyes" and the principle of transparency, thus making it possible to substantially reduce the risk of corruption and manipulation.
The German rules are more complex compared to the Czech Republic, especially the requirements for precise documentation of the procedure.
The marking, safe retention and respect for the confidentiality of tenders substantially limit the possibility of subsequent changes to the tenders submitted.
In addition, workers responsible for opening envelopes may not carry out any other activities related to the contract to be awarded.
The findings, despite the discovery of some irregularities, confirm that the rules for opening envelopes are largely applied.
Assessment and evaluation of tenders
The contracting authority must review and evaluate the tenders received within the time limit set.
At the same time, they must award the contract to the tenderer who best meets the award criteria in the tender.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU law sets out the process of assessing and evaluating bids in several steps:
The first step examines the suitability of applicants.
They must have a good economic and financial position and the required professional and technical knowledge and skills.
Candidates who have ever been convicted of bribery or embezzlement must always be excluded from procurement procedures.
Offers of excluded tenderers must be evaluated in terms of numerical accuracy, technical suitability and value for money on the basis of previously published award criteria.
The contracting authority must identify the most economically favourable offer and, in particular, examine all significantly low price offers.
Review and evaluation is particularly sensitive and prone to manipulation.
Candidates may, for example, be excluded without a legitimate reason, or tenders that do not meet the requirements may be kept in competition.
The outcome of the evaluation may be wrongly influenced by the preference of a tenderer or its disadvantage, which may prevent the selection of the most economically advantageous tender.
The contracting authority must therefore take specific measures to select the persons integrated into the process and must ensure that they meet the requirements of integrity and technical knowledge.
They must also make sure that the whole process and the decisions taken are transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Consistent with EU requirements, the relevant provisions in both countries require the review and evaluation of tenders in step-by-step.
During the evaluation, the requirements for demonstrating the suitability of tenderers, the evaluation criteria and their weights set out in the notice or the procurement documents shall not be amended.
The criteria set for assessing the suitability of candidates cannot be further applied.
Further evaluation can only be carried out on the basis of evaluation criteria.
The tenders submitted must first be examined from a formal point of view whether they are complete or do not include suspicious elements that might encourage manipulation.
Where tenderers are excluded from further examination and evaluation of the tenders submitted by them, they shall be informed immediately.
Where the evaluation of the tenders results in a finding of a disproportionately low bid price, the tenderer concerned must be given the opportunity to comment on the situation before the possible withdrawal of his tender.
The reasons for the decision must be documented transparently.
Different provisions
In Germany, tenderers must remain silent and only authorised persons may participate in the evaluation of tenders.
The mathematical accuracy of tenders can only be reviewed by the contracting authority.
Assessments may only be entrusted to staff who are not integrated into the decision-making phase of the choice of supplier or in the project implementation phase.
There are no precise provisions on who can carry out further reviews and evaluations.
If external companies are entrusted with reviewing and evaluating tenders, they must be aware that the offers are confidential and respect that fact honestly.
They can only make proposals to the contracting authority for decisions.
In the Czech Republic, bids must be reviewed and evaluated by a commission appointed by the contracting authority, which will draw up a report with a draft conclusion of the contract.
However, in both countries, the final decision depends on the contracting authority.
If the documents and declarations required in connection with the submission of tenders are incomplete in Germany, the tenderers concerned must subsequently submit the required documents within six days.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If tenderers fail to comply with this obligation, their tenders must be excluded.
In the Czech Republic, the contracting authority may decide whether to give the tenderer the opportunity to complete the missing documents.
If the candidate does not substantiate them, they must be excluded.
In Germany, not only the total price but also the unit prices must be reviewed.
If the bid price structure shows that prices for parts of the total project have been estimated disproportionately high or low, bidders must be asked to explain.
If they do not provide an explanation and if the contracting authority can prove that the tender contains compensatory prizes, such tenders must be excluded.
This is to prevent bidders from submitting price calculations based on the assumption that substantial quantitative changes will be made to individual parts of the overall project, which may lead to a significant increase in project costs.
In the Czech Republic, the total price of the work is evaluated and the prices of individual parts are not examined in detail.
Compensation of valuation is not a reason to exclude the offer.
In Germany, a contract cannot be awarded to a tenderer who offers a disproportionately high or low price.
If one or more offers vary in price by 10% or more than the price estimated by the contracting authority or other tenders, tenderers must demonstrate that their tender has been credibly and convincingly calculated.
If they are unable to do so, the contracting authority should exclude them.
In the Czech Republic, the procurement procedure may be cancelled after a price review if only tenders with disproportionately low prices have been received and the bidders have not justified these prices.
If the price of a tender is significantly higher than the contracting authority's estimate, that is not a reason for refusing to award a contract to the tenderer concerned (unlike German contract law).
Where there is a suspicion in Germany of conduct intended to limit competition, the contracting authority is obliged to report this fact without delay to the competent superior authority.
This must decide on the way forward and whether it is appropriate to inform the antitrust authority or law enforcement authorities.
It must also approve (e.g. if the contract exceeds €50,000 and the contract has not been awarded to the tenderer with the lowest bid), whether the contract will be awarded when the contract is negotiated or whether the procurement procedure will be cancelled.
Czech rules do not regulate this area.
Main control findings
BRH
Examination of suitability and procurement criteria
Most of the procurement procedures examined were in line with the relevant requirements.
In the case of some recommendations by potential suppliers made by self-employed workers, the contracting authorities themselves did not check the suitability of the tenderers themselves.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In some cases of procurement procedures, insufficient documentation was submitted as to whether the contracting authority took into account all published evaluation criteria or whether the selection decision was based solely on the price criterion.
Selection of interested persons and confidentiality of offers
Some contracting authorities used the services of unauthorized persons, such as self-employed workers or employees of construction offices.
They were incorporated into the planning or implementation process of construction projects, performing functions that were to be held exclusively by the contracting authority.
Contracting entities have sought to substantiate this with their lack of human resources in the sector.
In some cases, self-employed professionals used to review the offers of services of persons who were not formally bound to maintain the confidentiality of tenders and to perform with due care the fulfilment of their obligations under the contract.
As far as contracting authorities are concerned, there was generally no evidence of whether offers in the custody of self-employed professionals were available only to designated persons.
Review and mathematical control of bids
Some contracting authorities have handed over open envelopes for further examination to self-employed professionals without first carrying out the prescribed verification of tenders and mathematical examination and without documenting the results of these examinations.
In the event of any intent to manipulate, third parties could make changes to the bids that could not be identified by the contracting authority.
The examination of documents revealed a number of cases where unusual elements in the bids were not adequately labelled or where data on prices and products were missing.
Performance audits
A model check by one contracting authority revealed that in 75% of procurement cases, the most advantageous tenders deviated by more than 10% from pre-arranged costs.
One of the 20 procurement procedures was cancelled due to inadequate bidding prices.
In many cases, there was a lack of evidence or sufficient documentation on the examination of bids or negotiations with tenderers for further clarification.
In many cases, detailed information was also lacking, for example, about unit prices of the most important invoiced items.
The reason for the derogations were often cited changes in market prices or increases in material costs.
Contracting authorities have argued that identifying and proving compensatory prices is difficult.
In the case of one call for tenders made by an entity outside the ordinary contracting entity, a 66 % lower price was offered compared to the initial cost estimate.
No data on a closer examination of the cost or on the determination of the reasons for the deviations were not recorded.
In clarifying this issue, the contracting authority found no indication of price dumping for the tenderer to whom the contract was eventually awarded.
It was therefore not clarified whether the initial cost estimate was excessive or whether the price offered was too low.
Later, the contracting authority of that tenderer was assessed as a "low-cost company" which was unable to meet either qualitative requirements or deadlines.
In another procurement procedure, the contracting authority awarded the contract to a tenderer whose price was 35 % higher than the initial cost estimate.
The contracting authority did not cancel the tendering procedure and put forward an unfounded argument that the tenderer could be presumed not to have incurred a disproportionately high cost setting of its prices.
Suspicion of irregularities
Two incidents of irregularities were found with one contracting authority, and they were reported to a company responsible for technical supervision.
In one procurement procedure, two bidders submitted bids containing an identical price calculation, prompting the contracting authorities to exclude both bids.
The inspections did not show any material shortcomings in the application of other provisions.
SAO
Verification of suitability
For many construction actions, such as university buildings, roads and railways, contracting entities have not excluded tenderers from participating in the procurement procedure, even though they did not meet the requirements of the contracting authority referred to in the terms of reference, or did not substantiate the qualifications to the extent required, or, on the contrary, one contracting authority could not substantiate or explain the reason for the exclusion of the candidate who met the requirements.
Evaluation
For the construction of the wastewater treatment plant, the individual evaluation criteria of the tender procedure for the contractor of the construction were determined, but the contracting authority did not respect them during the procedure.
For actions in the field of railway infrastructure development, the weighting of the evaluation criteria for the award of the contract was not determined at the initiation of the procedure, but only at the beginning of the evaluation.
For the road repair project, the assessment of the criterion of "shortening construction time" was not carried out correctly.
For bidders in second and third place, the evaluation incorrectly stated a greater reduction in the construction time than indicated in their tenders.
Documentation of the reasons for the selection of the candidate
For the three housing promotion actions, the contracting authority did not substantiate on the basis of which criteria it assessed the offers received and how it selected the most suitable of them.
Correctness of the selection of suppliers of small-scale contracts associated with the construction of a ring road with an estimated price of up to 500 thousand.
The CZK could not be verified because the suppliers were selected only on the basis of telephone consultations on the price and date of fulfilment, but the documents on these negotiations were not prepared.
Summary
In both countries, the rules for the verification and evaluation of bids correspond to EU requirements.
However, it differs in the light of the specific management steps and the selection of individuals involved in the management.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, these steps in the procurement process are governed by stricter and more detailed requirements, especially as regards the application of the cross-price principle and the protection of tenders.
The same applies to the rules for verifying the appropriateness of the prices offered.
In both countries, in some cases of checks, it was found that substantial steps of the process in the verification and evaluation of the bids were not documented at all and, if so, only partially.
The absence of control tools and transparency in decision-making during the review and evaluation of tenders allows for manipulation.
The checks showed serious defects, such as the transmission of bids to third parties without prior appropriate examination and documenting the tenders by the contracting authority.
Where contracting entities entrust a third party with the performance of the functions associated with the examination and evaluation of tenders, appropriate measures and increased control of measures against increased handling options are necessary.
When checking price legitimacy, the audited German contracting authorities did not use the complete set of available instruments in all cases and did not deal with their own pricing structure.
In the Czech Republic, deficiencies were identified in the evaluation of the suitability of tenders and the application of evaluation criteria.
Completion of procurement procedure
After examining and evaluating the tenders, the procurement process is completed by awarding the contract or cancelling the procedure.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
In the case of a European procedure, all tenderers must be informed in advance of the award decision.
Suppliers shall have the opportunity to review the decision taken within a limited period of 10 or 15 days and to request its examination where appropriate.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The period of 10 days shall apply to electronic submissions and 15 days to other submissions.
The contract shall not be concluded before the expiry of that period or before the review procedure has expired.
If the review body rejects the complaint and confirms the decision, candidates and tenderers must be given the opportunity to have the right to be reviewed by an independent court.
This measure ensures that no contracting authority will be able to circumvent the legal protection of suppliers by rapidly implementing the decision of the procurement procedure.
The contracting authority must properly document the conduct of the proceedings.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries implemented management information obligations.
In both countries, the final decision on the outcome of the procurement procedure lies with the contracting authority.
However, he cannot arbitrarily deviate from the results of a properly carried out examination and evaluation.
The contracting authority is to conclude the contract within a specified period of time.
This is due to the fact that the tenderer is not bound by its tender after that period has expired.
The content of the contract must not deviate from the winning bid.
Failed bidders are to be informed of the outcome in a timely manner, stating the reason why their bid was not accepted.
The cancellation of the procurement procedure is only permissible if certain conditions are met, e.g. if the prices in tenders do not correspond to the specifications.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the mandatory waiting period prior to the conclusion of the contract covers both European and national procedures.
In Germany, the equivalent provision applies only to European procedures.
In all other procedures in Germany, tenderers cannot be informed of the award of the contract before deciding on its EU provisions and review award.
In the Czech Republic, the tendering procedure must be cancelled if a single tender has been received or only a single tender met the requirements for its consideration and evaluation.
In Germany, the contract must be awarded even if a single tender has been received, provided that the tender fulfils the conditions set out in the tender documents and is cost-effective.
Main control findings
BRH
The checks found few discrepancies in the completion of the audited procurement processes.
In some cases, European procedures have received authorising letters before the expiry of the notification period, which may invalidate the contract.
Also, in several cases of open procedures, the authorising letters of modification were incompatible with the content of the tender, such as new deadlines.
In some cases, the contracting authorities did not meet the time limits for awarding the contract.
In one open procedure, the contracting authority selected the second most advantageous tender because the bidder offering a price more than 50% lower no longer wished to fulfil the contract at the price originally offered.
SAO
During the reconstruction and construction of the university, in one case the contracting authority did not conclude a contract with the contractor in accordance with the draft contract contained in the tenderer's tender.
For some road repair and maintenance actions, highway construction and ring roads, contracts were concluded later than stipulated by law.
For building modifications in former military installations, the contracting authority sent a notice of the selection of the most suitable tender to all bidders only after the legal deadline had expired.
Summary
Both countries implemented EU rules on the termination of the procurement procedure.
The legal protection of unsuccessful candidates contributes to reducing corruption.
The Czech Public Procurement Act includes an institute of legal protection even in cases of contracts below EU limits.
In both countries, it was found that the limited time limit for concluding the contract was exceeded.
This can cause adverse economic consequences and increase the risk of manipulation.
In the future, contracting entities should eliminate such shortcomings in the conclusion of the procurement procedure.
Documentation, notifications, information obligations
The procurement process, with all its various stages, relevant findings and decisions, including the relevant justifications, shall be documented in a transparent manner.
Completion of the procurement procedure at European level must be published.
Data on procurement procedures are summarised in EU statistics.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
The obligation to document procurement procedures is in line with the essential requirement of the principle of transparency, applied at EU-wide level.
Only a proper and time-consuming decision-making and justification documentation gives a guarantee of transparency in the procurement process and, above all, guarantees effective legal protection of the interests of each tenderer in cases where the value of the contract exceeds the European limits.
The relevant documentation is also an essential part of the anti-corruption measures, as the obligation to substantiate individual decisions in detail and their merits significantly reduce the scope for manipulation.
In cases of European procurement procedures, the contracting authority must notify the completion of the EU Publications Office (EU's Office of Official Publications) within 48 days from the date of award of the contract.
The Authority publishes a notification in the EU's Official Journal and this also fulfils the transparency requirement.
The contracting authority must summarise the essential information on its procurement procedures and communicate them to the European Commission through the relevant national ministries.
On this basis, the European Commission issues annual statistics that make it possible to get an overview of the development of the single market in the field of construction.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have fully transposed into their national legislation the provisions of the European law on documentation and notification obligations.
The provisions on documentation and notification for the purposes of European statistics are almost identical in both countries.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the obligation to announce the award of a contract applies not only to European procedures, but also to national procurement procedures.
The notification period is only 15 days from the conclusion of the contract.
In Germany, the obligation to notify procurement procedures, in addition to those that are mandatory under European law, applies only to limited procedures exceeding the limit of €25 thousand ($625,000) and direct procedures exceeding the limit of €15,000 ($375,000) including VAT.
Only the parties to the proceedings are informed below this limit.
Main control findings
BRH
Documentation
A large number of assignments have not been fully documented.
The notification did not contain all the necessary information, e.g. the reasons for the delivery specifications and the national rules.
In the case of one procedure, the contracting authority did not explain why it had concluded a contract with a tenderer whose tender did not contain mandatory requirements.
In several cases, some required records were also missing.
Publication of award
In the case of some European procedures, the contracting authority erred in the publication of the notice.
In the case of several terms of reference, there was no evidence of disclosure of the notice.
Reporting obligation
The statistically proven files included the required minimum of information and were created and sent in time.
Preliminary transparency
In most cases, the contracting authority published information about the outcome of the contract.
In the case of one contracting authority, contract information was not disclosed due to a communication error.
It took the contracting authority six months to notice the error.
Consequently, the outcome of the proceedings was not disclosed during that period.
SAO
Documentation
For events related to the organisation of a major sporting event, significant deficiencies were identified in the documentation of the course of the procurement procedure, such as incorrect information on bidding prices in the evaluation committee's discussions.
In addition, some documents on opening envelopes have not been signed.
Publication of award
In the preparation of repairs and maintenance of roads, the construction of the motorway and the ring road, the announcement of the award of the public contract was sent after the deadline or it was not made public.
Summary
The provisions on documentation and notification and notification obligations include European requirements and are almost identical in both countries.
This generally ensures the transparency of procurement procedures and final selection.
Czech reporting obligations are somewhat stricter compared to German ones.
The inspections have identified shortcomings substantially reducing the value of documentation as a means of preventing corruption.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Contracting entities should continue to strengthen the transparency of their procurement procedures and fully meet the notification and notification requirements.
Aggregate evaluation and recommendations
Parallel controls of the SAO and BRH were focused on two areas that are essential for the public procurement process both in the Czech Republic and Germany, namely the application of EU procurement law and the prevention of corruption.
EU legislation gives opportunities to international competition within the EU to create a single European market.
Measures aimed at preventing corruption are not only to avoid or at least reduce it, but also to prevent financial damage and potential loss of confidence in the integrity of the government.
The audited supervisory findings of the two audit institutions - the SAO and BRH - with regard to the application of the procurement law of both countries and the comparison of its relevant provisions, give an internal view of the common and distinct elements which may assist both countries in the further development and application of this right.
Application of EU procurement law
Both countries have transposed EU public procurement law into their national legislation.
In both countries, there is thus an important common base for public procurement and the fulfilment of essential requirements in the field of: competition; equal treatment of candidates; transparency of procurement procedures.
Contracting entities reinforce these requirements in part with very large measures.
The Czech Republic has extended the provisions on public procurement requiring European procedures to procedures below EU limits and are therefore governed by national legislation.
However, the checks have shown that contracting entities are not always fully in line with all relevant provisions of EU requirements.
German contracting entities should continue to improve the quality of their procurement procedures in order to eliminate the aforementioned irregularities taking into account the implementation of EU requirements.
In the Czech Republic, the controls identified risks affecting economy and achieving value for money.
These include, in particular, the incomplete definition of the subject-matter of the public contract, which resulted in additional works which were often awarded in breach of the law, the lack of definition of the anticipated price and the required qualification prerequisites narrowing the possible circle of tenderers and thus reducing competition especially in the field of transport constructions.
Prevention of corruption
Joint controls were not intended to detect corruption cases.
The reason was that both BRH and the SAO did not have sufficient tools to do so.
However, they can examine whether the competent authorities of both countries are taking measures to reduce corruption and manipulation in public procurement and how these measures are applied.
When it comes to preventing corruption, both countries have focused on different aspects.
Above all, German provisions give room for broad and unlimited competition, transparency and controls as a central element in the prevention of corruption.
Czech regulations mainly monitor the strengthening of the transparency of procurement procedures.
BRH
In Germany, there are general principles for the prevention of corruption that apply to the entire federal administration.
These principles were also included among the procurement requirements and were adopted to meet the specific needs of such procurement.
The relevant provisions specify, at times with great precision, ways of complying with the requirements for preventing corruption during the procurement procedure and the selection of persons incorporated therein.
In BRH's view, the principle of preference for open procurement and calls for participation is a particularly appropriate tool for substantially reducing the risk of corruption in public procurement, while restricting competition increases the risk of manipulation.
Risk analysis and adequate controls (particularly the principle of cross-checking), transparency requirements, procurement documents and various organisational measures are also an effective mechanism to prevent corruption and manipulation.
BRH therefore does not feel the need for substantial changes to the current provisions that public institutions have to comply with in public procurement.
Anti-corruption measures are widely applied in practice.
Irregularities found in some areas have highlighted weaknesses in compliance with certain requirements.
Therefore, contracting authorities should provide further training to their staff, familiarising them with anti-corruption requirements and further raising their awareness in this area.
A significant proportion of the weaknesses revealed apply to activities delegated by the building administration to private entrepreneurs.
However, the absence of adequate controls in delegating powers increases the risk of abuse.
Activities susceptible to manipulation and corruption should therefore only be passed on to third parties if the administration can guarantee a sufficient degree of protection against unauthorised interference.
SAO
Anti-corruption strategies have been adopted at the government level in the Czech Republic, which also significantly affect the area of public procurement.
The SAO's auditing actions took place during the period when one of the most important parts of this strategy was implemented, namely a significant change to the Public Procurement Act and the adoption of follow-up implementing regulations.
The strategy adopted and the new legal regulations can be effective steps to improve the situation.
For example, under the new regulations, the contracting authority must justify the effectiveness of the public contract, the determination of the anticipated value of the contract, the adequacy of the requirements for the qualification conditions, the establishment of the basic evaluation criteria and the method of evaluation of the tenders, and properly document and publish everything properly.
Recommendations
Overall, both the SAO and BRH have a favourable opinion about the ways of implementing EU requirements.
In practice, their broad application has confirmed that EU competition, equal treatment and transparency requirements provide an appropriate basis for public procurement within the EU.
The transnational model, introduced in the EU, can also serve as a basis for similar projects aimed at facilitating and promoting international competition.
Taking into account the great potential of material and intangible damage caused as a result of manipulation and corruption in connection with public procurement, both the BRH and the SAO insist that it is the responsibility of contracting authorities to continue measures against corruption and manipulation and to improve them where possible.
In particular, organisational structures and procurement procedures should be continuously monitored in terms of weaknesses and risks in order to identify and respond appropriately to the need for corrective action.
Compared to practice in Germany, it has emerged that the share of open procurement procedures in the Czech Republic should increase, giving room to competition and substantially reducing the possibility of corrupt behaviour.
The award of contracts in parts may also have a positive impact on the price achieved in cases where it is permissible and appropriate for the contracting authority. A higher number of applicants put pressure on the price achieved.
The provision of its organisation also has an impact on the conduct of the procurement procedure.
It is provided by special state organisations in Germany, while in the Czech Republic, with the exception of transport structures, it is organised by the central authorities themselves or through contractual organisations.
Both the SAO and BRH want to further develop knowledge in their work where appropriate and address them with their parliament and government beyond their joint project.
Moreover, they are convinced that the principles of procurement law and their implementation, as described in this report, will also be of interest at the level of the International Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (INTOSAI), as these principles and findings are of general importance for effectively tackling corruption and to guarantee that public procurement is awarded in a regime of well-functioning and honest competition and that value for money is achieved.

JOINT FINAL REPORT on the results of parallel controls on excise duty management in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Joint final report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The joint report submitted informs about the course and outcome of international cooperation during parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, with a focus on the management of excise duties in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the highest audit institutions of both countries was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic in the exercise of parallel controls aimed at the administration of excise duties concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel controls was chosen on the basis of the fact that the two EU Member States are based on common European legislation to see how it is applied at national level, how the excise tax management system is set up and how the systems in Slovakia and the Czech Republic are different.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out was the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the identification of good practice.
Last but not least, the finding that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise duty management was very limited without parallel controls being carried out.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrík,
President
President
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel controls of the SPD administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia and their administration is in line with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences were found between the adjustment of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic, in the Czech Republic it contributes to the effective administration of excise taxes verification of the economic stability of applicants for the issue of permits and the obligatory marking and colouring of selected mineral oils and some other oils; In the SR, the distribution of control signs is simpler than in the Czech Republic and less burdensome tax administrator.
In the fight against excise tax evasion, supervision of the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw material, the implementation of the institute of fuel distributor and the registration of consumer packaging of alcohol has proved to be a good practice in both countries.
Revenue from excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's targets of reducing labour taxation, introducing environmentally austerity measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, including because there is no indexation of excise tax rates in both countries.
This has the effect of reducing the materiality of excise duties on total tax revenues and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, a real reduction in the tax burden on excise duties.
The state has long supported the implementation of environmental measures financially, but these measures have a negative impact on excise revenues, which will need to be replaced in the future by other revenues or by reducing state spending.
Administrative expenditures spent on excise tax management in both the Czech Republic and Slovakia have been growing for a long time, mainly due to wage growth, and their efficiency is declining.
In the Slovak Republic, this efficiency is also negatively affected by the expenditure on computerising the administration of excise duties (IT expenses) and the expenses incurred on the wages of employees carrying out permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
The electronicisation of excise tax management in the SR did not significantly affect the reduction in the number of tax administrations.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR recommend to the FŘ SR to reconsider the merits of the exercise of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses on alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the efficiency of administrative expenditures was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures in the audited period that would lead to a reduction in the staffing demands of the administration of excise duties.
The number of comparable administrative tasks of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in individual years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax entities in the Slovak Republic is about a third lower than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in the Slovak Republic carry out administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical exercise of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasize remote supervision and risk analysis.
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is administratively more demanding than in the Czech Republic and, given the ratio of the number of tax acts to the number of entities, even more costly.
Electronization of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the SR the administration of tax returns to excise taxes is fully electronized, in the Czech Republic documents proving taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are electronically handed over.
Both methods of electronization support effective administration of excise duties, which is why the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the SR recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditure on the deployment of EMCS could not be compared, as the FŘ SR provided expenditure data only for the upgrade of the system in the period 2011-2015, but expenditure was also spent before this period.
Expenditure incurred in that period only for EMCS upgrades in the SR was about 20% higher than the expenditure incurred in the Czech Republic for both the introduction of EMCS and the upgrade of this system over more than a decade.
The administrators of excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia did not reach comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenditures.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the SR the administration of excise duties is significantly more resource-intensive.
The introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excise products (EMCS) made the administration of excise duties more efficient, but in the Slovak Republic to a lower extent, as significantly higher expenditure was incurred on the introduction of the system and its modernisation than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The cooperation between the two audit institutions was carried out on the basis of the Cooperation Treaty in the implementation of parallel controls aimed at the management of excise duties of 18 August 2015.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic have agreed to carry out parallel controls that will primarily focus on the issue of excise tax administration and the results of which will allow analysis, mutual comparison and evaluation of the established facts.
Common audit issues were agreed on which parallel controls were based.
Characteristics of the subject and the parallel control objective:
The parallel controls aimed to compare the performance of excise administrators, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify the weaknesses of the excise tax administration process.
In particular, the following main audit issues should have been answered:
Did excise administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenditures?
Was the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise duties (EMCS) to streamline the management of excise duties and was the cost of implementing it effectively incurred?
The parallel checks carried out were to identify the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, especially in the area of regulation and in the setting of the organizational structure.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The General Directorate of Customs (DG) and the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic (FD SR) have joined a joint declaration on mutual cooperation between the Visegrad Four countries, the objectives of this declaration include the areas of excise duties, including the fight against fraud, exploring the possibility of harmonising legislation and finding harmonised interpretations on the rules of selected problems, exploring the possibility of joint activities to increase efficiency in detecting fraud and sharing experiences and best practices.
1 The EMCS is operated pursuant to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 establishing an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty.
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO of the Czech Republic
Control number: 15/33
Subject of scrutiny: The administration of excise duties
Objective of control: The aim of the SAO control of the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of customs authorities in the administration of excise duties, especially when monitoring transport in the system of conditional exemptions from excise duties and when securing tax (customs debts); to examine whether the system of administration of excise duties is set up to ensure the efficiency of the collection of revenues of the state budget.
Controlled period: 2012-2015 and, in case of factual context, periods prior to and downstream
Controlled person: General Directorate of Customs
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO of the Slovak Republic
Control number: KA-023/2016/1050
Subject of scrutiny: The administration of excise duties
Objective of control: The aim of the inspection was an independent and objective examination of whether the FCH SR and the customs authorities (CÚ) in the administration of excise duties function economically, efficiently and effectively in accordance with generally binding legislation.
Controlled period: 2012-2015
Controlled person: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation for excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
The excise tax administration legislation is divided into the level of EU legislation (see Annex 1) and the level of national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118/EC, on the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC, defines excise duty and lays down basic rules for the management of taxes and the management of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This directive makes it possible to impose taxes on consumption on other products.
EU legislation regulates in particular the minimum conditions for: the level of tax rates for each type of product selected, the production, storage, processing and possession of products subject to tax, tax exemption and refund, supervision of the transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and the keeping of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation makes it possible to introduce control procedures and institutes at national level, provided they do not distort competition.
Legislative of excise duties in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, excise tax legislation is concentrated in the Excise Tax Act (Act No. 353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of the tax on mineral oils, taxes on alcohol, taxes on tobacco products, beer taxes, wine tax and intermediate products and taxes on raw tobacco.
This law defines forms of disposal of products subject to excise duties, tax payers, authorisation procedures, conditions for the transport of products, tax returns and penalties for infringements of legislation.
The law and subsequent decrees further regulate certain other conditions for the management of mineral oils (branding mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils and storage of raw tobacco for a purpose other than the production of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in parts 45 to 47 of Act No 261/2007 Coll., on the stabilisation of public budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are contained in special legislation. The Fuel Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation govern the conditions for the sale, dispensing, distribution of fuel and keeping of the registration of fuel put into free tax circulation.
Act No. 61/1997 Coll., on alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol.
Act No. 307/2013 Coll., on Compulsory Alcohol Labelling, and the relevant implementing regulations provide for mandatory marking of alcohol in consumer packaging, conditions for handling control tapes and conditions for the handling of alcohol (i.e. for production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, takeover, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
The procedures for tax proceedings, which are not specified in special regulations, are governed by Act No. 280/2009 Coll., the Tax Code.
Penalties are imposed by procedures under Act No 500/2004 Coll., the Administrative Code.
The conditions for the issuance of a trade licence (concession) to operate a trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuels" and "production, modification and sale of fermentation, alcohol of consumer and spirits" are regulated by Act No. 455/1991 Coll., on Trade Licensing Business (Trades Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has used the power to introduce control procedures and institutes for controlling the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and for monitoring compliance with the legislation when dealing with selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as when dealing with selected products for which the tax has already been paid.
These are monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and raw tobacco, marking some other mineral oils, labelling tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic has used the right to apply excise duty to other products and introduced an excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of legislative changes for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the Government of the Czech Republic's resolution of 3 October 2012 No 735, the implementation of the "zero tolerance plan for the black market for spirits," there were major legislative changes in the Czech Republic in 2012-2015 introducing a number of measures against excise duty fraud.
During the same period, there were also substantial changes in the legislation on mineral oil tax, tobacco products tax and the criminality of preparing the tax cut.
Criminal protection of tax revenues
With effect from 1 July 2016, the criminality of preparing the offence of "reduction of tax, fee and similar compulsory payment" is introduced. The adjustment made should allow police authorities to take more effectively and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, such as the deployment of operational search means.
General provisions for excise duty management
The issue of an authorisation to dispose of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act shall be subject, with effect from 1 January 2015, to: reliability; indebtedness; economic stability; the right to operate a trade enabling the pursuit of an activity related to authorisation; a situation where the claimant is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
In particular, the aim of the legislation was to address the issue of the emergence of tax arrears, namely by reducing operators with a licence to deal with products subject to excise duty taxation.
The economic stability condition newly allows the tax authority to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both within the authorisation procedure and after the authorisation has been issued.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities that do not have sufficient financial income to properly comply with their tax obligations in order to dispose of the products selected.
Indicators have been established to assess the economic stability of the proposer (capacity, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) on the basis of which a financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, it is also up to the administrative discretion of the tax administrator with regard to the individual conditions of the procedure.
The law stipulates the periodicity of examining the fulfilment of the condition of economic stability due to the timeliness of the data - the screening takes place once a year following the deadline for filing a return on income tax.
The tax administrator has the possibility to set other conditions needed for the administration of the tax.
If the authorisation holder does not comply with the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the authorisation or, if necessary, cancel the permit.
Of the 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable at a high risk of arrears if the tax liability exceeds the amount of tax security (e.g. repeated beneficiaries).
The permit was revoked by 10 entities, other applicants increased the tax collateral, capitalised their deposit into the company or substantiated up-to-date accounting data, according to which they had already fulfilled all the conditions for issuing the permit.
In addition to the applicant, the conditions of reliability and indebtedness must be met by a natural person who is a statutory body or a member of the statutory body, or a natural person who, while not being the appellant's statutory body or a member of it, carries out that activity (sponsorship of legal persons as a statutory body or its member, so-called established entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 established entities had been examined.
The records kept under the Excise Tax Act (Sections 37 to 40 and Section 60 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.) contain data on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods manufactured, taken over, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment regime (contingent exemption scheme, import, re-entry into the conditional exemption regime, export, free tax circulation, self-consumption, loss);
the identifier (SEED ID) of the recipient or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of the occurrence and registration;
transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carriers, transport number);
registration numbers of related documents;
notification of the placing of alcohol in a consumer package marked with a check band for free tax circulation and details of its distribution.
The post-transport takeover record must be made without delay after it has been completed.
In the case of records kept electronically, the record must be kept or allowed to output in xls, xlsx, ods.
Líh
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures designed to provide a detailed overview of the activities of the entities (see Annex 3, Scheme A) from the production of raw alcohol through the marking of control tape to its distribution to the final seller or the authorized user of the exempt spirit.
In the Czech Republic, the supervision of customs authorities is also subject to production facilities for the production of alcohol, which is not in operation.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of the processing of alcohol and the production of spirits and to identify persons handling alcohol in consumer packaging, to reduce the management of alcohol to financially stable and reliable persons, and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most significant measures are: The records of the production, reception, inventory and the issuance of alcohol contain information on the amount of alcohol according to the stages of alcohol production and processing, indicating the document numbers.
Limiting the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and limiting the number of packages with broken control tape at the point of sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other container of max. one litre or three litres if it is a container made of glass.
Spirits in larger packages are viewed as unmarked, which it is forbidden to dispose of.
At the point of the final sale to a natural person for his personal consumption, there may be a maximum of one consumer pack with broken control tape, or three if they are fitted with a single-way valve.
Mandatory registration of a person who lists ethyl alcohol in products in consumer packaging having at least 15 % volumetric alcohol for free tax circulation and is: importer of alcohol, alcohol producer in the Czech Republic or operator of a tax warehouse under a conditional exemption regime, provided that personal and technical conditions are met.
Personal terms - reliability, integrity and failure to declare a disqualification - must be met by the applicant and the person in the capacity of the statutory body or the responsible representative.
The applicant must provide a deposit of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approx. €3,700 to €185,000), depending on the anticipated amount of control strips taken.
The technical conditions for registration are a suitable place for alcohol marking and the equipment of the marking point or tax warehouse with a camera surveillance device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administrator.
The registration markings of the control tape are introduced for the marking of spirits with a volume of more than 0,06 litres.
When carrying control tapes, the registration marking of control bands shall be included in the transport documents or customs declaration at the time of export.
The control tape until 30.11.2013 contained a 10-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration number, the application code for the allocation of control tapes and a classification code according to the level of volume concentration of ethanol.
The control tape from 1.12.2013 newly contains two types of identifiers and the amount of alcohol in consumer packaging expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 °C, with rounding to the whole milliliters downwards.
The register of control bands to mark spirits contains daily entries on individual ways of handling control tapes according to the registration codes, as well as documents on the basis of which the registration took place.
In the event of the destruction, loss or theft of specific control tapes, their holder is obliged to notify the tax administrator by electronic means the registration code of the control tapes concerned and their number on the following working day following the operative event.
Introducing the new facts of the offences and adjusting the level of penalties imposed for infringements of the legislation when dealing with control tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to or exceeded by up to ten times the amount of excise duty (e.g. when control strips are destroyed or lost in a number exceeding 0,1 % of the total quantity of the individual orders of control tapes made, if the control tape is not returned within the statutory time limit).
Restrictions on the handling of control tapes only to registered holders who may not assign them to another person, with the exception of providing them to a foreign supplier for the purpose of indicating spirits in consumer packaging manufactured outside the Czech Republic.
The checked tapes exported must be placed on consumer packaging and imported back no later than nine months after receipt from the tax administrator.
Compulsory registration of a distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging, subject to the fulfilment of similar personal conditions as for the person obligated to mark alcohol and with the obligation to deposit a deposit of up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. around €185,000).
Defining persons for the sale or purchase of alcohol in consumer packaging.
Authorised persons are obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or final sellers, or they may sell them as final sellers.
They can pick up alcohol from other registered persons, insolvency administrator, administration, organisational units of the state or non-registered persons in the execution of tax execution.
Notices of the inclusion of alcohol or sale in consumer packaging for free tax circulation shall be required to send the alcohol to the tax administrator immediately the following day after the relevant fact to the tax administrator through an information system maintained by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or while respecting the content in the xml format.
The notification shall include the number of control bands used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the volume percentage of alcohol, the European goods code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or the final vendor, as well as the name of the product and the batch of production.
Tax entities sent about 10.5 million notifications in 2014 and 2015.
Compulsory concession (specific form of trade licence) not only for the production and modification of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging by the entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or to another legal or business license to a natural person for his own internal use.
Concession trades can only be performed once a decision is made by the Trade Licensing Authority upon the fulfilment of professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed professional qualification is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit for tax administrators is an overview of retailers and their establishments and restrictions
trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, for a field including the production, treatment of fermentation, alcohol of consumerism, spirits and other alcoholic beverages, and sales were registered in 2014 about 94 thousand and in 2015 about 104 thousand concessions.
Checks on compliance with legislation in the field of handling products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic also ensure in their activities outside the tax administrator: trade licensing offices, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection Authority, the authorities of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic, the authorities of the Czech Trade Inspection Authority.
If it finds that there has been a breach of the obligation or a breach of the prohibition, it shall inform the excise administrator without delay.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has introduced a comprehensive system of supervision (see Annex 3, Scheme B), to which mineral oils loaded with excise duties are subject, but also selected mineral oils of excise duty unburdened, which have been misused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from mineral oil production through storage, transport, marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils, marking of certain other mineral oils to delivery to the final consumer or user and, in some cases, mineral oil consumption.
Customs supervision also includes the manufacture of markings for the marking of mineral oils and the management of these substances.
The labelling and colouring of selected mineral oils are subject to mineral oils listed under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (petrol other), 2710 19 29 (other not elsewhere specified medium oils) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49 unless their tagging is prohibited.
The labelling of certain other mineral oils is subject to e.g. benzol, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion.
Mark and colour selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a marker is only possible on the basis of the tax administrator's permission.
