THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils, which is a group of mineral oils under the Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion), whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following characteristics: the flash point is less than 150 °C, the distillation test shall be at least 20 % of the volume, including losses up to a temperature of 350 °C.
These mineral oils were misused as an addition to finished fuel, in particular diesel, or were directly used or sold for engine propulsion because the physical characteristics are very similar.
Registration with the tax administrator shall be subject to entities dealing with monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres.
In order to issue a marketing authorisation, the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the representative responsible must be met, which applies throughout 2 With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by burning.
3 Council Regulation (EEC) No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 For example, when mineral oil is used as fuel (excluding water navigation if they are not private pleasure craft) or as components for the production of fuel, if the markings are of a defect in their use.
registration.
As of 30 November 2016, the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations, on the proposal of the marketing authorisation holder, four registrations were cancelled.
Electronic registration shall include detailed information on the receipt, self-consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil including document numbers, numbers of notification of acquisition to the tax administrator, place of storage and consumption, purpose of consumption, place of storage and consumption, or on sale, place of delivery and registration number of the customer.
Notification of any acquisition of special mineral oil must be made to the tax authorities at intervals of 24 to 72 hours before admission.
Identification of business partners, name and nomenclature of special mineral oil, quantity, purpose of consumption or sale or transfer information shall be reported.
The notification of the anticipated quantity in the relevant year of the acquired, sold or consumed mineral oil shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications of the purpose of use and marking, storage or consumption point, identification data of the person who is further sold or transferred by the special mineral oil shall be transmitted before each change.
Notifications are submitted electronically via smart forms or a PDFa data box.
In 2015, persons handling special mineral oils submitted 630 notifications.
The seizure and forfeiture of special mineral oils or, where appropriate, means of transport must be pronounced by the tax administrator in cases where it finds the handling of special mineral oils without registration or where the registered person fails to comply with his notification obligation.
As in the case of failure to comply with obligations in the transport of products subject to excise duties, these deficiencies cannot be remedied retrospectively.
Registration of a fuel distributor is mandatory for persons who sell or are entitled to sell fuel.
Registered fuel distributors may only be persons meeting the following criteria:
Compulsory licence of the Trade Licensing Office (specific form of trade licence).
The application for a concession or, where appropriate, the appointment of the responsible representative, shall be given an opinion by the customs office examining whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory body or the members of the applicant's statutory body - the legal person and the appointed responsible representative fulfil the condition of reliability.
Where such persons satisfy the condition of reliability, the customs office shall issue an affirmative opinion.
A reliable person means a person of integrity, in terms of a criminal-law property nature, customs and tax law.
The condition for the issuance of the concession is professional competence.
The integrity of the same circle of persons as in the case of reliability.
The debtor is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will properly and timely fulfil his payment obligations towards the state, i.e. he does not have arrears to the state budget and on general health insurance.
The fuel distributor shall not be subject to a prohibition by the court or administrative authority of the activity preventing the pursuit of its activities.
The fuel distributor shall not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
The deposit (if any bank guarantee) of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. about €740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 (i.e. approx. €370,000) after three years of registration by a fuel distributor and the fulfilment of other conditions.
Notice of distribution of fuel is required by the distributor to the customs office within 20 days after the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification shall include details of individual fuel purchases and sales.
The reported data are details of business partners, document numbers, selected product, quantity, price, carrier and transport, loading point and unloading.
The right to refund the tax on mineral oils consumed in agricultural primary production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
The refund of excise duty on mineral oils can only be claimed for that activity which is manifestly linked to the activity carried out on land.
In 2015, there were about 64,000 claimed refund claims totalling CZK 1,172,844,680 (i.e. €43,401,720).
Since 2017, the government of the Czech Republic has also introduced the refund of excise duty on fuel to livestock farmers.
Newly, farmers or breeders who deal with cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats, for example, will be able to claim this entitlement.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of tobacco products at the old tax rate
In response to the long-term below-budgeted revenue from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced, with effect from 1 December 2014, a restriction on the sale of tobacco products at the old rate of tax in the event of a change in the tax rate.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid by the use of tobacco stickers.
The use of a tobacco sticker means its placement on unit packing (Section 116 of the Excise Tax Act).
For the application of the rate of excise duty, the production of a tobacco product in a state intended for the final consumer is decisive, with no need to remove it, supply, dispatch or sale or sale to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterising the excise duty rate is shown on the tobacco label together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, the label also lists the number of pieces in the pack or the amount of smoking tobacco in kilograms.
The tobacco sticker has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the sale of unit packs of cigarettes intended for direct consumption and bearing a tobacco label with a previous (old) rate of tax was established until the end of the last day of the second calendar month following the application of the new rate of excise duty.
The evolution of tobacco stickers in 2014 and the comparison with developments in previous years show that tobacco manufacturers have significantly frontloaded tobacco products with an "old" tax rate each year, resulting in a de facto shift in the effectiveness of the "new" tax rate by about one year.
Tax on raw tobacco
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the production of tobacco products without the authorisation of the tax administrator and the non-payment of excise duty, a raw tobacco tax and monitoring the handling of raw tobacco were introduced as anti-tax fraud measures.
With effect from 1 July 2015, the excise duty shall be subject to raw tobacco which has not been used or delivered for the manufacture of tobacco products to another Member State or third country or for which the origin, use or person to be supplied or to be supplied with raw tobacco has not been established.
Restrictions on dealing with raw tobacco
Measures such as the supervision of the transport and production of tobacco products, the marking of unit packs with control tape and the restriction of sales at the designated sites have been supplemented by restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
Production equipment for the processing of tobacco raw material and the manufacture of tobacco products is not subject to the supervision of customs authorities.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or modified.
Only a person who meets the personal circumstances of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative may be a registered person, which is valid throughout the registration.
The conditions of registration are: (a) the authorisation to operate a trade allowing the performance of the activity of the person storing raw tobacco, (b) reliability, (c) indebtedness, (d) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco has not been banned from operating activities, (e) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, (f) the provision of a deposit of 20 000 000 CZK (i.e. approx. 740 000 €).
Electronic registration shall include the date of receipt or dispensing of raw tobacco, the document number, identification of the trading partner, the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a person storing raw tobacco shall be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours prior to receipt or dispatch.
Details of the trading partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the address of storage, the purpose of use and the details of the carrier shall be reported.
The notice of the anticipated quantity in the relevant year of received or dispatched raw tobacco shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications are submitted electronically by a PDFa data box.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the prescribed essentials.
Legislative of excise duties in SR
The legal framework regulating excise duties in the SR is based on EU legislation and thus co-creates its single tax system.
Individual types of excise taxes are exhaustively determined by SR legislation, which is similar to the legislation of the surrounding countries.
Definition of legislation in the Slovak Republic
The legislative regulation of excise duties is ensured by four laws according to individual subject-matter of the tax.
Harmonisation was achieved by the adoption of the following laws on excise duties: Act No 98/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No 106/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No 530/2011 Z. z., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No 609/2007 Z. z., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All excise tax laws are rules of substantive law and deal with the taxation of the subject-matter of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No 563/2009 Z. z., on tax administration (tax rules), is a matter of procedural law, regulating the administration of taxes, rights and obligations of tax entities and others.
This legal framework transposed the individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/EC of 16 December 2008 on the general arrangements for excise duty and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC, and transposed the provisions of other directives and legislation of the European Community.
Structure of legislative changes for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Slovak Republic
Since 2011, legislation on the administration of excise duties has undergone several major changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In EMCS, the monitoring of the transport of selected products subject to excise duties under a conditional exemption scheme has been changed from a documentary accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system where these services are monitored in real time.
Under the EMCS electronic system, an institute of suspension of access to EMCS was introduced in 2015.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The customs office has the option of suspending access precisely on justified concern about the non-payment or undetermined tax on previous tax periods and its unenforceability.
This applies to the maturity of the tax, as the transport of excise goods requires the composition of the collateral, which shall, however, be released by the end of transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A major change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the possibility of using so-called red diesel was abolished.
The gas oil, commonly also called red diesel, was one of the mineral oils.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific legally defined purposes, e.g. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The abolition of red diesel was aimed at reducing the public deficit, simplifying the system for taxing mineral oils and reducing the administrative burden on the business entities concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel seller.
The purpose of this legal change was to introduce a registration obligation for all petrol stations.
Clarification of the movement of taxed gasoline and diesel is linked to the obligation to buy petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
In 2014, new institute institutes of tax entities were introduced, namely a fuel distributor and a fuel consumer.
That change contributed to the elimination of tax evasion for petrol and diesel and clarified the movement of these propellants (see Annex 4, Scheme A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading lubricating and base oils have been extended.
In the SR, however, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to designate an indication.
Excise duty on tobacco products
In order to combat tax evasion and the monitoring of tobacco raw material, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Materials Act has been extended and a new tax entity - a tobacco raw material trader - has been introduced.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
In addition, an obligation was introduced to record technological equipment for the production of tobacco products.
The legislation has brought about a new system for ordering, judging, printing, distribution and use of check marks designed to mark consumer packaging of tobacco products.
The checkpoint refers to cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Under the new system, the purchaser of the check marks must apply to the customs office electronically for the issue of the check marks by means of an information system for the collection of control marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was set up – in the Kremnice Mincovna.
The exercise of the tax oversight of the printing of control stamps was also introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system for printing check marks strengthens the goods control system, as a unique identification number is generated on the check mark, which can simply verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1-2nd place is the check sum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to a checkpoint or a group of packages; 4th place is a series identifier; 5th-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9.-12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
The checkpoint intended for the labelling of cigarettes must also indicate the price of cigarettes, the emblem for the validity of the excise duty rate, the number of cigarettes in consumer packaging and the length of cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer because the original three substantive law regulations were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The law was developed mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution to the issue of the taxation of alcoholic beverages, the management of their production, the monitoring of movements, the provision of the tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, to streamline the performance of tax administration, to reduce the administrative burden for small and medium-sized entrepreneurs.
A new way of addressing the issue of taxation of individual types of alcoholic beverages introduced the use of a uniform rate of excise duty on alcoholic beverage and took into account the volume percentage of actual alcohol content.
For non-fat wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the volume percentage of actual alcoholic strength in the final product is taken into account.
The concentration of beer is also expressed as a percentage of the actual alcoholic strength in the finished product.
A category of small-scale fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is to exempt from excise duty for a natural person who produces a sparkling fermented self-consumption drink and for the consumption of his household for a maximum of 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation has brought about a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using check marks for labelling consumer alcohol packaging.
Under the new system, the purchaser of the check marks must apply to the customs office electronically for the issue of the check marks by means of an information system for the collection of control marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was set up – in the Kremnice Mincovna.
The exercise of the tax oversight of the printing of control stamps was also introduced.
The changes contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Schedule B) and the elimination of falsification of control signs.
The new system for printing check marks strengthens the goods control system, as a unique identification number is generated on the check mark, which can simply verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1-2nd place is the check sum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to a checkpoint or a group of packages; 4th place is a series identifier; 5th-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9.-12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise taxes on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common Act No. 353/2003 Coll.
Solid fuel tax, tax on natural gas and certain other gases and electricity tax are part of Act No 261/2007 Coll.
In contrast, in the Slovak Republic, every excise duty is regulated by a special law, except for the Excise Tax Act on alcoholic beverages, which contains a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, as of 1 January 2015, the issue of an authorisation to dispose of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is conditional, among other things, on the demonstration of the economic stability of applicants, which customs authorities verify annually by carrying out a financial analysis.
In the SR, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding to waive or reduce tax security.
FŘ SR exercises tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of control marks for the marking of alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printer and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of control stamps is provided by the state enterprise Mincovna Kremnica.
The production of tobacco stickers and control tapes in the Czech Republic is not introduced in the printing works by customs authorities.
He will take the tobacco stickers and control tapes from the printer commissioned territorial office of the customs office in Kutná Hora.
Tobacco stickers are taken over by their customers at this territorial workplace, the control tapes to mark alcohol are further distributed to individual locally competent tax authorities according to the location of the marking.
The legislation of the Czech Republic does not define the manufacturers of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
In the SR there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or its part, in the Czech Republic such an obligation is not introduced.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco sticker bears the excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when collecting tobacco stickers at the designated customs office.
In the SR, on the other hand, the control mark does not contain excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced in the Czech Republic in the case of their use for agricultural plant primary production, the so-called green diesel.
Since 2017, this tax refund has been extended to livestock production.
In the SR, such support for farmers is not introduced (it existed until 31.12.2010 as so-called red diesel).
To strengthen the fight against tax fraud, bail of CZK 20 million was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic. CZK (i.e. 740 thousand €).
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors was reduced from 1,891 entities in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1,717 tax entities).
A similar institute of a fuel distributor is introduced in the SR, but without the deposit of the deposit needed to ensure excise duty on mineral oils.
There were 303 distributors registered in the SR in 2014 and 407 distributors were registered in 2015.
In the SR, an institute of a fuel seller and a fuel consumer is in place, which is authorised by the locally competent customs office.
Such an institute is not introduced in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils and also some other mineral oils are subject to labelling, in the Slovak Republic, after the abolition of so-called red diesel, the labelling of mineral oils is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the alcohol marking control tape contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of the alcohol and a 12-digit registration code indicating the spirit drink, according to which a record of control tapes is kept.
Destruction, loss and return of the control tape are entered in the register the following working day.
The holder of the tape is obliged to notify their use within the same time limit.
In SR, the control mark intended to mark alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number, which, if used once a month, is communicated to the tax administrator and is used to verify the authenticity of the check mark.
The register contains the number of collected, used and claimed check marks.
Both the Czech Republic and Slovakia introduced the institute of mandatory registration or registration of the distributor of alcohol.
In the SR, registration is subject to compliance with, inter alia, a storage area exceeding 200 m2; an annual turnover from the sale of a consumer pack of alcohol at least €100,000 or a paid-up equity of at least €100,000; a minimum of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining a registration is subject, among other things, to deposit a deposit of CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) in favour of the tax administrator for the entire period of validity of the registration.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In Slovakia, the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging requires a permanent presence of the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, the production of alcohol in consumer packaging requires a special form of registration of a person obligated to mark alcohol with the condition of posting bail in favour of the tax administrator from CZK 100,000 (i.e. €3,700) up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) depending on the amount of control strips collected and the installation of a tracking device with the continuous approach of the tax administrator.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and Slovakia far exceeds the EU's minimum requirements for subject matter and administration of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as to the risks identified in tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted in the audited period allow tax administrations to more pre-empt the emergence of possible tax evasion.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, in the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw material (e.g. sheets), an excise tax on raw tobacco or tobacco raw material has been introduced beyond EU legislation.
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw material are not a harmonised tobacco product, they monitor both the Czech Republic and Slovakia's movements.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic can recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the examination of economic stability for applicants for authorisation under the Excise Tax Act has proved successful because it reduces the risks of tax arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend applying such vetting also in SR conditions.
The distribution of check marks in the Slovak Republic is more efficient than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden customs authorities with the costs associated with transport between the printer and the customer of control tapes and tobacco stickers.
The SR Financial Administration has a better overview of the existence and location of technological equipment for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, the collection of tax on tobacco products is more efficient, because the tobacco sticker order itself is a tax return with a subsequent tax payment.
Thanks to the introduction of "propellant sellers" and "fuel consumer" institutes, the financial administration in Slovakia has a better overview of fuel sales points.
The introduction of mandatory mineral oil labelling in the Czech Republic makes it easier to control the misuse of mineral oils with a reduced tax rate or exempt.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and in SR (2014) a new control tape, or a stamp containing the identification code, was introduced.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains a registration code, while in Slovakia the new legislation has abandoned its introduction.
The impacts cannot yet be assessed due to the short effectiveness of legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol by a control mark or tape is an effective measure in the fight against tax evasion.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic may also recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States.
The SR's position on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterised by a pro-ient approach that does not block the funds of tax entities.
By contrast, the Czech Republic's approach is rather restrictive because it introduces a bail burdening the cash flow of tax entities, but it further reduces the risk of tax arrears.
Development of income from excise duties
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the State to increase the revenue of the state budget and also to regulate the quantity of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered harmful to the individual and/or to society (regulatory functions of the tax).
According to the Communication from the Commission: EUROPE 2020 - A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3.3.2010 under the flagship initiative Europe less resource-intensive, the European Commission's intention is to improve the market-based framework for the use of instruments, including in the form of a revision of energy taxation with a focus on reducing energy consumption and resources.
In order to fulfil the EC's intention, Member States should seek to shift the tax burden from the workforce, including to energy and environmental taxation, as part of greater "environmental" tax systems.
The collection of tax revenues from excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia includes the collection of excise duty on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and share of GDP is also monitored by the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD), among others.
Both supreme audit institutions used the following selection criteria to enter a query on the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP fell slightly, according to OECD data.
The exchange rate of the European Central Bank of the ECB was used to convert the amounts in CZK to EUR 31.12. of the relevant year.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against € in 2013 weakened by 9.1% year-on-year compared to 2012 (from 25,140 to 27,425).
This was mainly due to the CNB Bank Board's monetary policy decision of 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of collection of excise duties, excise duties and income per capita in € have decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant reduction in the share of excise duties in 2014 was due to a one-off shortfall in excise duty revenues from tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of old-tax tobacco products.
The share of excise duties is also influenced by the rise in revenue tax collection, which has grown significantly as a result of the improved overall economic situation of the Czech Republic.
The excise tax on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the total collection of excise duties (about 55.7% in 2015), but this fell despite significant economic growth compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duty on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although registration of fuel distributors was introduced in 2013 as anti-tax fraud measures.
The trend of environmentally-saving vehicles and the promotion of biofuels are negatively reflected in the tax revenue.
A negligible share is the tax on natural gas, the tax on solid fuels and the electricity tax, which is due to the low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to the surrounding states.
In the future, if there is no rate hike, their share will decline in the future in view of the ever-increasing energy performance of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the repercussions of a large-scale case of tax fraud consisting in the marketing of untaxed alcohol, alcohol containing methanol or insufficiently denatured alcohol in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a series of measures against such conduct and the recovery of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded by EUR 4 million.
The share of the tax on tobacco products increased as a result of rising rates.
The basic rates of excise duties changed between 2012-2015 for the tobacco tax, where the rate was increased mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011/64/EU, on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
Due to the CNB's currency intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, in addition to the tobacco product tax, has fallen significantly. It has risen only slightly for tobacco products.
In relation to price growth, GDP or living standards, the indexation of the excise tax rate is not set, so the function of excise taxes to regulate socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With the economic growth of the Czech Republic and the rise in living standards, real rates of excise duties are decreasing.
7 Indexation – automatic adjustment of a certain economic quantity for inflation, this adjustment takes place on the basis of a law or contract (for pensions paid by the State, it is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Slovak Republic
The current legislation on excise duties in the SR does not address the indexation of the level of excise duty rates on consumer price developments because they are fixed.

Of all the excise taxes introduced in Slovakia, it is the excise tax on mineral oils that accounts for the largest share of the national budget's full-year tax revenues, while its share did not fall below 52% in the whole audited period.
The second largest share is excise duty on tobacco products.
This tax accounts for an average of around 32% of total collection from excise duties.
Between 2012 and 2015, there was an increase in the collection of excise duty per inhabitant of the SR.
This development is due to a rise in excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The growth in excise duty collection per inhabitant of the SR is constant and corresponds to the evolution of excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the reduction in income in € per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention on the exchange rate of the koruna against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which is about 2.7 times higher in the Czech Republic, respectively 2.8 times higher, per inhabitant of the Czech Republic, however, the collection for these selected products is already only about 1/3.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower excise tax rates in the Czech Republic and the CZK exchange rate against foreign consumers.
The mineral oil tax also causes greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of a tax on tobacco products, growing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a not insignificant effect.
Evaluation of Real rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic fell as a result of the CNB's interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in total tax revenues is not rising and there is no shift from labour taxation to tax the consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the achieved values of the share of excise duties are consistently above average compared to the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is mainly influenced by the change in excise duty rates, the development of economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future shortfalls in excise duty collection due to environmental measures subsidised by the State in various forms will need to be replaced by other revenues or by reducing state spending.
By not introducing an indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, their regulatory functions are reduced and the EU's objectives of a less dependent environmentally dependent on environmentally unsparing sources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco are insufficiently supported.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic shows higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and revenue related to the administration of excise duties, i.e. it expresses the amount of expenditure per 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The efficiency of the tax administrator in tax administration is influenced by the scope and organisational layout of the tax administrator, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of electronization of individual activities.
The determination of the efficiency of the administrative costs of tax administration by the conversion coefficient method is based on the number of employees involved in the administration of excise duties in a line-based structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is carried out by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate organizational unit of the state and the accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax administration is provided by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, while the customs authorities are an internal organisational unit, costs and revenues are included collectively for the entire organisational unit.
Therefore, in view of the possibility of comparing the efficiency of the administration of excise duties, the expenses and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were included in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative tasks carried out mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some sub-control operations are carried out by other public authorities, but their importance is negligible.
In particular, the administration of excise duties shall be carried out by the following departments:
General Directorate of Customs
Department 23 DAŇOVÝ
Section 231 - Tax methods monitor and propose legislative measures, ensures legislative interpretation, methodically manages and coordinates: execution of tax administration and related rules agendas, in particular tax management and related control and supervisory activities, administration of transport of selected products;
Unit 232 - ELO and search performs searches and methodically manages the traffic checks of selected products and ensures international cooperation between the ELO and EMCS;
Unit 233 - Tax controls methodically manage and coordinate the implementation of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Department 30 LEGAL
Section 301 – Legal carries out methodological activity in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative procedure, tax control process, registration procedure, trial, payment of taxes, fines for late tax, penalty payments and interest;
Unit 302 – Administrative activities carry out decision-making activities in cases where the legislation provides for the competence of the DGC, e.g. deciding on a delegation of the body's territorial jurisdiction to another matter-of-factor tax administrator, decision-making on the attraction, i.e. taking over the case by the superior tax administrator, appeals against decisions of customs offices and examines initiatives for inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Unit 303 - Income management and enforcement methodically manage, coordinate and perform tasks in the context of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the performance of insolvency proceedings tasks;
Department 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION AID
Unit 601 - Risk and criminal analyses ensure and performs risk analyses and participates in the management of executive risks and the planning of control activities and control actions;
Unit 604 - Financial analyses carry out financial analysis in the customs administration, in particular in the context of the authorisation procedure.
Customs authorities carry out activities as part of the agenda at various points in the county, and even the agendas are scattered in more places:
Unit 02 - Analyses and information support that carry out risk analyses, risk profile management and collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Department 1 LEGAL
Section 11 – Legal and administrative activities which process the documents, opinions and submissions to the Appellate Body, issue a permit decision in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the law on the compulsory marking of ethyl alcohol and the Alcohol Act, decides on the provision of payment for the outstanding or not yet determined tax;
Department 3 – DAŇOVÝ
Section 31 – Taxation which carries out agendas: tax supervision of tax entities, e.g. control of compliance with the conditions laid down in the permits issued, supervision of the functionality and correctness of the production equipment for the production of alcohol and the detection of quantities and concentrations for alcohol produced, professional supervision for the denaturing of alcohol, physical control in the field of excise tax administration; non-tax controls in the field of controls on the basis of indirect relation to excise duty laws, in particular the control of compulsory marking and colouring of selected mineral oils, checking the taxation of selected products, checking the labelling of tobacco products, checking whether the seller or buyer does not infringe the law on prices and other pricing regulations, performs acts in connection with the law on the connection with the legal equipment of the livestock.
department 39 – Tobacco stickers and control strips – is the organisational unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region and carries out activities in the field of ordering, production and distribution and disposal of tobacco stickers and control strips.
For the liquidation of returned/damaged tobacco labels, both customs office representatives and representatives of the DGT are present to oversee the winding-up process and write down the liquidation alert.
For alcohol marking control bands, the director of the customs office shall appoint an internal act of proceedings to the three-member commission for the disposal of discarded uncollected/returned control bands by shredding.
Once the physical shredding of the control bands has been carried out, the chairman of the liquidation commission shall ensure the registration of the data on the destroyed control tapes;
Department 5 – CONTROL,
Section 52 - Tax inspections carry out tax inspections;
Department 6 – AGREED
Unit 61 – Supervision of entities supervises entities at points of sale, e.g. control of the sale of spirits and tobacco products;
Unit 62 - Mobile surveillance checks on the transport of selected products on the way.
Administrative costs of excise tax management in the SR
Since 1 January 2012, the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a challenging transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The formation of the FŘ SR was also reflected in the composition of the employees of the newly created departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In relation to the performance of excise duty management, excise duty management activities within the organisational structure of the FŘ SR have been integrated into a larger number of different sections and related unions.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Section of Customs and Tax Section of the SR Department of Excise Taxes (Loth-Slovakia):
Excise duty separation - directs and coordinates activities in the field of excise duty management; draws up expert opinions; makes proposals and comments on legislative changes; issues decisions on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax authorities; allocate and repeal registration numbers;
the tax supervision department - directs and coordinates activities in the field of tax supervision and tax control; carries out tax supervision;
ELO and SPD systems - guides and coordinates mutual administrative cooperation activities in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through SEED and MVS; ensures management and updates in SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
Unit of the check marks - directs activities in the field of printing and handling of check marks; carries out tax supervision of the loading and disposal of printing sheets and checkpoints in the printer.
The Department of the Vice-President of the Financial Administration
Expert of legal remedies for excise duties and duties (wide-Slovak scope):
the separation of legal remedies for excise duties - reviews the decisions of the customs offices on the basis of the proper and extraordinary remedies applied; the appeal procedure at the second instance of the decision-making process.
The Customs Section was established during 2012; individual customs offices (9 customs offices) which have territorial jurisdiction designated by higher territorial units were directly incorporated under it, with the exception of one customs office established, inter alia, to carry out tasks in relation to the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
the separation of excise duties - the pursuit of a methodological activity in relation to branches of customs offices and to customs offices' stations; performs direct acts of the tax administrator for selected entities, and this decides on the registration (tax warehouse, authorised recipient repeated, registered consignor), on the amount of tax security, fixes and returns tax, carries out tax supervision and tax control; decides to waive the suspension of the obligation to safeguard the presence of a customs office employee in a liquor tax warehouse;
legal – decision-making activities in respect of tax infringements; activities related to sound and extraordinary remedies; tax enforcement proceedings;
a branch of the customs office - decides on the registration (with the exception of the tax warehouse, the authorised recipient for re-entry, registered consignor), the amount of the security of the tax; prescribes and returns the tax; exercises tax supervision and tax control; decides on the security and forfeiture of the goods;
customs office station - the exercise of tax supervision of the holding and movement of excise goods; ensures the exercise of permanent tax supervision in a liquor tax warehouse; decides on the security and forfeiture of goods.
SR's financial administration's spending on excise tax management is steadily rising as, with the exception of wage growth, investment increases in effective tax administration and computerisation of financial management.
Although revenue from excise duties rose, spending grew faster as a result of IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project.
Wage expenses in the Slovak Republic are significantly affected by the performance of permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses, which the Czech Republic does not apply.
Expenditure by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on excise tax management increased significantly between 2012 and 2015 in 2015, this growth was mainly due to increases in wage expenditure and technical support expenditure.
In the Czech Republic, revenues from excise duties also grew at approximately the same rate.
Wage expenses in the Czech Republic are positively influenced compared to the Slovak Republic by the wider competences of the customs administration, e.g. the weighing of trucks, the control of the fulfilment of obligations in connection with the myth.
The efficiency of administrative costs in the Slovak Republic shows a slightly deteriorating trend year-on-year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but spending per employee grew.
In the Czech Republic, too, the number of employees did not change significantly, but spending per employee grew more slowly compared to SR.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, wage growth is an important factor in the worsening efficiency of administrative spending, which can be assessed as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a significant administrative burden in administering excise duties appears to be a negative factor, confirming an undisturbed number of employees in the field of excise tax administration.
In the SR, however, the administration of excise duties at lower revenues is significantly more demanding on staffing capacity.
Performance indicators of excise tax administration
The management of excise duties is a set of activities aimed at correctly identifying, determining and securing the payment of the tax.
The main processes in the administration of excise duties are tax assessment, authorisation and registration for activities, traffic supervision, control and search of tax entities.
The numbers of administrative tasks and managed entities are indicators of the performance of the tax administrator.
The correlation between the observed indicator and the number of tax administrations expresses the effectiveness of the tax administrator's activities and defines the cost of a particular activity.
Authorisation and registration for activities are a prerequisite for the handling and transport of selected products for commercial purposes under a suspensive exemption scheme.
The tax administrator is obliged to carry out a continuous administration with a view to supervising the fulfilment of the legislation and the conditions laid down by the tax administrator, for which adequate staff resources must be allocated.
The indicator monitored was the number of valid permits or registrations to operate on 31 December of each year.
The number of permits or registrations issued is not the same as the number of tax entities.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in the case.
The administrative tasks monitored are the most significant actions of the tax administrator (tax declaration, administration of transport in EMCS), or activities which are the sequence of acts concluded by a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Permission and registration for activities in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
It is possible to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products on the basis of the tax administrator's permission to operate a tax warehouse.
If the tax warehouse operator has multiple warehouses, the authorisation for each shall be issued separately, including the security of the tax.
Tax security is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administrator (i.e. the physical presence of an official and the provision of equipment by the tax administrator's conclusions).
In the Czech Republic, permanent tax supervision is not applied.
The operator of a tax warehouse is also registered for tax under Section 125 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.
Authorisation to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products suspended from tax purposes to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to an export point in another Member State or to a consignee in another Member State (replaces the status of registered consignor pursuant to Article 4(10) of Council Directive 2008/118/EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include authorisations for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels, excluding tax purposes, which are analogous to the authorisation of a tax warehouse.
Growing brandy produces alcohol with a reduced 50% tax rate (14,300 CZK/hl ethanol) – fruit spirits for growers. It is not tax in stock and the permit for operation is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced tax rate can be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per household of a grower intended for personal consumption over the production period (July-June).
The registration of cultivation burning, which is kept by the operators of the distillery and made available to the tax authorities, must contain information on the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
A beneficiary authorised for the re-admission of selected products and authorised beneficiaries for the one-off acceptance of selected products shall, on the basis of the authorisation of the tax administrator and the conditions laid down, be entitled to accept or repeatedly accept selected products in a conditional system carried from another Member State.
The beneficiary is not the operator of the tax warehouse and may not store or dispatch the selected products under the suspensive exemption scheme.
The user of selected products exempt from tax is a legal or natural person who accepts and uses, or according to Section 52a or 53 of Act No 353/2003 Coll., sells selected products exempt to another user; users have the status of tax entities without the obligation to register for tax purposes.
Exempt-free products may be accepted and used only on the basis of a final authorisation, and only from the supplier referred to in the permit.
On the basis of a permit, exempt mineral oils may be sold to another holder of an authorisation for use or to a user who is entitled to use mineral oils without authorisation.
Without a permit, exempt mineral oils may be sold in statutory cases, e.g.:
waste oils in quantities of less than 10 000 litres per calendar year if the user produced them themselves or were created during its operation,
exempt mineral oils collected in unit packings of not more than 20 litres intended for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production, while intended for sale to the final consumer.
It is possible to transport exempt selected products with an exemption document.
The distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging is entitled, after compulsory registration with the tax administrator, to sell or otherwise transfer the ethyl alcohol put into free tax circulation.
The warehousekeeper of raw tobacco is entitled, on the basis of registration with the tax administrator and the conditions laid down, to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products.
A person dealing with special mineral oils is entitled, on the basis of registration with the tax administrator and the conditions laid down, to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils which are in bulk or placed in a package exceeding 220 litres.
The fuel distributor is entitled, on the basis of the concession issued and the registration of the tax administrator, under specified conditions, to sell fuel in the territory of the Czech Republic, with the exception of the sale of fuel from the service station.
The transport of PHM must be accompanied by a tax document, proof of sale or proof of transport, or a delivery plan and bottling tickets.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent before the commencement of transport to the tax authorities.
The operator of the petrol station is the owner of the fuel sold at the petrol station.
Petrol stations are places where, on the basis of permission from the building authority, the sale or dispensing of PHM is usually allowed into the fuel tank.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators broken down into: registered – normal sale or dispensing of PHM as a rule to vehicle fuel tanks; with a defined approach – operation generally in various company sites (e.g. quarries, sawmills, agricultural farms, transport organisations, building courts), sales are made here for the other party limited on the basis of specific contractual relations; non-public - fuel dispensing points only for the operator's own consumption.
The pumping station is not the construction or equipment in the form of an operating tank located in operation (e.g. on the chassis) if the fuel is issued for its own use only.
Operating tanks are not subject to the permission of the tax administrator and are not registered.
To buy, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free tax circulation for resale for resale, natural and legal persons may, on the basis of the authorisation of the tax administrator.
They must also be authorised if they purchase or obtain liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption exceeding 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax control is a set of actions. Tax control is subject to tax liability, claims made by the taxpayer or other circumstances relevant to the correct determination and determination of the tax relating to a single tax procedure.
Tax control can be carried out jointly for multiple tax proceedings of one taxpayer.
Repeated tax control can only be carried out under the conditions laid down by law and justification at the start of the inspection.
Tax control shall be carried out within the time limit for determining the tax, which is three years, the time limit being extended by one year under the conditions laid down by law (e.g. filing additional tax proceedings, bringing criminal proceedings in relation to the tax in question) or building (court proceedings, international cooperation).
The time limit for determining the tax shall expire at the latest 10 years after the expiry of the period for making a proper tax claim.
The tax administrator is not required to carry out a tax check on each taxpayer.
The start of the tax inspection puts the time limits for the possibility of filing an additional tax return or additional billing by the tax entity (Section 141 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.) and reopens the running of the time limit for determining the tax (Section 148 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
Based on its outcome, the tax may be charged ex officio.
A local investigation is an individual time-limited act (one day) in which the tax administrator searches for evidence and carries out the examination of premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and transport packaging with tax entities and other persons involved in the tax administration, on the spot outside the premises of the tax administrator (e.g. at the tax entity, at the point of sale, on the road to transport).
The tax administrator is entitled to borrow documents and belongings, take samples or secure them.
Based on the outcome of the local investigation, tax cannot be separately assessed, but the taxpayer can be asked to file an additional tax return (Section 145(2) of Act No 280/2009 Coll.).
The control of traffic data in EMCS is not a local investigation.
Ordering control bands to mark alcohol may only be submitted to the tax administrator to the locally competent marking point of the markings by the registered person liable for alcohol and is carried out through intelligent forms that are automatically imported into the application of the alcohol marker register.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the ordered amount of control tapes and orders production.
He doesn't supervise the production of control tapes.
Production is provided by the State Securities Printer, a state enterprise.
A purchaser of control tapes takes control tapes from the tax administrator to the locally relevant marking point.
Ordering tobacco stickers to mark cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco perform the function of a tax return.
The value of the tobacco sticker corresponds to the amount of the tax liability, whereby the purchaser of the tobacco stickers is obliged to pay their value within 60 days from the date of their removal from the tax administrator.
The customer is obliged to calculate in the order himself the value corresponding to the amount of tax liability of the ordered tobacco stickers.
This period applies only if the value of the tobacco stickers is secured.
The order of tobacco stickers shall be submitted on a form set out by the Ministry of Finance in writing or via a data box with the possibility of using intelligent forms.
The production of tobacco stickers is provided by the State Securities Printer, a state enterprise.
The designated tax administrator, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (Kutná Hora territorial workplace), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax administrator, which further distributes them and further examines their transport, storage and use with customers.
Tax claims include proper tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including tobacco sticker orders, filed by tax entities.
Included is not the allocation of tax under the customs procedure on the basis of customs declarations and the granting of claims for refunds on: mineral oils used for the production of heat, other petrol used in the course of a business other than for the production of heat or engine propulsion, mineral oils used for agricultural primary production.
The fines imposed include administrative proceedings to deal with established infringements, a set of successive administrative acts. The international exchange of information on tax entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 takes place in the form of: requests for administrative cooperation, response to a request for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, event reports, inspection reports.
Transport under a conditional tax exemption regime between the Czech Republic and EU Member States - the Czech customs office is the tax administrator of the receiving or sending tax warehouse or authorised recipient.
Performance indicators in SR
Authorisation and registration for activity in the SR
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is mainly ensured by the customs authorities and the Department of Excise Taxation of the Section of Customs and Taxation of the SR, whose procedure for administering excise duties is governed by individual excise tax laws and the tax code.
These laws provide not only for the scope of the authorisation for the CÚ and the FD of the SR to administer excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax entities in connection with the registration or payment of excise duty.
The largest year-on-year increase in tax entities (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, due to an increase in tax warehouse permits issued, an increase in the registrations of the beneficiary for re-admission and the registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation refined the transport of certain bulk mineral oils as well as the notification obligation if they are transported freely or in packaging with a content of more than 150 litres or 230 litres, respectively, and also extended the list of mineral oils subject to control and procedure for transport with other goods, such as anti-ticking preparations, oxidative inhibitors, bitumen inhibitors, viscosity improvement products, anti-corrosion products.
For lubricating oils, a mandatory indication was introduced regarding the indication of their kinematic viscosity.
The approximation of the registration process for selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the SR is set out in the following parts of the document.
Operator of a tax warehouse
Under SR's national legislation, when registering a tax warehouse operator under all items of excise duty, a person wishing to operate a tax warehouse must also apply at the same time to register and issue an authorisation to operate a tax warehouse.
The resulting decision in the registration process is the registration certificate for the relevant excise duty, by which the tax warehouse operator obtains legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CÚ shall issue an authorisation to operate a tax warehouse which entitles the tax warehouse operator in that tax warehouse to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under a conditional exemption scheme.
If the tax warehouse operator has tax warehouses in multiple locations, the tax administrator shall issue a separate licence to operate a tax warehouse for each tax warehouse.
The transport of the subject of excise duty under the suspensive tax regime is monitored electronically through EMCS.
Each shipment generates a unique reference code, the so-called
ARC code under which the transport can be tracked online and therefore in real time.
If the operator of a tax warehouse is also a person authorised to distribute alcohol, it is obliged to notify electronically the commercial name of the consumer pack of alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer packaging of alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging which it puts into free tax circulation at the latest on the date of its introduction.
Registered sender
The registered consignor is a special type of taxpayer which cannot also be registered as a tax warehouse operator at the same time, even if it dispatches the subject of excise duty under the suspensive regime after its release for free circulation.
Under the national legislation of the SR when registering a registered consignor under all subject-matter of excise duties, a person wishing to dispatch the subject of excise duty under a suspensive exemption scheme after his release under the customs procedure "free circulation" must also apply to the CCA at the same time for registration and the issue of an authorisation to dispatch the subject of excise duty under that scheme.
The CU shall issue a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty and at the same time also issue an authorisation to dispatch the subject of excise duty under a suspensive exemption scheme after its release under the customs procedure ‘free circulation’.
Growing brandy
The basic act for the operation of cultivation brandy is to obtain a permit for the production of alcohol in a distilling plant from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, the permit from the Ministry itself does not entitle the holder of a permit to operate a cultivation distillery.
In order to be able to operate a cultivation distillery, a person must submit an application to the CU for registration and issue a registration certificate for the operator of a distillery.
The CU will issue a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, which at the same time authorises the operators of the cultivation distillery for the production of alcohol in the crop distillery.
The purpose of growing distillery is to provide services to growers.
Growing brandy cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislator allows a reduced rate of tax to be applied to alcohol produced in a growing distillery, amounting to 50 % of the standard tax rate, i.e. 540 €/hl a.
The reduced tax rate shall apply to ethyl alcohol produced in a growing distillery of no more than 43 litres per grower and its household per production period in the tax area.
The production period runs from the 1st 7th current year to the 30th of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year and therefore it is possible to apply a multiple reduced tax rate to the alcohol produced within one calendar year, as the alcohol is produced in two production periods.
This is the production of alcohol outside the conditional exemption scheme, which in practice means that the alcohol produced is in free tax circulation.
The grower for the alcohol produced will pay the cultivation brandy not only excise duty and value added tax, but also the price for the services provided.
The grower's brandy will issue a removal certificate to the grower, which serves not only as proof of proof of origin and how to acquire alcohol, but also to pay excise duty.
The transport of alcohol thus produced is not subject to monitoring by the tax administrator.
Importer of consumer packaging
National legislation allows persons intending to import consumer packs of ethyl alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country in business and to put it into free tax circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CPC for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
The consumer packaging importer shall not register for the relevant excise duty but shall be issued with a certificate of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
That certificate authorises the importer to import a consumer pack of alcohol or a consumer pack of cigarettes from the territory of a non-member country.
At the same time, before issuing the check marks, they must lodge a tax guarantee equal to the amount of alcohol or cigarettes it wishes to put into free tax circulation.
The consumer packaging importer must put into free tax circulation only the consumer pack bearing the check mark.
For this reason, it must submit to the customs office the number and identification number of the check marks exported to the territory of a third State.
On importation, the importer is obliged to have the number of check marks imported back from the territory of a third country confirmed by the customs office of importation.
When importing consumer packaging, the importer proceeds within the meaning of customs legislation, where the amount of excise duty is also part of the customs debt.
In the event of the release of consumer packaging for free tax circulation, the tax guarantee lodged shall be returned to the importer or may be used to pay the customs debt.
The consumer packaging importer is not tax in stock.
If the consumer alcohol-pack importer is also the person authorised to distribute the alcohol, he is obliged to notify electronically to the CU the commercial name of the consumer pack of alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the consumer pack of alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free tax circulation at the latest on the date of its entry.
Seller of consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and the elimination of tax evasion, the legislator has introduced a new tax institute for the consumer packing of alcohol.
A person who wishes to hold a permit for sale must apply to the CU for authorisation and comply with the legal conditions (business license for a commercial activity; integrity in relation to intentional economic crimes; it has not been withdrawn for ten years for sale; it is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation, a accompanying document is not required when transporting these goods.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove how to acquire consumer packaging of alcohol, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation.
The holder of the permit shall keep a record for each establishment per calendar month the number of pieces of consumer packaging of alcohol received, the number of pieces of consumer packaging of alcohol issued, the stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol on the last day of the month and the registration of the shortage or surplus in the number of consumer liquor packages received and issued.
The holder of the authorisation is obliged to buy or otherwise purchase alcohol in consumer packaging in the course of business only from the person authorized for distribution.
Distributor of consumer alcohol packaging
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and the elimination of tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for distributors of consumer alcohol.
A person intending to hold a distribution authorisation must apply to the ACT for a distribution authorisation.
The applicant must meet the legal conditions (business license for a commercial trade licence; the storage area exceeds 200 m2; the annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol at least €100,000 or a paid-up share capital of at least €100,000; a minimum of 10 employees; has no arrears against the customs office; it does not have arrears on compulsory levies; integrity in relation to intentional economic crimes; it has not been withdrawn for sale for ten years; it is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation, a accompanying document is not required when transporting these goods.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove how to acquire consumer packaging of alcohol, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation.
The holder of the distribution authorisation shall, for each establishment, keep a record for each establishment of the number of received pieces of alcohol consumer packaging, the number of pieces of consumer packaging of alcohol issued, the stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol on the last day of the month and the registration of the shortage or surplus in the number of consumer packs of alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the distribution licence is obliged to buy alcohol in consumer packaging only from another person authorised for distribution.
The person authorised for distribution shall notify the data for each calendar month electronically by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Retailer of fuel
Due to the monitoring of free-tax propellants as well as the elimination of tax evasion, a new type of tax entity has been introduced, namely a fuel seller.
In the territory of the SR there is no special regulation regulating petrol stations.
That is why petrol stations are incorporated in SR's national legislation as fuel retailers.
A person who wishes to sell petrol, diesel or LPG for final consumption in free tax circulation in the tax area is required to apply to the CU for a sale permit before commencing the sale and provide a document proving that the storage facility is certified and equipped with an appropriate verified measuring device allowing the amount of mineral oil when receiving and dispensing, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
If the fuel seller is a tax warehouse operator, an authorised consignee or a registered consignor, the CU will also automatically issue an authorisation to sell fuel to registered persons.
The fuel seller is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep a record of purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG per calendar month and is also obliged to notify the CU of the new supplier (distributor) of the fuel.
The fuel seller is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As they are free-tax propellants, a accompanying document is not required when transporting these goods.
However, when delivering the fuel through the car tank, the distributor, when pumping the propellants, the distributor prints a so-called bottling plant from a measuring device embedded in the car tank.
That document shall include, in addition to the details of the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove how fuel is acquired, which also contains the fuel distributor's number allocated by the tax administrator.
The tax administrator in the territory of the SR in the exercise of tax supervision of mineral oils records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
Above all, it is an effort to avoid roadside checks when transporting roadside, so carriers use secondary roadways, circumventing the toll collection system due to more difficult monitoring of actual transport.
Also carried out are the transport of mineral oils in converted double-bottomed tankers.
Many times it happens that illegal transport is accompanied by a vehicle that carriers report possible mobile patrols to change routes and avoid roadside checks.
There is also mixing of propellants with light fuel oils or waste oils.
Distributor of propellants
Due to the monitoring of free-tax propellants as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity has been introduced, namely a fuel distributor.
A person who intends to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in the tax area in the course of a business activity in the free tax circulation is required to apply to the customs office for a distribution authorisation before commencing the distribution and to provide a document proving that the storage facility is certified and equipped with appropriate verified measuring equipment, as well as a list of suppliers and purchasers.
The fuel distributor is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep separately for each establishment the registration of petrol, diesel or LPG for the calendar month.
The fuel distributor is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from a fuel distributor or from a registered person.
The fuel distributor can only sell in the tax territory to a fuel distributor, registered to the person or consumer of propellants.
However, when delivering fuel through a car tank, the distributor prints, when pumping propellants, the fuel seller, or the consumer of propellants, the so-called bottling from the measuring device embedded in the car tank.
That document shall include, in addition to the details of the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate.
As they are free-tax propellants, a accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel, which also contains the number of the distributor of the fuel, or the registered person, allocated by the tax administrator.
Consumer of fuel
The consumer of fuel has a special status in national legislation.
A person who buys in the tax territory in the free tax circulation for the own consumption of petrol, diesel or LPG and that mineral oil is stored in a storage facility, the volume of which is 15 000 litres or more, is required to notify the customs office of this fact at the latest before the first placement in the storage facility.
Motor consumption shall be included in the register by the customs office.
In addition to legal facts, it is obliged to give the address of the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large shipping companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
Storage equipment shall be verified and equipped with a measuring device enabling the amount of propellants to be measured when receiving and dispensing (condition, measuring rod).
The tank must comply with technical standards.
The fuel consumer must only purchase fuel from a fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As they are free-tax propellants, a accompanying document is not required for transport.
