However, when delivering fuel through a car tank, the distributor prints a so-called bottling from a measuring device embedded in the car tank when pumping propellants to the consumer.
That document shall include, in addition to the details of the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove how fuel is acquired, which also contains the fuel distributor's number allocated by the tax administrator.
The tax administrator in the territory of the SR in the exercise of tax supervision of mineral oils records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer in the business and meets the legal conditions.
Provided that the conditions laid down by law are met, a small independent brewery may apply a reduced rate of tax, i.e. €2,652 per hl/percent volume of actual alcoholic strength.
Annual beer production is limited to up to 200,000 hl of beer.
As it is the production of beer outside the conditional exemption scheme, there is no need for a accompanying document for transport as it is in free tax circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, it is small family businesses that also run restaurants or saloons in which they offer their own-made beer for sale.
Administrative acts in SR
This sub-chapter brings the exercise of the tax oversight of excise tax administrations to selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the Slovak Republic.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative operations (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, due to the implementation of more transport in EMCS.
By contrast, the biggest decline was recorded year-on-year in 2014, by up to 4.3%, due to fewer completed tax inspections and fewer tax returns filed.
That decrease related to legislative changes.
Tax controls
By carrying out the tax audit, the CPO ascertains or examines the facts decisive for the correct determination of the tax.
CÚ staff are shown in the performance of the tax audit by delegation to carry out a tax audit, which includes, among other things, the purpose and subject-matter of the control and the extent of the tax periods checked.
In practice, this means that a controlled tax period can be one month, but also more tax periods.
The extent of the tax periods checked is determined by the CPU.
The tax audit begins with the drafting of the tax inspection notice.
The receipt of the documents will be confirmed by the ACT.
The issued documents are obliged to be returned by the CÚ within 30 days of the completion of the tax audit.
An employee of the CÚ will draw up a report from the tax audit.
If the tax audit finds a difference in the sum that the audited taxpayer was required to pay, to declare or to which he claimed the refund, the CÚ, together with the protocol to the audited taxpayer, will also send a notice of comment on the findings set out in the Protocol.
The tax inspection shall be terminated on the date of receipt of the Protocol.
The deadline for carrying out the tax audit shall be no more than one year from the date of its commencement.
The tax inspection for registered persons and selected registered persons shall be carried out as necessary, but at least once until the day of the expiry of the right to set the tax, which is 5 years.
The FŘ SR issued an internal management act regulating the abovementioned deadlines because of the uniform procedure of the tax administrator in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
Local investigations
A local investigation is the activity of the tax administrator, in which it searches for evidence, examines and ascertains the facts that are needed for tax administration purposes.
A CÚ employee writes an enrollment on the local investigation and submits his copy to the taxpayer.
When conducting a local investigation, the CÚ employee has the right to unlimited access to land, operational buildings, rooms and places including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The clearing of the quantity of alcohol produced shall be determined in the form of a local investigation.
The facts found are the basis for carrying out tax control.
Also in the performance of the local investigation, the CCA is entitled to take samples as well as to secure the item.
The FŘ SR issued an internal management act regulating the exercise of tax supervision and the local investigation for individual items of excise duty due to the unification of the tax administrator's procedures.
Permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1 May 2004, there was also a change in the area of excise duty management.
The need for more efficient spending of state budget funds in managing excise duty on alcohol, improving the business environment in the area and introducing legislative tools for more effective suppression of the grey economy in the area resulted in the adoption of new laws in connection with the administration of excise duties in 2004.
One of the measures brought about by the new legislative change was not only the transfer of the tax administrator in the area of excise tax administration from tax authorities to customs offices, but also the introduction of the need for a tax administrator to be present in a liquor tax warehouse.
In the territory of the Slovak Republic, national legislation exhaustively defines that it is possible to adopt, issue, produce or process alcohol in a tax warehouse only in the presence of an ECA employee.
This does not apply to a tax warehouse which receives, stores or sends alcohol only in consumer packaging of alcohol.
At the same time, the CÚ is obliged to secure employees in the tax warehouse so that the income, dispensing, production or processing of alcohol is not restricted.
The operator of the tax warehouse creates an obligation to safeguard the conditions of the working environment for CÚ employees.
On the basis of a contract concluded with the FŘ SR for the premises provided, the CÚ pays the rental costs to the operator of the tax warehouse on a monthly basis.
In a tax warehouse in the production, processing or storage of alcohol, the production facilities for the storage of alcohol must be adapted in such a way that the quantities of alcohol produced, processed alcohol, alcohol stored, including stocks of alcohol and alcohol contained therein, can be ascertained at any time.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If alcohol is not accepted in a tax warehouse, issued, produced or processed, the customs office may waive the obligation to safeguard the presence of a customs office employee, who is obliged to secure that area through the closure of the customs office.
In practice, however, this option is not used very often, as tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs office employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators make use of the legal option within the meaning of Law No 467/2002 Z., on the production and marketing of alcohol, and use production facilities to produce alcohol in a distillery for cultivation burning and also for the purposes of the distillate distillate distillate distillery, which must be tax warehouse.
The exercise of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses on alcohol is ensured by approximately 250 customs officers.
Issuing vouchers to collect alcohol control stamps
The basic act for the collection of control marks is the sending of an application to the customs office for the allocation of a registration subscription number and issuing a voucher for the collection of alcohol control stamps.
Alcoholic beverage, which is ethyl alcohol, means goods of the Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength of more than 1.2 per cent vol.
The check mark is intended for the labelling of consumer alcohol packaging.
Consumer packaging of alcohol is considered to be closed consumer packaging filled with spirit intended for direct human consumption.
Consumer packaging of the Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 may be entered into free tax circulation in the tax territory only if it is marked with a check mark.
Only the operator of a tax warehouse, the authorised recipient and the consumer packaging importer, who will put it into free tax circulation, may mark the consumer packing.
The check stamp contains, among other things, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numerical character. The identification number contains the registration number (1-6 instead of the numerical character), the volume of alcohol (7.-11. instead of the numerical character) and the volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer pack (12.-14. instead of the numerical character).
Original pattern of control mark on alcohol:
The registration subscription number shall be assigned to each customer by the CU's check marks separately.
Only a check mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of alcohol, the identification number of which corresponds to the volume of consumer packaging, the volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer pack and the customer's control mark.
National legislation at the end of 2014 brought the introduction of a new information system for control stamps.
The aim of the new information system for control marks was to simplify and inform the system of ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of control marks intended for the labelling of consumer alcohol packaging.
Only the operator of the tax warehouse, the authorised recipient, the consumer packaging importer and the consignee (the customer) of alcohol, may mark the consumer packing.
A purchaser of the check marks wishing to take control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office electronically for the issue of the check marks.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of the check stamps is obliged to request their issue, report data arising from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and keep a register of check stamps.
The number of items of control stamps ordered shall not be less than 500 pieces or their multiple.
The tax administrator also communicates with the purchasers of the check stamps through the electronic system of control stamps, in particular when announcing the number of check marks that the purchaser of the check stamps can remove, or when determining the date of receipt of the check stamps by the customer of the check stamps in the printer.
The purchaser of the check marks is obliged to deposit on behalf of the tax administrator funds corresponding to the price of the check marks, which he may withdraw and the amount of which shall be notified to him by the customs office before taking control stamps.
The price of the check mark takes into account the amount of the printer's refunds. However, it does not take into account the level of excise duty.
The checkpoints are entitled to print the state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice.
FŘ SR supervises the handling of control marks and their disposal in the printer.
The FŘ SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when dealing with checkpoints.
FŘ SR secures the sale of control stamps to the supplier of check stamps in the printer.
Remove check marks can only be taken in the printer from the Financial Directorate employee.
Issuing vouchers for the collection of control marks on tobacco products
The purchaser of the check stamp must ask the CPU to allocate the registration number and issue a voucher for the collection of the check stamp.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes can only be put into free tax circulation if it is marked with a checkpoint.
It is only possible to label consumer packs of cigarettes with a checkpoint only in a cigarette company.
The purchaser of the check marks may only be a tax warehouse operator, an authorised recipient or importer of tobacco products who wishes to place tobacco products for free tax circulation in the tax territory.
Only a check mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of cigarettes, the data of which corresponds to the relevant price of cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the pack, the length of cigarettes, the emblem of the tax rate and the registration number.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes can only be sold for final consumption at the price shown on the control mark.
National legislation at the end of 2014 brought the introduction of a new information system for control stamps.
The aim of the new information system for control signs was to simplify and inform the system of ordering, assessment, printing, distribution and use of check marks designed to mark consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A purchaser of the check marks wishing to take control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office electronically for the issue of the check marks.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of the check stamps is obliged to request their issue, report data arising from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and keep a register of check stamps.
The checkpoints are entitled to print the state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice.
FŘ SR supervises the handling of control marks and their disposal in the printer.
The FŘ SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when dealing with checkpoints.
FŘ SR secures the sale of control stamps to the supplier of check stamps in the printer.
Remove check marks can only be taken in the printer from the Financial Directorate employee.
The consumer packing of tobacco with a check mark may be indicated by the operator of the tax warehouse or the importer of tobacco products.
The consumer packing of cigars or cigarillos with a check mark may be indicated by the operator of a tax warehouse, an importer of tobacco products or an authorised recipient.
Only a check mark shall apply to the labelling of consumer packaging of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos, the particulars of which correspond to the emblem for the validity of the rate of excise duty.
It is only possible to mark consumer packs of cigarettes with a check mark in the company that made them.
The number of items of control stamps ordered shall not be less than 500 pieces or their multiple.
Within three working days at the latest, the CÚ shall notify the purchaser of the check marks by electronically the number of check marks he can withdraw, the price of the check stamps and the FŘ SR account number.
The CÚ may reduce the number of items of control stamps ordered if there are circumstances on the basis of which it can reasonably be assumed that there may be a tax infringement.
FŘ SR will determine the date of receipt of the control stamps by the customer of the check stamps, but no later than 10 days.
The date of receipt of the control stamps of the FŘ SR will notify the purchaser of the control stamps through the electronic system of control stamps.
The verification marks are issued exclusively by the Financial Directorate in the printer, but only after the receipt of funds corresponding to their price to the relevant account indicated in the electronic notification of the customs office.
The purchaser of the check stamps is obliged separately in the breakdown for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco to keep a register of check stamps in the electronic system of control stamps.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012, the separation of the ELO and the SPD systems of the Department of Excise Taxation of the SR shall be responsible for securing the exchange of information on the basis of a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the competent authorities of the financial administration.
These include, in particular, requests for screening of entities in the context of the administration of excise duties, requests for information relating to the administration of excise duties, as well as requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications takes place in electronic form under the EMCS.
The following acts are included in administrative cooperation between EU Member States: requests for administrative cooperation (application for verification, request for information on excise tax administration, request for confirmation of registration in SEEDs); response to a request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; control report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Permission and registration
In SR, permanent tax supervision is applied to alcohol tax warehouses, in the Czech Republic this supervision is replaced by the continuous supervision of the tax administrator through a tracking device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are tax warehouse, in Slovakia they are only registered by the tax administrator.
In SR, an institute of a registered consignor is introduced, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In the SR, at a reduced rate of excise duty on alcohol in the case of cultivation burning, it is possible to burn 43 l a.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the reduced rate of alcohol tax can only be applied for 30 litres.
Growing distillery in Slovakia must be licensed not only by the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic, but also from the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, only the Ministry of Agriculture allows growers.
In SR, imports of consumer packaging of alcohol are made, in addition to the tax warehouse operator, by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
The authorisation of the importer shall be subject to registration of the applicant with the excise administrator.
In the Czech Republic, no special permission from the tax administrator is required to import consumer packaging of alcohol.
In SR, the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol is subject to the issuance of a licence from the tax administrator for retailers.
The seller of consumer packaging of alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep a register of, among other things, the purchase and sale.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any permit for the final seller of consumer packaging alcohol, it is sufficient to issue a concession for the sale of alcohol by the Trade Licensing Authority; the final seller does not keep any special records.
In SR, a fuel seller must have a permit from the tax administrator to sell them.
The national legislation in SR does not regulate any special regulation of the petrol station, all activities relating to petrol stations are regulated only in the Excise Tax Act on mineral oils.
In the Czech Republic, petrol stations are regulated by a special law on fuel, but the tax administrator does not issue any permit to sell fuel.
Petrol stations are registered and their list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In SR, it is technically impossible to get a list of petrol stations from the financial management system.
In Slovakia, there has been a significant increase in the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities since 2012.
This increase was due to a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits fell significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of bail for fuel distributors.
Administrative acts
In the SR, substantive legislation provides for the obligation to exercise tax control of selected tax entities.
This issue is further specified by the internal management act issued by the FŘ SR due to the application of the uniform procedure of the tax authorities in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
In the Czech Republic, substantive legislation does not regulate the obligation to exercise tax control, the procedural law stipulates only the possibility of carrying out an inspection at the latest by the time limit for tax assessment.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax inspections carried out and local investigations in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is that the internal management act of the FŘ SR determines in what cases and under what time limits the tax administrator must carry out a tax inspection, while in the Czech Republic the accuracy of the declared amount of excise duty or its refund is verified mainly by local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative tasks in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 as a result of the increase in the number of transport services in the EMCS system and at the same time as a result of the increase in the number of tax returns filed.
In the SR, the number of administrative tasks between 2012 and 2015 had a slightly increasing trend, which was influenced by the increasing number of transport services in EMCS and at the same time the decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the numbers of comparable permits and the registration of tax entities were reflected in the different legislative arrangements.
The number of comparable administrative tasks of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in individual years of the audited period.
In Slovakia, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds compared to the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for approximately the same amount of administrative tasks.
From this it can be concluded that the SR is more focused on carrying out administrative tasks by the tax authorities, e.g. the exercise of physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, emphasis is placed more on remote surveillance, e.g. tracking devices, immediate sending of data via a web interface and risk analysis.
Electronization of administrative tasks
Electronization of administrative tasks in the Czech Republic
Tax returns can be filed via a data box.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced so-called interactive tax return forms, which, however, can no longer be automatically processed.
The data must be further transcribed to the taxpayer's personal tax account.
The benefit is to limit the error rate of the filed tax returns (DAP), which saves the actions of the tax administrator related to the repair proceedings erroneously filed by the DAP.
DGC is working on a new DAP electronic processing application.
In addition, through intelligent forms: filing applications for tax or registration for activities and notifications of changes to data, to make refund claims, to comply with reporting obligations when dealing with special mineral oils, the handling of raw tobacco and the fulfilment of biofuel obligations.
Loading with control tapes is recorded by tax entities in the ORO WebKlient information system, which is available to registered entities for the registration of the tax administrator of the specified data.
Transport of selected products around the Czech Republic under the conditional tax exemption regime must be implemented in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality in the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
Transport of selected products in free tax circulation around the tax territory of the Czech Republic can always be carried out with proof of their taxation, proof of exemption from excise duty, by a decision of the customs office to release the selected products under the customs procedure, a simplified accompanying document or another decision to assess excise duty.
The required content of the data is determined by law.
In order to facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.).
This allows the document form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents sent through the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic to a data warehouse, where each such document is assigned a unique 12-digit identification code (JIK).
JIK is used for the purpose of checking by the customs authorities on the way and prevents repeated transport on the same document.
For the largest operator of a fuel tax warehouse in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of PHM into free tax circulation, CS ČR has on-line access to an electronic registration system into which the entity automatically stores issued tax documents.
CS CR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for recording and monitoring of the transport of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should use 70% of the existing EMCS functional specification.
The advantage will be a user-known environment for both declarants and customs officers.
It will also be linked to a system of global guarantees, to a tax registry or a risk analysis system.
The system should allow for an overview of free circulation traffic between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of written documents without registration and sharing of negotiating numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current process of registering the transport of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen primarily in the abuse of a simplified accompanying document, the reuse of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronization of administrative tasks in SR
When administering excise duties, the SR Financial Administration uses electronic communication in monitoring the movement of goods in the EMCS system under a conditional exemption regime, control stamps, filing tax returns, as well as when registering and registering tax entities.
In 2014, a one-way electronic communication of tax entities with the tax administrator was also introduced, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
As part of electronic communication, the tax entity has access to a personal internet zone, the so-called electronic personal mailbox, which is designed for communication with the financial administration, after entering the access data.
Within this zone, the taxpayer has access to an electronic mailroom through which it submits applications, notices, tax returns and other documents relating to the administration of excise duties.
However, electronic communication through a personal internet zone does not apply to all tax entities.
National legislation defines tax entities that are obliged to communicate with the tax administrator electronically.
These are mainly value added tax payers, a tax adviser representing a tax entity and lawyers representing a tax entity.
The SAO SR also addressed the issue of the scope of computerisation of excise tax administration during the audit.
These were only fully electronic acts, namely tax returns and electronic communications within the ELO.
Apart from the transport carried out in EMCS, there has been an increase in the computerisation of selected comparable administrative tasks, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
A fully electronized processing of the tax return is already in place in the SR, from filing it to registration of the tax liability.
In the Czech Republic, the electronic processing of the tax return is not set up.
In the Czech Republic, the possibility for tax entities to insert mandatory documents for individual transports in free tax circulation is set up for tax entities.
In the future, the reporting of transport in free tax circulation is being prepared in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system.
Evaluation
The system of reporting transport in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax supervision, thus eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid in violation of the legislation.
These can be recommended as good practice.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Due to good practice in the Slovak Republic in the area of electronization of tax returns, the SAO recommends the SAO of the SR and the SAO of the Czech Republic to complete the computerization of the processing of tax returns in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes to the organisational structure and staffing in excise duties
The organizational arrangement of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic has undergone fundamental changes.
Organizational arrangement of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
The customs administration of the Czech Republic since 1 January 2013 consists of the General Directorate of Customs and Customs Authorities, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
The DG is an entity for the entire customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out comprehensive excise tax management since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
CS CR also performs:
(a) control:
In the field of road transport (weighting of trucks, payment of charges for the use of roads, fulfilment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and in matters of international passenger transport),
the management of waste and packaging material,
The safety of imported food,
In the area of consumer protection and the protection of intellectual property rights,
The employment of foreigners,
(b) customs management - it is a comprehensive application of customs legislation, commercially policy measures and formalities on the import and export of goods;
(c) the collection and enforcement of cash benefits imposed by other public authorities within the framework of a shared administration;
(d) the activities of the police authority (referred to customs authorities) in criminal proceedings committed by breaches of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax administrator.
While the scope of competencies (the exercise of control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there are savings in costs from the extent, as the public administration does not have to spend expenses on the position of the control group for each subject of control separately.
At the same time, the administrative burden of the audited persons is reduced by repeated control.
10 The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic continues to exercise the scope to verify the fulfilment of obligations in the record of sales (Section 2(2) of Act No. 112/2016 Coll., on the Registration of Sales) and, as of 1 January 2017, supervision of compliance with the law and conditions of operation of gambling, including the imposition of sanctions (Section 116 of Act No. 186/2016 Coll., on Gambling).
As part of the Modernisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic project, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-tier structure into a two-tier structure with effect from 1 January 2013, while the middle article of the management (customs directorates) was abolished.
The DGs spent around CZK 51 million on the project. CZK (i.e. approx. 2,031,000 €).
CS CR since 1 January 2013 consists of DGCs and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
Customs and their competences are laid down by law, the administration of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial workplaces.
The territorial workplaces are the internal organisational units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is entitled to establish and abolish territorial workplaces and to determine their material scope by decree.
Legislation does not provide for any competence for territorial workplaces; the territorial workplace exercises the competence of the customs office on its behalf.
Organisational structure by 31.12.2012
Organisational structure from 1. 1. 2013
The administration of excise duties until 31.12.2012 was carried out by the DGC, eight CŘ and 58 departments of the CÚ (including branches), i.e. a total of 67 trade unions and departments.
As of 1 January 2016, the administration of the DG and 51 departments in the CÚ and their territorial workplaces, as well as eight departments of the legal department of the DGC and the CÚ services ensuring mobile supervision, i.e. about 60 posts.
The CS CR's costs are most significantly influenced by wage expenditure.
As a result of the reorganization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there were no savings in personnel resources.
The performance of the main processes is ensured by customs officers in service under the law on the service of members of the security forces.
The possibility of reducing the numbers of these members is only very limited in the Czech Republic, because under the provisions of Section 42(1) of Act No 361/2003 Coll., on the service of members of the security forces, they can be dismissed from the service only in cases exhaustively defined.
Reduction of posts due to organisational changes in the Security Corps is not grounds for dismissal and the employer is obliged to provide members with the allocation of adequate service posts within the corps, or to provide posts with another security force (e.g. The Police of the Czech Republic, the Prison Service of the Czech Republic), otherwise they will be reassigned to a reserve for temporarily non-attached, in which members of the security forces are entitled under the law to 80% of the average service income.

Organisational arrangement of excise tax administration in SR
As part of the programme statement for the years 2012 to 2016, the Government of the Slovak Republic set as one of the priorities the completion of the reform of the tax administration through the UNITAS programme, which will secure additional budgetary resources by unifying the collection of taxes, duties and levies and the suppression of tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, bringing about the merger of the Slovak Tax Directorate and the SR Customs Directorate into the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the creation of the financial administration.
The FŘ SR was established as of 1 January 2012 by Act No 333/2011 Z., on the bodies of state administration in the field of taxation, fees and customs, as amended, as a budgetary organisation which is based in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
FŘ SR, CÚ and Criminal Office of the Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No 199/2004 Z. z., Customs Act and amending and supplementing certain laws, as amended, are customs authorities if they carry out tasks under customs regulations.
Within the meaning of Act No 333/2011 Z. z., on government bodies in the field of taxation, fees and customs, as amended, together with the tax authorities, forms the financial administration.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Financial Operations Centre, the Tax Office, the Tax Office for selected tax entities, branches of tax offices, customs offices, branches of customs offices (CÚ tax branch, branch of CÚ combined, branch of CÚ customs) and customs office stations.
The main mission of the FŘ SR is to effectively collect and administer taxes and duties, i.e. also excise taxes, to fulfil the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the FŘ SR is the President of the Financial Administration, who is appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The president of the financial administration is responsible for the activities of the entire financial administration and therefore for the activities of the FŘ SR, which he manages and represents in full.
Organisational structure of FŘ SR from 1. 1.2012 in abbreviated form
Within all customs offices in the territory of the Slovak Republic, the activities and processes in the field of excise duty management ensure, in addition to the branches of customs offices (38 branches) and customs offices (18 stations), the excise tax departments (9 departments) and the legal department (9 departments).

Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Within the organisational structure of the SR financial administration, 74 organisational units with a total of 1,300 employees were involved in the management of excise duties in 2015, in addition to the FŘ SR; these departments manage nearly 48,000 tax entities.
Within the organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, in 2015 the administration of excise duties dealt with about 60 organizational units with a total of 1,011 employees, which manage about 114,000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of individual activities of the administration of excise duties is divided between several personally independent departments.
Their mutual coordination and cooperation is addressed through middle and top management.
In the SR, the pursuit of individual activities (registration, tax return, tax control) in the field of excise tax administration is distributed between the excise tax department and the branch of the customs office, under which the same employees of the tax administrator often deal with that agenda.
Evaluation
In the SR, the number of tax entities is about one-third of the total number of employees in the field of excise tax administration compared to the situation in the Czech Republic; the effect of the higher number of employees on the efficiency of excise tax administration is not clear.
EMCS
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the establishment of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty, the aim of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to enable real-time information on transport and to carry out prescribed controls, to simplify the movement of intra-Community goods under suspension of excise duty.
When implementing the system, Member States should have allowed economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of that EP and Council Decision allows national specifications, national databases forming part of the system and those technical or software which the Member State deems necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration are included in the EMCS.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionality of EMCS
In the Czech Republic, EMCS was preceded by a system of registration of selected products (EVV), which was operated from May 2004 to the end of March 2010.
EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented with European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
In the Czech Republic, the so-called customs module and the declarant module were introduced.
The tariff module contains a number of national functionalities.
Beyond the Community system, in the EMCS system, shipments are monitored in the EMCS system under a conditional tax exemption scheme initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The system ensures, after approval, a notification of receipt intended for the authorised recipient for the one-time receipt of the information to the tax registry with subsequent invalidation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from the ELO including sending answers with an attachment in any format and securing translations.
It is also possible to receive a report on manual termination of exports in the ECS (only the referral of an automatically created message is implemented in the EU).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS will not allow the approval of an e-AD or notice of admission without the reaction of the competent customs authority to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The declarant module is available for tax entities free of charge, it has the form of a web application to which the user logs in with a user name and password (coordinates) that are allocated to him after registration with CS ČR.
Each action against the EMCS customs module shall be provided with a valid electronic signature in the EMCS Treaty module.
The Declarant module allows tax entities to directly register data on commenced and terminated services under the suspensive exemption regime, so that tax entities do not have to spend funds on the acquisition of the scheme.
The national functionalities of the declarant module make it possible to retrieve and store data off-line (saves time for frequently used data), fill in recipient data based on SEED ID control, and require mandatory completion of data that is optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows for every shipment sent from the Czech Republic in real time to block the provision of excise duty at the appropriate amount of taxable supply until the end of the transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by EMCS.
Without sufficient collateral quantity, it is not possible to send the e-AD proposal for approval to the CA of dispatch from the declarant module EMCS.
Each warranty has a unique number and contains ARC transport (including the amount of blocked collateral) for which it was used.
The taxpayer can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS Treaty module, where it sees the current amount of blocked and unblocked excise tax guarantees.
Expenditure on the deployment and use of EMCS
The development of EMCS was carried out on the basis of eight performance contracts from 2006 to 2017 totalling CZK 46,791,924.60 (i.e. 1,761,412.56 €) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. £1,640,401.10) excluding VAT from 2006 to the end of 2015.
In the audited period, expenses of CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (i.e. € 547,438.99) were spent on the EMCS upgrade.
The amount spent on EMCS upgrades in the audited period and converted into one transport injected into EMCS averages CZK 16.49 (i.e. €0.62), excluding national transport, this expenditure per transport between the Czech Republic and EU Member States is CZK 24.40 (i.e. €0.92).
The technical support for EMCS was implemented on the basis of four performance contracts from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, the total amount of technical support of CZK 7,499,6775 (i.e. €281,389,77), including value added tax, had been invoiced.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 on a single transport injected into EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (i.e. €0.23).
The development and technical support invoices related to the national solution and led to the development of the EVV application, which the DGC already operated before EMCS itself.
Invoices were paid under programme funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the supply of services as well as other applications provided by the supplier for Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under a conditional exemption scheme.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document - SAD, which was used before the system took effect, thus ensuring better control and traffic management.
It has been in place in the SR since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented with the requirements of EU legislation.
For each transport, a unique reference code is generated, so-called
ARC code under which this transport can be tracked online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionality of EMCS
EMCS ensures the receipt and dispatch of excise goods by only such tax entities that are authorised to use EMCS, which greatly reduces the risk of tax evasion.
The biggest development of functionalities occurred in 2011 when EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the deployment and use of EMCS
The introduction of EMCS was implemented as another module of SysNeD application equipment and therefore it is not possible to accurately determine the cost of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
EMCS's goal was to replace the system based on administration of transport in paper form.
The benefit of the EMCS is a comprehensive overview of transport between individual Member States within the EU from the announcement of the start of transport to its termination, while the reduction in administrative costs for tax administrators and tax entities for the processing, transmission and archiving of documents is significant.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, a national functionality was introduced into the EMCS system allowing traffic monitoring in a conditional system between two locations in the Czech Republic or Slovakia.
In addition, automatic functionality of online monitoring and ensuring a guarantee for excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
There is also a national functionality that monitors the riskiness of the taxpayer or transport, with the subsequent mandatory response of the tax administrator.
The Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic record a comparable number of intra-EU transport in the EMCS system.
However, spending in the SR on upgrading this system was €744,310,01 higher than in the Czech Republic between 2012 and 2015.
The SAO of the SR received data from the FŘ SR on the upgrade of EMCS only for the period from 2011, although this system was introduced and operated earlier.
Nevertheless, the expenditure incurred on the EMCS upgrade in the SR was €188,134.44 higher than the expenditure for the deployment and upgrade of EMCS for about ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
For the audited period, the volume of expenditure related to the upgrade of EMCS in the SR per transport 2.3 times exceeds the expenditure of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation of the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR met the objectives.
Both audit institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the excise tax management system in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in both tax systems that affect the efficiency of excise administration.
During parallel controls, examples of good practice have been identified that could contribute to curbing tax fraud, their importance with rising tax rates will increase.
Procedures have also been identified to reduce the costs of administering excise duties.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons when mutually coordinated due diligence is not carried out with the tax administrator.
In this, the role of supreme audit institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel control of the value added tax administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The 1977 Lima Declaration underlines that the highest audit institutions (SAI) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The Declaration calls for tax revenues to be checked to the greatest extent possible.
The Organisation of the European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers taxation to be one of the most important parts of public revenue.
The VI. EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of public revenue carried out by the SAI.
A major step towards optimising SAI control activities is the development of a specific strategy for auditing public revenues.
This applies in particular to taxes as the bulkiest source of public revenue, which is most prone to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAI may be unable to carry out control activities without cooperation with another state's SAI.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in the income of many countries.
To combat this offence, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
The SAI carrying out checks in this area must be willing to engage in closer cooperation with each other.
It was at the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn that the idea of carrying out an inspection of the Value Added Tax Administration (VAT) and the VIES system in the framework of the cooperation of the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof, arose.
Careful preparation followed, with both sides first having to familiarize themselves with the legal environment and procedures for managing VAT in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Based on the analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was carried out which was included in the control programme.
Achieving an effective and efficient VAT administration is a long-standing problem, and individual states (especially the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We believe that the results of our control can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrators, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the international information exchange system.
Report on the results of parallel checks on the management of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 – 2005 – 1215
Subject-matter of the inspection:
(CZ) Value Added Tax Administration after the Czech Republic joined the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the control action in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the management of value added tax after the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (EU) linked to the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the application of the right to a value added tax exemption for intracomonity delivery.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system of control of intracomonarian value added tax, with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the aforementioned regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
System of exchange of information on value added tax Audit actions were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the German Bundesrechnungshof (BRH) in mutual cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two audit institutions on 8 June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected commercial transactions carried out between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as the "CFN"), the use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of VAT management systems of both countries.
The joint final report on the results of the control actions was prepared within the meaning of European Directive 31 for the implementation of INTOSAI audit standards.
The audited period was the period from 1 May 2004 to 31.12.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
Parallel control in the area of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAI.
Outside the main point, exchanges of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 – covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are closely linked to the main point.
In addition, the inspection included the legal situation in the area of international bus passenger transport and a comparison of some statistical data.
Comparing the VAT systems of the two countries found differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While entrepreneurs are registered in Germany regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among other things) is for registering exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, only one tax identification number is allocated to payers, which they also use in intra-community transactions.
In Germany, a VAT number is allocated to payers when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intracomonality transactions, he must apply for the allocation of a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different methods of registration cause problems, conditions should be levelled across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International bus passenger transport.
In the Czech Republic, the international bus transport of persons is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport taking place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC, on the common system of VAT (see 4.2)
3) VAT tax returns.
While in the Czech Republic, payers file VAT returns only for individual tax periods (month or quarter), in Germany, payers are obliged to file so-called preliminary VAT tax returns (monthly or quarterly) and have to file an annual VAT return at the end of the calendar year.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to file preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to file VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic, payers submit recapitulative statements to the tax authorities, in Germany, payers submit recapitulative reports to the CLO.
The tax authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have data from the recapitulative reports available immediately after their submission.
The German tax authorities have information from the recapitulative reports only after they have been processed at the CLO.
Combating VAT fraud requires updated information on intracomonality transactions to be available as soon as possible.
The monthly submission of recapitulative statements would shorten the time difference between the date of the transaction and the update of the VIES data.
This would in turn allow for early verification of taxation in the Member State of the acquirer (see 4.4).
Which, but would require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for submitting a recapitulative statement.
5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech CLO monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for received requests for information.
The German CLO does not track the past time.
As a result, the German tax administration handled a significantly lower percentage of the applications received within the deadline.
Because of these problems, BRH recommended the German CLO to carry out permanent warnings (see 4.6).
6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States is developing its own risk management system (risk management system, hereinafter referred to as "RMS"), which has its strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5.).
As part of the cooperation, the two SAI examined selected cases of intracomonality transactions carried out between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together, using the legislation for the CLO, thirty-one cases of commercial transactions have been examined where there were doubts about their implementation or suspicion of VAT evasion.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained in the form of international cooperation and assessed the VAT liability of the payers.
In these cases, the payers either improperly claimed a VAT exemption claim or did not declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used because of the various legal provisions in the two Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases have been found where payers erroneously reported business transactions in recapitulative statements.
As a result, the figures in the VIES were incorrect and tax administrations had to examine these cases (see 6.).
The course of the inspection
The course of the control action in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and March 2007 by the Department II – the revenue department of the state budget and the territorial unions of Central Bohemia, northwest Bohemia, southern Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were: Ministry of Finance (hereinafter referred to as "MF") and 10 Financial Offices – Financial Office in Humpolec, Financial Office in Jihlava, Financial Office in Kadani, Financial Office in Liberec, Financial Office in Nymburk, Financial Office in Otrokovice, Financial Office for Prague 1, Financial Office for Prague 4 Financial Office in Sokolov and Financial Office in Třinec.
The audit conclusion of this audit was approved by the SAO College on 23 April 2007.
The course of the control action in Germany
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and February 2007 by the Audit Group on Indirect Taxation and Personnel Designated Regional Audit Offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
The audit was part of the 2006 control plan and was therefore notified to the Federal I.F. in 2006.
After the testing phase, the inspection started in the fourth quarter of 2006.
According to the cases selected by BRH and later elected SAO, BRH had to notify a review of a number of federal states.
In addition to interviews at the Federal I.F. and CLO, the check was carried out in the following federal states:
Baden-Württemberg, Bavaria, Hamburg, Lower Saxony, North Rhine-Westphalia, Rhineland-Palatinate and Saxony.
Included were the tax files of the following tax authorities:
Bruchsal, Ettlingen, Freudenstadt, Karlsruhe-Stadt, Leonberg, Mühlacker, Singen, Tuttlingen, Cham, Fürstenfeldbruck, Munich - FÚ for Corporations/ Legal Entities (München-Körperschaften), Munich II, IV and Munich V, Starnberg, Hamburg-Altona, Hamburg-Hann-Hansa, Hamburg-Hordn-Mitte (Hamburg-Mitte), Hamburg-North (Hamburg-Nord) and Hamburg for large enterprises (Hamburg-Genburg),
In addition, negotiations were held with the Augsburg-City Financial Office (Augsburg-Stadt), Aurich, Düsseldorf-old city (Düsseldorf-Altstadt), Eisleben, Kelheim and Verden.
A report on the control findings was submitted to the I.M.F. in May 2007.
Cooperation between the two audit institutions
As part of the preparation of parallel control actions, several meetings of representatives of the two audit institutions took place in the period prior to their start.
Participants in these meetings became acquainted with the organisation of tax administrations, the legislative regulation of VAT issues and the VAT management system in both countries.
At the meeting, which took place in May 2006, the topics of the testing phase were agreed.
The results of the test phase were evaluated at the next joint meeting in August 2006.
As part of this negotiation, a timetable for the next progress of the work was agreed and the following topics of parallel checks were established:
1. Registration of VAT payers.
2.
International bus transport of persons - legislation in the Czech Republic and Germany.
3. International exchange of information, in particular the procedure of tax administrators in handling requests for information and examining selected problem cases listed in requests for information and spontaneous information transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany.
4. VAT tax returns.
5.
Summary reports.
6.
Statistics on the delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
7. Risk management in the area of VAT.
On the joint audit day of the SAO and BRH, which took place in December 2006, the two sides became acquainted with each other with the course of the audit in the Czech Republic and Germany and discussed the results of parallel control actions so far.
The report on the results of parallel inspections of the VAT administration between the Czech Republic and Germany was drawn up at a working meeting in July 2007.
4. Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payers who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
According to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Tax and Fees (hereinafter referred to as Law No. 337/1992 Coll."), the taxpayer, the tax payer and the legal successor to a natural or legal person defined by law as a tax entity is understood.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421,865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
On 1 December 2005, there was an increase in the number of tax entities registered for VAT to 457 590.
A taxable person who has its registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months, becomes a payer from the 1st day of the third month following the month in which it exceeded the registration limit (Section 94(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter referred to as "Law No 235/2004 Coll.).
The registration application is required by this person within 15 days of the end of the month in which they exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow a taxable person to be registered so-called retrospectively in cases where the reason for registration is to exceed the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with a right to deduct may become a tax payer, even if he does not exceed a turnover of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575), if he fulfils one of the other conditions set out in Act No 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not comply with any of the conditions laid down by law can apply for registration for VAT voluntarily.
Delivery of the application for registration to the locally competent tax administrator initiates registration proceedings under Act No. 337/1992 Coll.
The voluntary VAT payer on the VAT registration application shall also indicate the date on which he applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator shall examine the data communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the completed application for registration with all annexes.
If he has doubts about the data, he shall invite the taxpayer to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After verifying that the tax authority fulfils the conditions for registration, the tax authority issues a decision in the form of a certificate that the taxpayer is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as the Tax Code).
On the certificate, the tax administrator shall indicate the date of the VAT registration and the periodicity of the VAT registration period.
The tax period is the calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year did not reach CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335 750).
If the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335 750), the tax period is the calendar month.
The payer, whose turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150), is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax year and will notify the tax administrator of this change.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the VAT number in the registration certificate is always of a constitutive nature and the taxpayer is obliged to state them in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law so provides (e.g. Act No. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The VAT number contains the code "CZ" and the common part, which is made up of the general identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is a birth number, or another general identifier, if a special law so provides, and an identification number for a legal person (Paragraph 33(12) of Act No 337/1992 Coll.).
If the taxpayer has not complied with its registration obligation even at the request of the tax administrator, it shall be registered immediately by the tax administrator concerned.
The registration procedure results in the issue of the Ex officio registration certificate, which is delivered to the taxpayer.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that obtained a business license is allocated to the Tax Code at the time of its first registration for any tax.
The same VAT is used by the tax entity even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No 235/2004 Coll., which is effective from 1 January 2005, the tax administrator may, in the event of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, impose on the taxable person compensation of up to 10% of the sum of the proceeds or income for taxable transactions that this person has improperly carried out without tax for the period from the date to which he should have been a registered payer by law until the date on which he or she became a registered payer on the basis of a decision of the tax administrator (Article 98(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.).
Payment of the amount thus determined is considered to be a tax payment (Section 98(3) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it is not a penalty.
The abolition of registration of the VAT payer subject to compliance with the conditions laid down by law is possible for two reasons:
1)
Abolition of registration at the request of the payer, mainly in respect of the amount of turnover that does not reach the registration limit (Section 106(1) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer is entitled to apply for the withdrawal of the registration at the earliest after 1 year of the effective date indicated on the registration certificate.
2) Revocation of registration "ex officio" (Section 106(7) of Act No 235/2004 Coll.), unless: (a) the payer did not take place without notice of reason to the tax administrator for 12 consecutive months of performance, (b) the payer fails to comply with his obligations under Act No 235/2004 Coll., (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Payers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who performs a transaction with a place of performance in the Czech Republic and is a person liable to declare and pay tax on this transaction pursuant to Section 108 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. (the so-called "unfounded payer") becomes a payer on the date of this transaction.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration to the Financial Office for Prague 1 at the latest on the date of implementation of the performance.
It is required to indicate in the registration application all the TINs allocated to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If a "unsettled" payer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic, the Financial Office for Prague 1 registers it retroactively, because under Act No 235/2004 Coll., the taxpayer became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic.
During retroactive registration, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires evidence from tax entities that the performance has been carried out (factures or explanatory letters).
If a "unsettled" tax entity applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable performance is carried out, then the Financial Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts for the performance to take place.
As of 31 December 2004, 473 "unsettled" payers were registered at the Financial Office for Prague 1, 2004, of which 124 payers from Germany, and as of 31 December 2005 951 "unsettled" payers were registered, including 233 payers from Germany.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 106(9) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the registration of an "unsettled" payer on 31 January of the following calendar year, unless the payer incurred any obligation to declare and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
The SAO's audit found that if a "unsettled" payer submits a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, i.e. in accordance with the statutory regulation within the deadline for filing the tax return, the tax office often does not have it available on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant for the possibility of deregistration of registration to the tax office are known later than 31 January, it is no longer possible in the Czech Republic in a given calendar year to cancel the VAT registration of the "non-sustodied" payer.
Registration of payers in Germany
In view of the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (Sections 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, ‘the AO’), anyone carrying out a business activity is obliged to inform the municipal/municipal authority or the relevant tax office.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after starting a business.
This information is processed by the Municipal/Municipal Office for the Financial Conduct Authority.
If the IRS finds out an undertaking that has started but has not registered, the competent tax authority may register that payer ex officio – even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both tax residents and non-resident tax residents in Germany are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in Paragraph 2 of the German VAT Act (UStG).
This obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover they make.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
For entrepreneurs permanently living abroad, there are special tax offices.
For example, for those who have their registered office in the Czech Republic, the relevant Financial Office is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Financial Office; as of 1 March 2006, a total of 1,050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register so-called semi-dependent independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
As the work permits of staff from the ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
Those undertakings do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs set out in Paragraph 2 of the UStG because they are usually dependent on a single employer who determines their working time and the way in which they perform their work.
For the purpose of registration, the entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire from the competent tax office in which he must provide information on the company and the activities he carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax authorities or by services with a general focus responsible for assessing taxpayers.
This form carries out a risk assessment of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions follows certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the relevant tax office, the following three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the tax office, the other five (or four) are to distinguish payers, the last being always the check digit.
If an entrepreneur intends to participate in an intracomonality trade, he or she needs an VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an exempt intracomonality supply.
CLO assigns a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and if he has a VAT tax number.
CLO assigns VAT ID to entrepreneurs automatically when payers indicate intracomonarian supplies in their VAT return.
The structure of the VAT ID is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
Registration of an entrepreneur may be revoked: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business), after carrying out all administrative work (assessment for all marketing years) and 2. if the tax administration realises that he is no longer engaged in a business activity.
The validity of the VAT identification number is normally linked to the validity of the VAT tax number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are required to inform the CLO of the abolition of the tax number so that the CLO can terminate the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (Section 19 (1) of the UStG), tax residents in Germany are not obliged to pay VAT in the case 1. that the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2 in the following year is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000.
So-called small entrepreneurs ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice other entrepreneurs VAT and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not obliged to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and have to file an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that he will not apply the provisions of Paragraph 19(1) of the UStG.
This confession is binding on him for the next five years.
An entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For tax non-residents, there is the possibility to appoint a tax representative (Section 22a of the UStG).
A prerequisite is that they carry out exclusively tax-exempt commercial transactions and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
The function of the tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur, who thus does not have to register for VAT.
The invoices must include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While entrepreneurs are registered in Germany regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among other things) is for registering exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
If the taxpayer does not exceed the specified limit in the Czech Republic, he has the option to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration procedure is standardised in Germany, but as a result of different organisational models in federal states, there may be differences.
In the Czech Republic, the payer is allocated a VAT number at the time of his first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he also uses the same VAT number in intracomonality transactions.
In Germany, a VAT number is allocated to the payer when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intracomonality transactions, he must apply for the allocation of a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and BRH have discovered, the German two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, as in the Czech Republic, which allocates a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration to intracomonality transactions.
On the other hand, the two-tier system allows retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax office of their business.
This retroactive registration allows for a correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax year, in particular an accurate estimate of the VAT liability.
As different methods of registration cause problems, conditions should be levelled across the EU.
The German parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as the Tax Code).
The Federal Tax Office will allocate the Tax Code at the birth of a natural person.
This VAT number will be valid throughout the life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax office will apply for an economic VAT number to be used as a VAT ID.
In the future there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of VAT ID.
Work on the introduction of the IT device to manage the TIN has not yet been completed.
International bus transport of persons
Legislation in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., with effect from 1 May 2004, the transport of persons between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with a right to deduct.
Such carriage is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by taxable entrepreneurs in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
The return transport is considered to be a separate transport.
If "unsettled" tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out other economic activities in addition to international bus passenger transport, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International passenger transport in the Czech Republic was exempt from VAT on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V. 5(1)(b), which states:
