‘For the purposes of Article 28(3)(b) of Directive 77/388/EEC, the Czech Republic may continue to exempt value added tax on international passenger transport in accordance with point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Article 28(4) of the Directive is met or while the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier.’
Description of the legislation in Germany
Pursuant to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in Paragraph 3b(1) of the German VAT Act, the place of supply of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) is the route (i.e. the place where the transport takes place.
The German tax system therefore makes no distinction between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route that takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable provision of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also makes no distinction between tax residents and non-residents.
If a non-resident taxpayer transports passengers through Germany, then the part of the route that takes place in Germany also represents a taxable provision of transport.
Before carrying out its services in Germany, the non-resident must notify his intention to provide passenger transport to the competent tax office.
The tax office shall register this non-resident tax (cf. 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach specified in the taxpayer's notice.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare his taxable transport provision in the German VAT return.
As of 1 March 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Financial Office registered 741 Czech payers who did business in passenger transport.
Where the carriage of passengers is provided to a tax resident who is a taxable person for VAT, the non-resident does not have to pay VAT himself to the tax office.
Instead, the entity required to pay VAT to the tax authority and the invoiced net amount to the non-resident taxpayer is a resident of the recipient of the services; this process is known as the ‘reverse charge’ and is in accordance with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
In addition to the notification of the non-resident tax and his VAT return, the German tax authorities have several means to assess the accuracy of the declared taxable provision of passenger transport.
Customs mobile control groups carry out an audit of the certificate of buses authorised (licenses) for foreign transport, which are used to transport passengers through Germany.
After each audit, mobile control groups send a control report to the relevant tax authority.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to require the bus driver to pay VAT before continuing to carry out further transport.
A non-resident tax may deduct the VAT thus paid on the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the IRS has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may notify the intention to carry out an audit that must be carried out at the Office of the Tax Office or may use the administrative cooperation funds referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if a non-resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT assessed in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may apply for administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If a VAT return is to be reviewed or the non-resident's obligations are to be carried out, BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labour-intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid as taxable the provision of passenger transport.
In particular, the audit of the accounts of the non-resident gives rise to disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration must carry out an audit of foreign accounting, which means not only the need to know a foreign language, but also a familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to take more time than an audit of a tax resident, but this audit is limited to the provision of passenger transport carried out in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident does not only have to accept the right to carry out the control of his national tax administration, but also the right to carry out an audit by other Member States in which he transports passengers.
In addition, in each Member State in which only one provision of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all the tax obligations applicable to it in those Member States, in all languages and on all tax forms of those Member States.
Actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore entails disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in the two countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, the transport of persons between individual EU Member States, or between Member States and third countries, is exempt from VAT with a right to deduct tax on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory constitutes a taxable supply.
Where such transport is provided by a non-established payer in Germany for the first time, it is obliged to notify the competent tax authority in advance of the transport.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to declare in Germany the taxable provision of part of the transport in the tax return.
Implementation of the law is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Financial Office are in passenger transport business.
Compared to the effort, the tax revenue, if it is realized, is rather low.
Member States collecting VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT shall be subject to time consuming obligations without a financially sensitive result.
In order to avoid disproportionate costs to impose VAT, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the state where the transport begins or where the provider is located.
Such taxation would require adaptation of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
Tax returns for VAT
Submission and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to file a VAT return on the form prescribed by the I.M.F. within 25 days of the end of the tax period, even if he has not been subject to a tax liability, unless the law provides otherwise.
The tax liability itself is due within the period for filing the VAT tax return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the import of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., for which the tax is determined by customs regulations.
If, as a result of the assessment of excess deduction, a refundable overpayment arises, the payer shall return without request within 30 days of the assessment of the excess deduction.
The deadline is not applied in cases where the tax administrator initiates tax proceedings relating to the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73(11) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., the right to deduct can be exercised in a regular VAT return at the latest for the last tax year in which the right to deduct could be exercised.
At the end of that period, the right to deduct may be further exercised within 3 years of the end of the tax year in which the right to deduct could have been exercised first.
However, this is only possible in the form of filing an additional VAT return.
The amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, allows the filing of an additional VAT return only for the period when the right to deduct could be exercised for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return if (a) the sum of the corrections increases the tax liability, (b) he makes a correction that does not change the last known tax liability, but only the data by the tax entity previously claimed, (c) he corrects the rate and the amount of tax according to Section 49 of Act No 235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit an additional VAT return if the sum of the corrections reduces the tax liability.
An additional VAT return is required to be submitted by the payer by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The submission of a VAT return in electronic form can be made both via the Internet network or on a technical data medium.
Submissions over the Internet can be made as a submission with a data message bearing a guaranteed electronic signature or as a submission with a data message not covered by a guaranteed electronic signature.
In the case of submission with a data message not covered by a guaranteed electronic signature, submission is still required in written form, i.e. delivery of the computer assembly to the tax administrator (e-print).
The VAT tax return contains separate lines concerning the values of intracomonant supplies/equipment.
The values of the acquisition of services are reported on the special lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of initial automated control within the ADIS system.
The values of the supply of goods to other Member States to taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with those set out in the recapitulative statements submitted by Czech payers.
The values of the acquisition of goods from other Member States from taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with those obtained through the VIES system from the recapitulative statements of payers from other EU Member States.
The tax office is undergoing a test of the credibility of VAT returns under the ADIS system.
This test takes place automatically, as tax returns for VAT cannot be assessed without a test.
The credibility test includes the calculation of the credibility criteria and the evaluation of risky types of VAT returns.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 37(1) of Act No 337/1992 Coll., the Financial Conduct Authority may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2 000 000 (EUR 67,150) within the prescribed period.
An automated tax information system used by the FC to provide technical support for tax administration.
The SAO's audit found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility of imposing a fine on payers for not filing a VAT tax return.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are obliged to submit preliminary VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not obliged to pay VAT must submit an annual tax return.
In general, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which VAT is incurred (section 18(2) of the UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the previous calendar year or, in the case of a newly established undertaking, the relevant entrepreneur is obliged to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day in the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to file a monthly VAT return if a tax has been refunded last year which exceeded EUR 6 136 (Art.18(2)a of the UStG).
VAT returns do not need to be filed if the amount of annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT tax liability must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax period in which the VAT was incurred.
The refund of the tax may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FC.
There are no deadlines (under the law) for processing tax returns and the refund of excess VAT deduction.
For the purpose of a timely refund, it is possible to offer to secure the amount to be recovered.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT Act provides for the possibility to extend this period (Section 18(6) of the UStG).
Such an extension should be requested separately.
It makes it possible to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT liability a month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of a monthly return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT liability.
Whenever an error is found, the entrepreneur must file a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered with the tax office, the entrepreneur cannot correct the erroneous preliminary tax return, but only the annual VAT tax return.
Correction of the annual VAT return to or against the payer is possible during the following 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are obliged to file preliminary VAT returns electronically.
Financial authorities may apply exemptions from this rule in order to avoid undue harshness.
Submission of an annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the Internet, either with or without certification.
If it is carried out without certification, the payer must file a return once more on paper with personal signatures.
In the event that the payer does not file a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a gross estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In the event of late submission, a penalty payment may be imposed on the payer (maximum of 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000).
BRH found during a previous check that tax authorities often do not measure this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
Therefore, the standard fine does not meet its objective of shortening the average delay, especially when submitting an annual VAT return.
The VAT tax return contains separate lines relating to the values of intracomonant supplies/management of goods.
The values of the acquisition of services are reported on the special lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be recognised on a separate line of tax return/to VAT.
In the case of VAT returns presented in paper form, a copy must be made either by means of a scanner or by staff specifically authorised to do so.
The data from the VAT returns submitted electronically is immediately available to the IRS employee.
Once all the data is entered into the system, the RMS staff will pass them through and make a selection of cases that meet certain criteria.
The VAT return collected must be checked by a Financial Officer on the basis of a control report drawn up by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration must grossly estimate the amount of VAT that the taxpayer has to pay, the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers file VAT returns within 25 days after the end of the tax year.
The tax period, depending on the payer's turnover, is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month.
In Germany, payers file advance VAT returns, depending on the tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days after the end of the calendar quarter or month.
Until 31 May of the following year, payers are required to file annual tax returns.
The obligation to file an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ on the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly preliminary) tax returns by filing a single annual VAT return;
– if the payer corrects the admitted intracomonality transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period for which the recapitulative statement is made;
– the federal states do not usually compare the VIES data on intracomonality acquisitions of German payers prior to the processing of the annual VAT return.
In accordance with the registration (see 4.1.3), German payers are obliged to file an annual VAT return irrespective of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German financial authority to examine the maximum turnover limit for small entrepreneurs.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare the annual VAT return with direct tax returns and the final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are only able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover from the filed income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to file VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to file tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the Czech Republic
The summary report (hereinafter referred to as "SH") is filed under the provisions of Section 102 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. of the payer who made the supply of goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State.
Data on the value of goods delivered are always shown in the Czech currency by individual tax entity, indicating their VAT ID, under which they are registered in their country.
Data on the services provided are not included in SH.
SH is served by payers with both monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days of its completion to the locally competent tax authority.
Correction of erroneous data is made in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the error detection date.
The erroneous data referred to in SH shall always be replaced by the data provided in the subsequent SH.
Like tax returns, the payers can file SH in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not administer SH or the subsequent SH and should have filed them under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator will invite him to submit it and at the same time instructs him about the consequences in the event of the non-submission of SH or the subsequent SH, i.e. the fact that the tax administrator is entitled to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for failing to comply with the obligations of a non-monetary nature.
The SAO's audit found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility of imposing a fine on payers for failing to comply with their legal obligations.
In the case of the administration of SHs in particular, tax entities are not sufficiently motivated to fulfil their obligations because the non-submission of SH does not affect VAT liability.
According to Section 102(5) of Act No 235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator is obliged to examine the data in SH, or in the subsequent SH, to remove any ambiguities and use the data to determine the tax liability.
In the event of non-compliance with data in SH and data in the relevant (payers with the monthly tax period) or the relevant (substitutes with a quarterly tax period) VAT return, the tax administrator should verify the accuracy of the tax liability declared in the VAT return.
Incorrect data in SH will be removed by the tax entity by filing a subsequent SH itself, or may be invited to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct the details of the supply of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system where:
– the payer does not demonstrate the information given in SH (or subsequent SH), correcting it by administering a subsequent SH,
– the tax authority has demonstrated that the data provided by the payer in SH or the subsequent SH are not true.
By entering a correction without filing a subsequent SH by the payer, the tax administrator does not replace the filing of the taxpayer, only adjusting the data in the VIES database so that they are up to date, complete and accurate.
Data from SH shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
They can be sent and accepted only by the national authority of the financial administration, designed to cooperate with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic, the International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (CLO) fulfils this function.
O_MCTL is an automatic message that the CLO receives from other Member States.
It contains all the erroneous VAT ID specified in the SH lines sent.
If a faulty VAT ID is used in one of the transmitted common SH or subsequent SH rows, a record is made to the error VAT ID table.
The table contains so-called "Notice of doubt on VAT ID."
The tax administrator will examine the data and record the result of the verification into the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is obliged to declare VAT and state the value of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of goods procured declared by the Czech payer in their VAT return and in the value of the goods delivered, as stated by the payers of other Member States in their SH, are sent from the CLO to the tax office for verification.
Tax administrators are obliged to investigate the irregularities.
There can be three situations:
a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant lines of VAT return tax returns is lower than the value of the supply declared by EU payers.
In this case, the tax administrator will check the accuracy of the data.
(b) The difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself submits an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administrator whether, despite this fact, it will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
(c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by the Czech tax payer in the relevant lines of the VAT return tax return is higher than the value of the goods delivered declared to EU payers.
Here, too, it is at the discretion of the controller to verify the accuracy of the data.
After examining the difference and clarifying the causes of its creation, the tax administrator shall bring the result of the verification to ADIS.
The results of the screening are transmitted back to the CLO.
The number of cases sent from the CLO to the tax authorities for verification for individual quarter of 2005 is shown in Graph 1 (source note: MF).
The above-mentioned Graph 1 demonstrates that the number of cases transmitted from the CLO to the tax authorities fell for each quarter of 2005.
A significant decrease in the number occurred for the 4th quarter of 2005. The CLO has raised the minimum financial limit, including with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between VAT return data and EU data may not always be due to an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error resulting from the fact that in individual EU Member States some types of transactions can be reported to SH in a different way.
The most common reasons for irregularities in the values of the reported transactions found at the audited tax authorities are shown in Table 1.
Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in Germany
Entrepreneurs who make intracomonality deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or participate in tripartite transactions shall be required to lodge once a quarter of the year to the SH, which indicate intracomonality delivery by beneficiary (section 18a(1) of the UStG).
SH must be submitted by the 10th day of the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If an extension of this period is allowed in the case of provisional VAT returns, this also applies to SH.
SH must be supplied to the CLO.
As of 1 January 2007, they must be submitted electronically.
Exemptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue harshness.
In cases where taxpayers become aware that erroneous data are provided in SH, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not lodge an SH, the CLO will initiate proceedings to enforce the submission of such a report.
Part of this procedure is: – the first reminder – the second reminder associated with the threat of a fine/penalty, and – the assessment of the penalty payment.
Although the German Tax Code allows a fine of up to EUR 25 000 (Section 329 AO), the CLO assesses fines in three steps, in amounts of EUR 125, 250 and EUR 500.
In addition, Paragraph 26a(1)(5) of the UStG provides that payers act illegally if they deliberately or negligently do not administer the SH properly, submit them incomplete, do not administer them on time or if they do not correct or correct at all late SH.
This offence can be punished with a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intracomonality deliveries cannot be entered into VIES by the Financial Conduct Authority because the processing of SH is the sole task of CLO.
The SH data is stored only in the CLO system.
Therefore, data from SH are visually available only after processing them to CLO.
The time limits for the processing of SH are set out in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The data from SH must be stored within three months following the relevant calendar quarter.
In the event of incorrect VAT ID in SH German payers, CLO will receive O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
CLO contacts a particular entrepreneur and asks him for the correct information.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case shall be referred to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
BRH discovered during the inspection that most entrepreneurs had corrected the VAT ID at CLO's request.
However, the challenge, the threat and the imposition of three additional fines takes up too much time in cases where the payer can be involved in a cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The IRS rejected the exemption of reported intracomonality deliveries in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the IRS asked him to file a revised SH on the CLO, as the tax authorities cannot correct the VIES data themselves.
BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor the CLO checked the submission of the repaired SH, so payers often did not comply with the request.
In view of the fact that the CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, a comparison of the data on the supply of goods declared in the VAT return and in SH will not take place prior to the submission of these data by the CLO of the other Member States.
This check can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied in the preparation of VAT control.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed into the CLO.
The incorrect VAT ID is selected and are then submitted to the Member States concerned.
These data are used for the purpose of controlling the acquisition carried out by the tax authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, the CLO will check them on the basis of a comparison with data from previous calendar quarters.
Where they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is generated and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created at a later date and presented to the tax authorities.
RMS installed for the purpose of the assessment procedure will then check these data with data on intracomonality acquisitions.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who do not have full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have made supplies of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State shall lodge SH within 25 days of the end of the calendar quarter to the locally competent tax authority.
The tax authorities will process SH and transmit the data to the CLO.
The values of the supply of goods to another Member State, referred to by the payers in SH, shall be compared at the tax authorities with the values of the supply of goods to another Member State, those payers in VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who made intracomonality delivery are required to be served quarterly by the SH by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
SHs are served on CLO, from 1 January 2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities have information from SH only after they are processed at the CLO.
The payers from both the Czech Republic and Germany list only the supply of goods in SH, the provision of services is not mentioned in SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are unable to correct the wrong lines filed by SH themselves.
As a result of this limited approach to the data of the German VIES system, the erroneous VAT ID was not corrected, even though the payer provided the FCA with the correct VAT ID.
The German tax authorities do not compare the data on intracomonality supplies contained in the VAT tax return of the German payer and his SH.
Differences between the data of these two statements are usually not found before the German CLO provides VIES data to other Member States.
In view of the BRH findings, it is clear that the comparison would increase the reliability of the transmitted data in VIES.
Data on the supply of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT tax returns.
The comparison is made by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are passed on to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in the payers' tax returns.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intracomonarian acquisitions.
Such general control is processed only for payers who do not have full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax authorities control the taxation of intracomonant acquisitions of other payers only if RMS produces a control warning or if the payer is intended to be checked anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities from the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of RMS.
Troubleshooting carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intracomonality acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specially VIES, provides information to the financial authorities that can be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if the payers serve SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, as most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are obliged to file VAT returns on a monthly basis - and SH does not require any further information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, the submission of SH may be linked to the submission of a VAT return.
However, the obligation to administer SH per month would cause more time disagreements between the reporting of intracomonality delivery and intracomonality acquisition and could increase the flow of data between individual CLOs.
In 2006, the German federal government considered the general provision of monthly SHs.
Its implementation failed because of the doubts of the federal states.
They feared that the monthly submission of VIES data to the CLO of other Member States could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the monthly reporting obligation to SH and monthly data transfer were to be effective, the monthly update of VIES would require a European standard of monthly SHs.
Statistics on the delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
Within the framework of foreign trade, Germany represents the most important trading partner for the Czech Republic.
The total volumes of intracomonial transactions in goods made between the Czech Republic and Germany are shown in Table 2.
Both SAI requested data on the number of erroneous VAT number or VAT ID, contained in O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data shows substantial differences.
The cause of these differences may be a different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers to their numbers to the calendar quarter for which SH was submitted, the German CLO refers to their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was adopted.
International exchange of information level 3
Implementation of international information exchange in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States regarding intracomonality trading transactions and payers who have made such transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, namely the exchange of information on request and the exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information upon request is carried out in the form of a so-called request for information (hereinafter referred to as the "ŽOI"), using standardised SCAC forms.
Tax administrators from the Czech Republic send their ŽOI, respectively replies to delivered ŽOI through the financial directorates to CLO, which provides translation of the information given on standardized SCAC forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
The CLO also ensures the income of ŽOI from other Member States and replies to the dispatched ŽOI, their translation into Czech and distribution to the locally competent tax administrators for processing.
Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 sets a maximum time limit for processing a range of 3 months from receipt of the application.
The SAO's control was subjected to all ŽOI, transmitted during the audited period between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Of the total number of 94 ŽOI, received in the Czech Republic from Germany, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) were dealt with within the prescribed three-month period, another 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were dealt with after this deadline and the remaining 1 case was not sent to Germany by the time of the SAO's audit.
More detailed information about the deadlines in which responses to the ŽOI received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic contains Figure 2.
Of the total number of 335 ŽOI sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) received a reply within the specified three-month period, a further 179 (i.e. 53.4%) of the applications were answered after this deadline and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) had not been received by the time of the SAO's examination (in the remaining 1 case it was not possible to determine from the transmitted data when the response from Germany was delivered).
More detailed information about the deadlines in which the responses to the ŽOI sent to Germany were delivered to the Czech Republic contains Figure 3.
The percentage of the values of intracomonant transactions, presented in the ŽOI transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany, contains graph No. 4.
As can be seen from the above graph, the value of commercial transactions, examined through ŽOI, was most often in the range above EUR 60 000.
The international exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic or structured automatic exchange of information, or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax managers from other Member States are often transferred without prior request information that may be relevant to them in the management of VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at the CLO.
Information is transmitted electronically between Member States.
‘Automatic exchange’ under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and at predetermined regular intervals.
"Structified by automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information about the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available for the tax administrator from the form of the Report on the delivery of a new means of transport pursuant to Section 19 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the issued tax document.
When processing the aforementioned form, the tax administrator shall complete the necessary data into a specially created template and transmit it in turn to the contact worker at the Financial Directorate, where the data are collected and transmitted to the CLO for subsequent processing and transfer to other Member States within a specified period of time, i.e. no later than two months after the end of the quarter in which this information was available.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on mail order sales that is exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU operations that appears to be unjustified and information on potential "missing traders".
This information is sent to other Member States in the form of spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of international information exchange in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the locally competent tax authority.
The tax authorities send the completed form SCAC 2004 by email directly to the German CLO, which transmits the SCAC forms to foreign CLO.
The tax authorities were instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information checked by the BRH were sent in order to ensure taxation of intracomonality acquisitions in another Member State, or to prove the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it shall check the value of the supply of goods or services referred to in the application for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
Where there is no reasonable grounds for such request, the German CLO shall reject any application containing an amount lower than that fixed limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are neither in German nor in English.
In order to answer the request for information, the CLO sends the request to the competent tax authority, pointing to the three-month deadline.
There are no additional deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor past time limits, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to alert the tax authorities to reply to blank requests for information.
The tax authorities will obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit covering any taxable process over a period of several months or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only relate to one business operation that has recently been carried out.
This short and flexible audit type does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has demonstrated its usefulness in the investigation of individual taxable business operations.
As part of an automatic exchange without prior application, Germany provides information to other Member States - on the VAT ID allocated to payers resident in other Member States - on the refund of input tax to payers resident in other Member States.
In addition, Germany has committed itself to providing other Member States with the following information through structured automatic exchange:
a. Delivery of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without the use of their VAT ID, b. sending or catalogue sale in other Member States that is not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intracomonality acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. intracomonality delivery of goods which the German payer did not show in SH because he treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. potential "missing trader" which carried out intracomonarian transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who supplied goods to potential "writing traders" or to those recipients who misused their VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
The dispatch of ŽOI or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and in Germany by the locally competent tax authorities, which send the completed SCAC form to CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the SCAC bilingual form (English - English) and translates the sent information into English or German, the German tax authorities follow the instruction according to which they are to write ŽOI or spontaneous information only in German on a single-language form.
The German CLO does not provide for the translation of German texts.
By examining the ŽOI transmitted between 1 May 2004 and 31 December 2005 between the Czech Republic and Germany, the SAO found that the Czech tax administration had handled 74.5% of the applications received within the prescribed three-month period, while the ŽOI sent to Germany was processed by the German tax administration within the deadline of only 40.6% of the cases.
Although the German CLO draws the attention of the tax authorities to a three-month deadline, it does not follow the past time limits.
The result of the missing notifications is a large number of delayed responses to the HOI.
Because of these problems, BRH recommended conducting regular notifications to the CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information from the German CLO, it is now alerting the tax authorities to answer unfinished responses to the HOI.
Risk management in the area of VAT
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, VAT risk management is dealt with by several departments at various organisational levels of the tax administration.
Under the I.M.F., risk management issues and the fight against VAT fraud are dealt with by the following services:
The Department of Methodology and the Performance of VAT and within it the VAT Risk Management report, which, among other things, manages the risk selection of possible tax evasion and evaluates the trends of these risks at both domestic and Community levels.
It coordinates nationwide the functioning of the role of the credibility of VAT tax returns and the use of data from the VIES system in terms of risks of tax evasion in the context of intracomonality transactions.
Based on data from the trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risky commodities, processes conceptually risk management in the field of VAT and cooperates with relevant EU institutions and other Member States in this area.
The International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT, which inter alia ensures the exchange of VAT information, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, ensures public awareness and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAI requested data on the number of erroneous VAT number or VAT ID, contained in O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data shows substantial differences.
The cause of these differences may be a different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL messages.
While the Czech CLO refers to their numbers to the calendar quarter for which SH was submitted, the German CLO refers to their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was adopted.
The Tax Control and Search Methodology Department, which among other things carries out risk analysis under the methodological management of tax controls and, in line with the risk analysis, sets priorities for targeting tax controls in the plans of the Financial Directorate, processes risk analyses in the context of reducing tax evasion, including the collection of knowledge gained in tax management as well as other sources, and proposes measures to curb tax evasion.
Search departments are set up in financial directorates to carry out, among other things, searches for tax entities and areas that are risky in terms of the occurrence of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), searches for unregistered tax entities in terms of risks of tax evasion (e.g. internet services, job mediation, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of links of chain fraud and the transfer of information to local tax authorities.
A specialised control unit is set up at the selected 12 tax offices.
They have regional competence, tax controls outside the territorial jurisdiction of the tax authorities are carried out on the basis of a mandate.
The need to establish a department of specialised tax inspections has emerged from the increasing findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which occur primarily in chain-linked entities.
These departments focus on controlling tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities and multinational companies and large-scale tax entities in terms of turnover size.
The following mechanisms to limit VAT risks have been integrated into the ADIS system: – the role The credibility of VAT tax returns, used to assess the riskiness of the tax returns filed; – the role The selection of tax entities for control, which allows the payer to be selected for inspection on the basis of the chosen criteria, – the role of VIES through which tax administrations have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES allows, inter alia: – to verify the validity of VAT ID of payers from other Member States, – to obtain from other Member States the values of goods supplied to the Czech payer, declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States, – to generate a set of payers who did not do SH, – to carry out a formal check of the data provided by the payers of the Czech Republic before sending these data to other Member States, – to generate a set of payers for which the data on the supply of goods to other Member States mentioned in the VAT returns do not match the data in SH, – to generate a set of payers for which the value of the goods from other Member States mentioned in the VAT returns.
As part of the activity to limit the risks of tax evasion, tax administrators have access to registers of government bodies such as a business register, land register, motor vehicle register, trade licensing register, etc.
More detailed information is provided in chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal (federal) structure of Germany, the federal tax administration (especially the CLO) and the tax administration of the 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither the CLO nor the tax administrations of federal states share a fully consistent database.
At the CLO level, the ST I 2 unit (KUSS) collects the findings of the control relating to tax fraud in a separate database called the OPUS.
The KUSS, in cooperation with the tax authorities, has introduced a new database called ZAUBER designed to transfer the names of tax fraudsters' companies "missing traders."
The KUSS coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
KUSS experience is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, specialists in several other CLO and MF departments are entrusted with RMS-related duties and powers.
At CLO level, a formal check is in place for the composition of the VAT ID of other Member States in SH submitted by German payers.
This formal check is carried out prior to the provision of data from SH to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
The verification of the validity of the VAT ID referred to in SH is made on the basis of O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the invalid VAT ID correction procedure, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, the CLO RMS is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and creates several types of control reports based on several characteristics, which usually feature in so-called carousel commercial operations, in order to identify potential "missing traders".
The financial authorities of the federal states have instructions to process these inspection reports and in some cases report on the results of their CLO findings.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed the need to take into account all the characteristics available if the existence of a tax fraud case is to be presumed with sufficient probability (place of exclusive focus on the company's turnover).
BRH therefore proposed to the I.M.F. to take into account different characteristics when processing the reports.
RMS should also sanction other facts, such as the payment behaviour (morality) of the taxpayer, the field (economic activities) or the shareholder structure.
The second level of RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the federal states and aimed at processing VAT returns.
RMS, for example, generates a list of those payers who have declared intracomonality delivery in their tax returns.
This list is sent to CLO to monitor the full use of SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares the intracomonality acquisition, reported in the payer's annual VAT return, with the VIES data.
The tax administrations of the Länder seek to avoid comparing quarterly data, as this comparison would reveal too much disapproving data attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
– a different period of implementation of the intracomonality transaction in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand and the beneficiary on the other;
– Different accounting for sales discounts and sales events (bids) and their different reporting in the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from VAT and VIES tax returns, many federal states have introduced elements of RMS, which are based on the data of VAT returns and certain other facts (such as the structure of the company's name, the age of shareholders, the number of employees and the payment behaviour/or morality of the taxpayer).
Bavaria has introduced a rule-based RMS that allows a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter referred to as risk managers) to program its own rules for singling out potential perpetrators of tax fraud.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
The competent tax authority will therefore receive the recommendation created by RMS before setting the VAT.
As this RMS is unable to translate current findings into its activities, risk managers must adjust the relevant rules based on the feedback of the tax authorities.
The administrative district of Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with tax file data in which the inspection revealed tax evasion.
Based on these data, RMS is able to identify the characteristics of tax evasion.
RMS creates a once-a-month list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The competent tax authorities use this list as a basis for audit decisions proposed by taxpayers.
After the audit, auditors must report on their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The administrative region of North Rhine-Westphalia uses an adaptive artificial neural network, which is combined with a rule-based fuzzy system.
Based on the large number of data assessed for VAT returns and certain other facts, this neural-fusion system or system of collecting potentially useful information (the so-called data-mining system) calculates the likelihood that a taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential perpetrators of fraud.
Local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers for inspection and report the findings of the data processing centre.
The implementation of one of these three RMSs in the other Länder is further ongoing.
Since none of these three RMS is based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful for dealing with tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH have found that each Member State has developed its own RMS.
As well as the different approaches in the three federal states of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
The tax authorities of EU Member States are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud – especially carousel fraud – does not prove to be a national problem, but rather a European problem.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State, but in multiple states.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by only one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
VAT loss caused by fraud in the EU may not affect a Member State instigator of fraud.
Any Member State that is involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
There should therefore be a European exchange and debate on RMS.
Selected control findings when verifying commercial transactions
As part of the cooperation on the implementation of parallel control actions, the SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information about selected business transactions that were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
Furthermore, the two audit institutions jointly examined the implementation of several commercial transactions where there were doubts about their implementation or irregularities in the way in which the payers from both countries declared these commercial transactions in their VAT and SH tax returns respectively.
At the request of BRH, the SAO examined a total of 8 cases involving commercial transactions carried out between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
Furthermore, in 43 cases, the SAO examined the values of intracomonant transactions with Germany on the basis of warnings from BRH, which Czech payers reported in their tax returns and SH.
BRH examined a total of 23 cases at the request of the SAO relating to commercial transactions carried out between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with the CLO.
By examining selected cases, it was found, among other things, that a different method of registration in EU Member States leads to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to data in VIES, the Czech payer was to acquire in the third quarter of 2004 from the German payer of goods worth EUR 60 500.
As the Czech payer ordered the acquisition of the goods only at a value equivalent to EUR 29 869, the Czech tax administrator sent an application to Germany to examine the value of the goods delivered.
In response to the ŽOI delivered from Germany, the German side stated that in the second quarter of 2004 the German payer had supplied the Czech payer of goods worth EUR 27 381, in the third quarter of EUR 31 997 and in the fourth quarter of 2004 worth EUR 10 276.
The reply further showed that the VAT ID of the German payer had only been in force since 28 September 2004, but the German CLO retroactively issued a VAT ID certificate from 1 May 2004 following an additional request from the German payer for the VAT ID certificate.
The German payer repaired SH.
The Czech payer, based on this information, was the acquisition of goods.
The SAO, asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that the Czech payer, on the basis of an investigation by the tax administrator, filed additional VAT returns for individual tax periods in 2004, in which he increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States and at the same time exercised the right to deduct VAT when acquiring goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT tax returns, the Czech tax administrator could not clearly determine whether the supply values from the aforementioned German supplier were also included.
BRH, based on the SAO's request, found that the German supplier was registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not apply for a VAT ID when registering, he was only assigned an identification number for transactions within Germany.
Although it is usually not possible to allocate VAT ID to the payer retroactively in Germany, in this case the German tax official assigned the aforementioned German VAT ID payer retroactively as of 1.5.2004.
The German CLO allocates the VAT ID retroactively if the German entrepreneur did not cause a delay in the assignment; for example, if the delay was caused by CLO after the payer's VAT ID application.
In this case, the CLO allocates the VAT ID retroactively, because the entrepreneur does not need his own valid VAT ID for intracomonality supplies under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
Conversely, the German beneficiary does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier in order to declare intracomonality acquisitions.
Because of these different procedures between Member States, the German CLO assigned a VAT ID retroactively in this particular case.
2.
The Czech tax administrator asked for information on the verification of the registration of the German VAT payer as part of the international exchange of information.
VIES indicated the date of registration of 5.3.2005, with the date of 1.10.2004 on the registration certificate of the German payer issued by the locally competent German tax authority.
In a reply delivered from Germany, the German side stated that the German tax entity had been registered since 1 October 2004, but VAT ID was granted to him in Germany for organisational reasons only on 16 February 2005.
The SAO, asking the locally competent tax administrator, found that the Czech tax administrator had carried out a VAT check on the Czech payer for the tax period of the third quarter of 2004 to the second quarter of 2005.
With this check, the tax authority found that the Czech payer included in the VAT tax return services worth CZK 9,897 (EUR 314), provided to the German payer in the period prior to its VAT registration (i.e. before 1 October 2004).
For the tax year III quarter of 2004, the tax office assessed the tax entity's VAT of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
BRH, at the request of the SAO, found that the German payer was not allocated VAT ID until 16.2.2005 when he informed the tax office about his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it retrospectively for VAT on 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer reported intracomonality acquisitions from the Czech Republic worth EUR 160 (approx. CZK 5,000).
3. In the VAT return for September 2004 and SH for the third quarter of 2004, the Czech payer reported a supply of goods worth CZK 114 615 (EUR 3 642) to a German payer.
When verifying the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, the Czech tax administrator found that his registration was valid from 11 November 2004, i.e. after the delivery of goods by a Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer filed an additional DAP for VAT, in which he reported the tax base on transactions carried out in the Czech Republic worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3 642) and VAT of CZK 21,777 (EUR 692), which he paid.
The SAO's inquiry with the locally competent tax authority in the Czech Republic found that the Czech payer subsequently filed a request for a retrial in respect of an additional VAT return and as evidence submitted a confirmation from the German tax administration that the German payer had been taxed since 1 January 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer as part of the international exchange of information.
The reply received from Germany showed that the German payer was not allocated VAT ID until 11 November 2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the request for a retrial.
BRH found that this case was not an intracomonality acquisition of goods, as the German payer obtained the VAT ID until 11.11.2004.
However, the German beneficiary ordered the acquisition as an intracomonality acquisition and declared VAT on that acquisition when it claimed a refund of input tax at the same amount.
However, since there would be no changes in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the tax administrator in Germany did not correct the data in his VAT return.
BRH further found that the name of the German payer, mentioned in ŽOI, was changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in a mix-up of two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of goods by a Czech payer in the first quarter of 2005 worth EUR 22 686 from a German payer.
The SAO, asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that this administrator carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, during which he verified that the delivery of the goods had taken place and the Czech payer had booked and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not admit the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return because the German supplier did not state his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer was registered for VAT for intracomonality transactions only from 21.4.2005, i.e. after the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the registration certificate to the German payer so that he could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech Financial Conduct Authority assessed the transaction as the acquisition of goods from a non-payer from Germany, and therefore did not additionally measure the tax on the Czech payer from that commercial transaction.
BRH found that, under German law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States did not have to have a VAT ID allocated to an intracomonality supply of goods.
The supplier must only have a VAT ID of the customer from another Member State and must be able to prove the transport of the goods in question to another Member State.
Under the German VAT Act, it was therefore an intracomonality transaction and VAT should be assessed in the Czech Republic.
In any case, it is important that the Czech tax administrator noticed this transaction, because the delivery of the machine at that value was not the basic business of the German supplier.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to respond to ŽOI relating to intracomonarian transactions worth less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to VIES data in the third quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to acquire goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer.
The Czech tax administrator carried out a tax inspection with the tax entity for this tax year.
As part of international administrative cooperation, he asked the German tax administration to verify the supply of these goods through the SCAC form.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of the goods, claiming that he had never traded with the German company and the acquisition of these goods was not accounted for in his accounts.
The German tax authorities rejected the requirement to provide evidence – contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents on the ground that the turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no other explanatory justification was given.
As the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence to obtain the tax on the acquired goods, he terminated the tax inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
BRH, based on the SAO's request, found that the German payer acted as a so-called "fiscal representative" (Sections 22 a – e UStG).
The German payer reported those deliveries in his annual VAT return and in SH.
Entitlement to the exemption of delivery was recognised.
Based on warnings from BRH, the German tax office will send documents needed to the Czech Republic to collect the tax on acquired goods in the Czech Republic.
As mentioned in chapter 4.6.1, the replies to the ŽOI sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the three-month deadline more often than the replies from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO's audit found that the Czech tax administration had sent a request for information to Germany on 5.10.2005 concerning the examination of the value of the delivered goods for the 4th quarter of 2004.
The German payer reported a supply of goods to a Czech payer worth EUR 86 307 in SH for this period, but the Czech payer stated in the same period in the VAT tax return the acquisition of goods only at a value equivalent to EUR 35 314.
In response to ŽOI, delivered to the Czech Republic on September 9, 2006, i.e. after the deadline for processing, provided for in Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German party stated that the application could not have been processed because the operation of the German firm was terminated at the end of 2005.
By failing to meet the deadline for processing the ŽOI, the Czech tax administration did not have the documents needed for tax proceedings in the Czech Republic.
7. The Czech tax administrator applied in 2005 via the SCAC form to examine the delivery of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to the German payer, carried out in the third and fourth quarters of 2004, which showed the hallmarks of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that a response had not been received from the FRG until the time of the inspection.
The SAO further found by asking the locally competent tax administrator that the Czech payer did not include in the VAT tax return the supply of new means of transport for the German payer worth CZK 11,816,103 (EUR 375 472).
The Czech tax administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity filed a subsequent SH.
BRH, following a request from the SAO, found that the German CLO had not, for technical reasons, hand over the aforementioned ŽOI to the locally competent tax authority for verification.
Following warnings from BRH, a check was carried out in Germany by the German acquirer, which found that the acquisition of all cars had been properly taxed and that the respective cars had been sold to another payer in Germany.
8. According to VIES data, the Czech payer was to acquire a passenger car worth €48,500 from a German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The purchase of these goods was not acknowledged by the Czech payer.
By asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
Tax returns were not filed by the Czech payer even after the tax administrator's calls, so the tax office sentenced him to VAT of CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004.
On 2 June 2005 the CLO drew attention to the aforementioned supply from the German payer.
As the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, the tax administrator sent the ŽOI to Germany concerning the aforementioned supply.
As the response to the ŽOI was not delivered to the Czech Republic until 7 February 2007, it was not known until the end of the SAO's audit how the Czech tax administrator used the information obtained by international exchange.
The tax office revoked the Czech payer's VAT registration on 23 August 2005 due to non-compliance with VAT obligations.
In some cases, only a partial response was sent to the ROI, as the audit carried out by the tax authorities at the payers was not completed at the time of the SAO and BRH inspection:
9.
The Czech tax administrator applied in 2005 via the SCAC form to examine the delivery of a car worth EUR 16 991 to the German payer, made in the third quarter of 2004, which showed the hallmarks of carousel fraud.
In response to the ŽOI, the German tax administrator stated that he had only an invoice issued by the Czech payer for supplies worth EUR 16 335.
BRH, following the SAO's request, found that the control carried out by the German tax office with the acquirer from Germany had not yet been completed.
The German acquirer ordered the acquisition of goods worth EUR 16 335 twice in tax returns for the months of August and September 2004.
10. The Czech tax administrator applied in 2005 via the SCAC form to examine the delivery of cars to a German payer worth 198 167 euro, carried out in the fourth quarter of 2004 and I. quarter 2005, which showed the hallmarks of carousel fraud.
The German tax administration sent a partial response to the ŽOI to the Czech Republic, in which it confirmed the acquisition of some cars by a German payer and further stated that the investigation in Germany had not been completed.

BRH found that the German payer had, in that period, in its VAT tax returns, ordered the acquisition of goods from other Member States for a total value of EUR 579 114 and that the control carried out by the German tax office from the acquirer of Germany had not yet been completed.

11.
The Czech payer was to acquire EUR 35 716 worth of goods from the German payer in the first quarter of 2005, according to data from the VIES system, but the Czech payer did not acknowledge this acquisition.
As the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not carry out any activity at the company's headquarters, the Czech tax administrator asked as part of the international exchange of information to verify how the German payer communicated with the Czech payer.
The answer to the ŽOI delivered from Germany showed that according to the findings of the German tax administration, the Czech tax entity is unknown at the communicated address and that the goods were taken over by the agreed carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer only supplied the goods worth EUR 21 659.
The Czech payer sent the German payer a false confirmation of the payment of EUR 155 153 in favour of the German payer.
After discovering the fraudulent conduct on the part of the Czech acquirer, the German payer, with the help of his other Czech customers, managed to recover the supplied material, with the exception of one item worth EUR 7 916.
The SAO, asking the locally competent tax authority in the Czech Republic, found that the tax administrator, on the basis of the information obtained, assessed the Czech VAT payer for the acquisition of goods from other Member States amounting to CZK 388,522 (EUR 13,044).
BRH, based on the SAO's request, confirmed that the German supplier had ordered the supply of goods to the Czech payer only worth EUR 7 9116 after repairs.
According to the German legal situation, the German payer reported the repaired value of the goods and a decrease in the taxable amount in the quarter in which the correction took place.

12.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator requested, via the SCAC form, to verify the supply of goods and services made in the third quarter of 2005.
According to this ŽOI, the Czech payer was to deliver goods totalling EUR 396 126 to the German payer during this period and to provide services worth EUR 11 885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation into the Czech payer for the purpose of examining this delivery.
In response to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator said that the Czech payer had supplied the German payer with a production line, including assembly.
Individual parts of the production line were supplied by the Czech payer before the Czech Republic joined the EU and after 1 May 2004 the line was assembled on the basis of the order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed to have defects.
In the third quarter of 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer took the issued invoices but did not acknowledge them and did not pay them.
The SAO further found by asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic that all invoices are duly registered in the accounts of the Czech payer.
VAT returns for the third quarter of 2005 include only amounts that have been substantiated by the Czech payer and relating to invoicing after 1 May 2004.
BRH found that based on a response from the Czech tax administration, the locally competent tax authority in Germany concluded that the transaction involved the supply of goods from the Czech payer to the German payer, including the assembly services.
In this special case, the place of so-called performance of the work is where the production line was installed.
Under the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the service supplied is obliged to pay VAT.
At the same time, the beneficiary can claim the deduction of VAT on the same amount.
As there would be no changes in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the corrections to the VAT tax return were neglected by the German tax authority.
13. According to VIES data, Czech payer A was to acquire a machine worth EUR 58 000 from the German payer C in February 2005.
The Czech tax administrator sent an application to Germany to examine this delivery.
In response to the ŽOI, the German side said that the machine had already been supplied by the German payer C to the Czech payer B in 2004, which, however, was to return the machine to the German payer C in October 2004.
According to information from the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but transported to the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, a reply to a request for information showed that the German payer C had sold the machine to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Because the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intracomonant delivery of goods.
The SAO, asking the tax administrator of the locally competent payer B, found that according to VIES data, the German payer C supplied the Czech B goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 0227 in the third quarter of 2004.
Payer B denied this acquisition of the goods, so the locally competent tax administrator from the Czech Republic sent the ŽOI to Germany.
According to the reply to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
Another investigation by the payer B found that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in the accounts of the payer B, and that it could be a machine of the same type as was delivered by the German payer C's organisational unit to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO further found that the Czech tax administrator of the locally competent payer A carried out a local investigation with this payer.
The tax administrator had at his disposal the invoice of the German payer C of 7.2.2005, on which the payer A was listed as a purchaser of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that the payer A did not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payet A had a lease agreement with another Czech company, where the lease was a machine of the same type.
The transfer of the machine from the leasing company took place on 9.2.2, the transport of the machine was carried out by a leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech Tax Office to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found that the German payer C had not supplied the machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer, D.
It was therefore not an intracomonant supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax administrator did not recognise the German VAT exemption and corrected the data in his tax return.
German payer D supplied the machine to the Czech payer B.
According to the German legislation, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, BRH found that the German payer C gave in his SH for the first quarter of 2005 the delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000 to the Czech payer A.
This supply was not examined by the German tax authorities during the tax audit.

14.
When inspecting the ŽOI received, the SAO found that the Czech tax administration had received a request from Germany on 4.10.2005 from Germany asking the German tax administrator to verify the intracomonality delivery from a German payer worth 879 680 625 euro to the Czech payer.
According to the German tax administrator, there was a suspicion that this was a feigned intracomonarian supply of goods.
It was further stated at the ŽOI that the German payer had not carried out any active commercial activities since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation with the Czech taxpayer.
According to the statement of the manager of the Czech company, in the above case it appeared to be a claim by the German taxpayer against the German tax administration, which was claimed by the Czech payer as a partner of the German company to the German tax office.
According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administrator has no information until now that the German tax administration has dealt with the issue related to the Czech payer.
According to the available information, it was not a supply of goods, yet the stated value is still included in the VIES system as an intracomonality delivery of goods to a Czech payer from Germany.
The main reason for the following irregularities was that the beneficiaries did not report intracomonality acquisitions of goods in their tax returns (see also chapter 4.4.1):
