15. According to VIES data, the German payer supplied the Czech payer with a total value of EUR 33 205 in the third quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005. The Czech payer did not admit this acquisition.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The Czech tax administrator asked for verification of the delivery of goods from Germany as part of the international exchange of information.
In response to this request, the German tax administration said that the German payer had sent part of the goods to the address of the Czech payer, the remaining goods were collected personally by the Czech payer.
By asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that even before receiving a response to the ŽOI, the Czech payer filed additional VAT returns for those periods.
Despite this submission, differences in acquisition values have not been resolved, so the Czech tax administrator recommended carrying out a tax inspection with the Czech taxpayer.
The inspection has not yet been carried out.
16. According to VIES figures in the third quarter of 2004, the German payer delivered goods worth €46,854.
Over the same period, the Czech payer granted an intracomonality acquisition only equivalent to EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator asked for verification in the framework of the international exchange of information the value of the deliveries made.
The reply to the ŽOI, received from Germany, was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of the supply of goods 31 999 euro, i.e. a value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer and the VIES data.
The SAO, asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that after receiving a response from Germany, the Czech tax administrator contacted the Czech payer and agreed with it that after examining these invoices with the owner of the company, he would discuss filing an additional VAT return for the third quarter of 2004.
An additional VAT return has not yet been filed.
The Czech tax administrator told the SAO that it would proceed in such a way as to meet the set deadlines for any additional VAT assessment for the relevant tax period.
17.
The German payer was to deliver €11,600 worth of goods to the Czech payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The German tax administrator asked for confirmation as part of an international exchange of information about whether the Czech payer actually existed, because an alleged partner of the German payer founded more fictitious companies in Germany.
When examining the business transaction, the Czech payer confirmed the acquisition of the goods to the tax authority.
According to the Czech payer, however, the goods were not transported from Germany to the Czech Republic and were further sold during 2005 in Germany.
The Czech payer presented documents for the sale of goods for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany, he did not grant or pay the tax on the sale of the goods in question in the Czech Republic or in Germany.
All these facts suggested tax evasion in the territory of Germany and the Czech tax administrator communicated them to the German tax administration in response to the ŽOI.
The SAO, asking the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, found that the Czech payer, on the basis of the investigations carried out, filed an additional VAT return for the fourth quarter of 2004, in which he included the value of the acquisition of goods, among other things, from the German payer and at the same time exercised the right to deduct the tax on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
VAT on the sale of goods in Germany was not included in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return after the local investigation was carried out unchanged.
According to the Czech legislation, this case did not involve the acquisition of goods from other Member States because the goods were not dispatched or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator therefore incorrectly concluded the local investigation.
BRH found that the German tax administrator had corrected the German payer's tax return immediately after receiving a reply to the ROI stating that the goods had not left Germany, had corrected the German payer's tax return and demanded VAT of EUR 1 600 from him.
In addition, the competent tax authority has sent a warning to the tax office of the actual recipient of the goods to ensure that the resale of these goods is correctly taxed.
In the following cases, the payers reported intracomonality transactions that were unlikely to actually take place:
18.
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech payer acquired a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German payer in February 2005.
The application was accompanied by a copy of the Czech VAT registration certificate.
In addition, a copy of the passport of the person who, as has been said, had carried out the transport of that car was accompanied.
An investigation by the Czech tax administrator found that it was a stolen passport, the person in it did not bring any vehicle to the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax entity.
The VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German side, was never issued by the Czech tax administrator.
This information was provided by the Czech tax administrator in response to the ŽOI along with the statement that it could not confirm the acquisition of the goods – the car in question.
The SAO's inquiry with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic found that the Czech payer did not resettled at the address listed in the Commercial Register and the company's manager was uncontactable.
After the execution of the complaint procedure for the February 2005 tax year, the Czech tax administrator imposed a tax liability of CZK 0 on the Czech taxpayer.
Another investigation by the Czech tax administrator found that the car in question was sold to another Czech entity, which bought it through an advertisement on the internet.
BRH found that the locally competent German tax administrator, on the basis of the Czech response to the ŽOI, would not recognise the German taxpayer's right to exempt that supply from VAT.
19. During the audit, the German tax authority was unable to clarify the difference of EUR 3,000 between the value of the goods acquired in the payer's tax return and the value provided from another Member State.
It was reported that the Czech payer was to deliver goods worth €89,4224 to the German payer during the fourth quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the data in VIES, the German tax administrator asked for verification of deliveries and their remuneration in the international exchange of information.
The Czech tax administrator said in a reply to the ŽOI that the sole manager of the Czech company was removed from the Commercial Register on 8 July 2005 and the new manager was not registered.
The German recipient of the goods was apparently related to a partner of Czech society.
The Czech payer filed tax returns for both VAT and SH, which was signed by an unauthorized person - the company's partner, after deleting the manager from the Commercial Register.
The Czech payer's accountant confirmed to the tax administrator that the company's partner had deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Cash papers were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic, when asked by the locally competent tax authority, found that the tax administrator had recognised the Czech taxpayer for the fourth quarter of 2004 entitlement to an exemption from VAT on the supply of goods to another Member State worth CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 422,145) and for the 1st quarter of 2005 in the amount of CZK 1,416,180.
BRH found that the tax administrator in Germany had not repaired the German acquirer's VAT return because the German judge had in the meantime confirmed the insolvency of the German payer.
Since the earlier check revealed no signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to enforce the tax liability imposed.
20. According to data in VIES, in 2005 the German payer acquired goods worth EUR 4 251 196 from the Czech Republic after acquiring goods worth EUR 43 274 in the previous year.
In the 2004 tax return and in the 2005 tax return, the German payer did not report an intracomonality acquisition.
Furthermore, it did not show adequate supplies either.
Due to these differences, the German tax office sent the ROI, relating to the fourth quarter of 2005 and the first quarter of 2006.
The Czech supplier reported an intracomonality delivery of goods to a German payer totalling CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5 615,299) in SH for these two quarters.
On 6 September 2006, the ŽOI was delivered, in which the German side asked to check whether the Czech payer of reported intracomonarian supplies had taken place.
In response to this ŽOI, the Czech tax administration said that the German party's request could not be met because the Czech payer had no manager.
As is apparent from the materials provided by the SAO by the relevant tax authority, on 30 March 2006 a report was drawn up with the managing director of the Czech payer for the start of the VAT inspection for the fourth quarter of 2004 and January to December 2005.
At the same time, the payer was asked by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the abovementioned periods, but did not provide any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the only manager of the Czech payer ceased to function on 16.5.2006, a new agent was not appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech payer has stopped filing VAT returns.
As part of the SAO's audit in cooperation with BRH, among other things, it examined several cases of intracomonality deliveries made between the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not the subject of a previous exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the cases examined was transmitted by the two highest audit institutions through the CLO of both countries.
21. The Czech company (eCR), which is not resident in Germany informed the competent tax authority (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out a taxable supply in Germany.
Because of this information, the company has been registered since June 2005, but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) accepted an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind farms and for the delivery of these wind farms on behalf of, at risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to a lack of its own capacities, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows contractual relations and how wind farms are transported:
According to the German legal situation, the place of execution of these transactions must be determined according to the following:
– A Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent wind farms for assembly under his name, his risk and his account to Austria.
As the assembly of that supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
– Since the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his risk and on his own account, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the shipment began, in Germany.
Although wind farms were dispatched to another Member State and the recipient is a registered payer from another Member State, the supply of the German subcontractor (eD) could not obtain an exemption because another Member State of destination differs from another Member State of the registered office of the Czech company.
This delivery is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of transport.
The transport of some wind farms started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
– Delivery of those wind power plants that are manufactured in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
– The supply of other wind farms produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intracomonality delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intracomonarian delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not report any intracomonality acquisitions in its VAT return in Germany or injected SH to the German CLO.
So it is possible that the Czech company has reported all intracomonality deliveries uniformly as an intracomonality delivery from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that (eCR) showed no intracomonality delivery to Austria, but intracomonality delivery to Denmark.
Examination of the taxation of intracomonality acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), even though this case shows no indication of tax fraud or evasion.
In addition, the SAO and BRH examined transactions to highlight the differences between the reporting in the tax return and the VIES data caused by the different VAT legislation in 2004.
Controlled cases also demonstrate that changes in the legislation need time to apply new legislation to practice by both payers and tax authorities:
22. In SH for the second to IV quarter of 2004, the Czech payer reported an intracomonality delivery to a German payer with a total value of CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25 197 885).
Over the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported intracomonality delivery to another German payer with a total value of CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970.
According to information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers listed the above mentioned supplies in SH in accordance with the wording of Act No 235/2004 Coll., in force in 2004.
By further examining the above transactions, the SAO-controlling group found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the statutory regulation of the supply or acquisition of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the valid wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as an intracommunity supply of goods, in terms of the German legal regulation in force in 2004 it was not an intracomonality acquisition, but a taxable performance with the place of implementation of the fulfilment in the territory of Germany.
The difference in statutory regulations in the Czech Republic was eliminated by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., amending certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1 January 2005.
23. Furthermore, when examining selected intracomonant transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was found that the Czech payer reported an intracomonial delivery to the German payer in the 1st to 4th quarter of 2005 with a total value of 240 411 163 CZK (EUR 871 823) and another Czech payer reported intracomonial delivery to the German payer for the same period with a total value of 263 470 776 CZK (EUR 846 050).
According to information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, in the case of electricity supply, the place where the acquirer has its registered office, place of business or where it has an establishment for which the goods are delivered.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have introduced electricity supplies to SH in 2005.
By showing the intracomonality of electricity supply in SH by the two above payers, the VIES data was distorted by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
The cooperation met the objectives of BRH and the SAO.
Both SAI received a deeper knowledge of VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
Cooperation has revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that VAT management legislation differs.
During parallel checks, suspicious cases of intracomonarian transactions were found.
Some of them make sense to subsequently check.
Based on the control findings, both SAIs developed recommendations on VAT management.
Monitoring these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
The new experience and knowledge gained through cooperation between the two audit institutions is the basis for the successful implementation of the following VAT administration controls.
Communications
The report was drawn up in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, the Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in controls on excise duty management between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The joint report submitted informs about the course and outcome of international cooperation during parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and Najvyšší Control Office of the Slovak Republic, focused on the administration of excise duties in the period after the two countries joined the European Union.
The cooperation was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement in control activities concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel checks was chosen in view of the fundamental change in the system of collection of excise duties, which took place in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union from 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow non-taxable goods to circulate until the date of its final consumption delivery.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under the suspensive exemption scheme.
The system places great demands on the tax authorities and foresees close interaction between the competent administrations of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in controls on excise duty management for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Control number: (Czech Republic) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of control: (Czech Republic) Administration of excise duties (SR) Procedure of colné organs in sprays of spotreb taxes
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO-ČR) and the Najvyšší Control Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO of the SR) concluded on 8 February 2006 the "Contract of Cooperation in Control Activities".
The subject of the contract was cooperation during parallel checks carried out by the "Interim Tax Administration", included in the auditing plan of the SAO-ČR for 2005 under No 05/34, and "Control of the procedure of colné organs in sprays of spotrebné taxes", included in the control activity plan of the SAO SR for 2006 under No 48/11.
Parallel checks were in the nature of coordinated control.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information that the contracting parties could not obtain when checking the administration of excise duties on the territory of their State and in drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of controls within the meaning of the European implementing directives for the implementation of INTOSAI Audit Standards - Directive 31.
In the Czech Republic, the control (hereinafter referred to as the Czech Republic) was carried out by groups inspecting the state budget department and from the territorial unions of Central Bohemia, southern Bohemia, western Bohemia, northwestern Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and northern Moravia between 7 February and 2 June 2006.
The inspection involved 27 controllers.
The audited persons were the General Directorate of Customs (hereinafter referred to as the CD) and 11 tax authorities.
Within the DGC, 12 selected customs offices out of a total of 54.
The audit on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SR") was carried out by the Section of the Financial and Tax Office of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with exposures of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 between 13 February and 2 June 2006.
The inspection involved 8 controllers.
The aim of the parallel checks was to examine the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation was focused on the procedure of tax administrators in the exercise of supervision of the transport of goods subject to excise duties, in particular the registration of initiated and completed traffic under the conditional exemption regime, and on the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between excise tax administrators of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
2. Management of excise duties
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by the financial authorities until 31 December 2003.
Since 1 January 2004, this agenda has been taken over by the customs authorities, which have so far levied excise duty only on importation.
In the Czech Republic, mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty.
The state budget's revenue from excise duties in the Czech Republic amounted to a total of CZK 82.8 billion in 2004 and 19.5% of the state budget's revenues from taxes and fees.
In 2005, the state budget revenue from excise duties amounted to CZK 103.6 billion and the share of state budget revenues from taxes and fees amounting to CZK 460.4 billion was 22.5%.
In 2004, the income from excise duty on mineral oils to the State budget was 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it was 90.9%.
The difference to 100% of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the income of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in the SR shall be exercised by the customs authorities from 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise duty on mineral oil, which they have been administering since 1 January 2002.
Until then, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the tax authorities.
Excise duty in the SR is subject to mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
The revenue of the state budget from excise duties in the SR totalled 43.4 billion Sk in 2004 and in total tax revenues of 209.5 billion Sk, excise duties accounted for 20.7%.
In 2005, the state budget revenue from excise duties was 50 billion Sk and total tax revenues of 222.6 billion Sk accounted for 22.5%.
Graph 1 — Comparison of revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic with revenues from excise duties
Legislation in both countries is based on European Union rules governing this area, in particular: - Council Directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements for the holding, movement and monitoring of products subject to excise duty (hereinafter referred to as "Directive 92/12/EEC), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as ‘Regulation No 2073/2004’), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the transport of products subject to excise duty under the suspension of excise duty (hereinafter referred to as ‘Regulation No 2719/92’), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 3649/92 on a simplified movement for excise duty (hereinafter referred to as Regulation No 2719/92), - Commission Regulation (EEC)
The basic legislation governing the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No. 353/2003 Coll., on Excise Taxes, as amended, (hereinafter referred to as "Law No. 353/2003 Coll.").
When administering excise duties in the SR, customs authorities are bound, inter alia, by the following generally binding legislation: - Act No 98/2004 Z. z. o spotrebne oil tax in the knowledge of non-corporate predtoy (hereinafter referred to as Law No 98/2004 Z. z., - Act No 104/2004 Z. z. z. o spotrebalé tax on wine in the denial of non-corporate predpisov (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 104/2004 Z. z."), - Act No. 105/2004 Z.
2.1 Movement of excise goods under a suspensive tax exemption scheme between Member States of the European Union
The conditions for the movement of excise goods under the suspension exemption procedure are governed by Directive 92/12/EEC in Title III — Movement of goods from Article 15 to 20.
Under those provisions, the transport of those goods may be carried out only by an authorised warehousekeeper, which means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
A consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of an authorised warehousekeeper, but who may not, under a suspensive exemption scheme, store or dispatch them further.
The authorised warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and Slovakia means the operator of a tax warehouse, the economic operator is the beneficiary for the repeated or one-off acceptance of products subject to excise duty.
Under Directive 92/12/EEC, the transport of excise products subject to excise duty is only possible with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be issued by the consignor before the commencement of the service in four copies, unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch request a further copy.
2.2 Procedure for the start and termination of the transport of goods under the conditional exemption procedure between the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for the commencement of transport is governed by the provisions of Section 25(3) of Act No 353/2003 Coll., which states, among other things:
‘The operator of the tax warehouse shall, before commencing the transport of the selected products, inform the customs office which is the place competent for the tax warehouse from which transport is to be commenced;
transport of selected products can only be initiated with the consent of this customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the transport of the selected products without delay after the condition of securing the tax is met ..."
A freight forwarder in the Czech Republic may commence the transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of transport only if the tax is provided for the amount of tax attributable to the products transported.
Before commencing the transport, the sender is obliged to prepare an accompanying document in five copies.
On the accompanying document, the customs office shall indicate its consent to the commencement of transport.
Production No 1 shall be retained by the consignor, copy Nos 2, 3, and 4 shall be surrendered by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be retained by the customs office authorising the transport.
Under the Slovak legislation, the recipient in SR will keep copy No 2 of the accompanying document. On the copies Nos 3 and 4, they shall acknowledge receipt of the products and submit the two copies to the competent customs office locally.
Production No 3 confirmed by the customs office shall send to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which he accepted the products.
Production No 4 shall be retained by the customs office of the consignee.
Transport is terminated by the acceptance of products by the recipient.
The release of the tax security will be decided by the customs office in the Czech Republic, which authorised the start of transport, within 5 working days of the submission of copy No 3 of the accompanying document, which is confirmed by the beneficiary and the Slovak customs office.
Chart No. 2 — Circulation of the accompanying transport document initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic
Transport from SR
The procedure for transporting alcohol and tobacco products from the Slovak Republic to another Member State of the European Union has been amended by 31 December 2005 as follows:
Under Paragraph 26(4) of Law 105/2004 Z.
‘Pri preprave liehu from the tax warehouse into the tax warehouse of the territory to the tax warehouse but to the authorized referee, or to the tax splnomocnenc in inom memberskom is the odosielatel’ (supplier’) obligatory in the beginning of the preparation to send the kópiu of the first diel of the sprievodní document electronically or fax to the Colný úradu Poprad; túto kópiu is obligatory sowing and the colny mouth of the font into the piatich working days from the dauňa zaratia pre-treatment."
Under Paragraph 22(4) of Law No 106/2004 Z.
‘Pri preprave tabak manufactories from the tax warehouse into the tax warehouse of the territory to the tax warehouse but to the authorized prime minister, or to the tax splnomocnenc in the inom membership is the odosielatel' (supplier’) obligatory in the beginning of the preparation to send a cubicum of the first diel of the sprievodate document electronically or fax to Colný úrad; túto kópiu is obligatory sowing and the colny mouth of the song najneskor to the piatich working days from the dña beginatia pre-treatment."
In the transport of other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) during the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as the ‘controlled period’), the taxpayer was under no obligation to notify the Customs Office of Poprad or the competent customs office of the commencement of services under the suspensive regime.
The tax administrator only became aware of the transport of these products during a local investigation or during a tax inspection from the accompanying documents and from the tax entity's accounting documents.
The consignor in SR is obliged to prepare an accompanying document in four copies before the start of the transport.
Production No 1 shall be retained by the consignor (when transporting alcohol and tobacco products, he shall send a copy of copy No 1 electronically or by fax to the Customs Office of Poprad and to the competent customs office).
Production Nos 2, 3 and 4 accompanies the goods transported.
According to the Czech legislation, the recipient in the Czech Republic will keep copy No 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in the Slovak Republic and confirm the acceptance of the products on the copies No 3 and 4.
The confirmed copy Nos 3 and 4 will be sent no later than the first working day after the end of the transport to the locally competent customs office in the Czech Republic.
The customs office shall retain copy No 4 and copy No 3 to verify the correctness and validity shall be returned to the consignee.
The beneficiary shall send a certified copy No 3 no later than the following working day after receiving it to the Sender to SR.
Transport in the SR is considered to be completed on the day of receipt of the products by the beneficiary.
The end of the transport is demonstrated by the consignor by submitting copy No 3 of the accompanying document confirmed by the recipient and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Graph No. 3 — Circulation of the accompanying document for transport (iron and tobacco products) initiated in Slovakia and terminated in the Czech Republic
In 2006, amendments to all laws on excise duties were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the suspension arrangement is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the local competent consignor before the commencement of the transport.
A document proving the cessation of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products is the copy No 3 of the accompanying document confirmed by the beneficiary and its competent tax authority.
A document proving the cessation of transport of mineral oils, wine and beer is copy No 3 confirmed by the recipient.
Confirmation by the tax administrator of another Member State of receipt of those goods by the consignee shall be required if that controller is required, under the legislation of the competent Member State, to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Records of operations initiated and terminated by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
In order to monitor the transport of goods under a conditional exemption regime between Member States of the European Union, a single electronic system is not in place.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the establishment of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty requires Member States and the European Commission to establish an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) from 1 July 2009 allowing excise tax administrations in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the carriage of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently only used in paper form, and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under the conditional exemption regime and to ensuring a more effective control of the movement of untaxed products across all Member States.
This system will include national databases for each Member State's transport.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transport initiated and terminated on the territory of the Czech Republic in the module Evidence of selected products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have access to the system online.
In the case of transport carried out only on the territory of the Czech Republic, tax authorities may obtain information about the start or end of the service immediately after the registration of the accompanying document by the customs office to EVV.
The customs office shall release the security of the tax on the transported products provided by the consignor at the time of registration by the customs office of the competent beneficiary.
Customs authorities in the SR use a database based on SysNed's application software, which ensures the automation of their activities in the management of excise duties and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse, a tax warehouse operator or an authorised recipient in SysNed's application software, this figure is automatically transferred to the "System for Exchange of Excise Data" database (SEED).
3. Preparation and conduct of cooperation
The first coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO-ČR and representatives of the SAO SR, at which the specific cooperation procedure for the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties was discussed, took place in January 2006.
The two sides became acquainted with the legislation on excise duties and the organisation of excise tax administrations in both states.
Particular attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the SR in authorising or in the initiation and termination of the transport of products subject to excise duty under the conditional exemption regime and the exchange of information between excise tax administrations of both countries.
At the meeting, it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak sides would: - process the total data on the quantities of products subject to excise duty transported from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic and vice versa, the transport of which started in the audited period, - compare the data on mineral oil transport - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and alcohol - the Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 under the conditional exemption scheme initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic and vice versa in the months of November 2004 and September 2005.
During the inspections, the periods examined were extended by the months of October and November 2005 and the transport of tobacco products under the suspensive exemption scheme was also subject to scrutiny in these months.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of products subject to excise duty which were carried under the suspensive tax exemption scheme between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the audited period.
4. Comparison of registrations of goods under suspension of tax
The SAO-ČR handed over to the Slovak side a database of transport terminated in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5 876 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items related to mineral oils, 134 items of alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
The SAO handed over to the Czech side a database of transport terminated in Slovakia, which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 696 related to mineral oil, 2 066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The SAO-ČR compared the data on the traffic listed in the register of initiated traffic in the Czech Republic with data on completed traffic registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are presented in Table 3.
Data on transport in the months of November 2004 and September 2005 compared the SAO-ČR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which the SAO handed over to him at the beginning of the audit.
The database did not contain data allowing reliable transport to be agreed and therefore only 63% of the commenced services were assigned.
Individual services were assigned according to multiple data, e.g. the consignor, the recipient, the date of transport, the quantity of products transported.
Data on traffic initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic in the months of October and November 2005 compared the SAO-ČR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which contained all data according to the accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93% of the commenced services were clearly assigned.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the amount of mineral oils were given in litres or tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
The amount of alcohol was in most cases mentioned in litres, which, however, could be converted into litres of absolute alcohol based on the database of that percentage alcohol content.
The amount of tobacco products was shown in pieces, in thousands of pieces and kilograms depending on the type of tobacco products.
For traffic initiated in the Czech Republic, the termination of which could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or where the information about the transported quantity of products was not met, the accompanying documents were checked.
The control was subjected to accompanying documents for 487 transport of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products.
The examination of these documents was carried out at the customs offices at which the SAO-ČR carried out checks.
For services authorised by other customs offices, the accompanying documents were requested through the DGC.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the implementation of 141 traffic, for which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not substantiate the confirmed copy No 3 of the accompanying document, or did not agree with the quantity of products listed in the database.
Furthermore, data on the services registered in the Slovak database were handed over to the Slovak side, which, however, did not contain the database of transport of the Czech customs administration.
The SAO SR found 95 traffic in the Slovak Customs Administration database.
The verification of the remaining 46 services was requested by the locally competent customs authorities, who proved their termination with copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side copies of the accompanying documents, on the basis of which transport was also identified in the Czech database, with the exception of transport carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of initiated traffic.
A check of these cases was found to be:
- 11 transport of alcohol was registered in the Slovak transport database in the total amount of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 transport of alcohol in a total amount of 404.66 litres of alcohol carried out in 2005.
The SAO-ČR found that it was a transport of taxed products, the start of which the sender does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The freight forwarder informed the tax administrator in writing about the start of the service. He carried out the transport on the basis of accompanying documents used for the transport of products under the suspensive exemption scheme;
- a total of 94 transport of mineral oils, Combined Nomenclature code 2710 11 21, totalling 173 thousand litres realized by the Czech tax entity between September 2004 and December 2005 were registered in the Slovak transport database.
The SAO-ČR found that between May 2004 and June 2005, the tax entity carried out transport of 102,000 litres of untaxed mineral oils without proper authorisation.
The tax entity held a special authorisation for the receipt and use of products exempt, on the basis of which it could supply untaxed products only to the holder of the same authorisation.
He did not notify the opening of the transport authority in the Czech Republic and did not provide a tax security of CZK 1,207,680.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the tax entity delivered 71,000 litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of the SR. Even in these cases, he did not comply with the legal obligation by not announcing the opening of the transport office to the customs office.
The transport of products put into free tax circulation on the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State may be initiated by the consignor in the Czech Republic without the consent of the customs office, but he is obliged to inform the customs office in writing before the commencement of the transport.
A tax entity taking products put into free tax circulation in another Member State is obliged to report quantities and ensure tax before they are withdrawn.
Products may be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are governed by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also accepts the use of the accompanying transport document under the suspensive exemption scheme, which must, however, clearly indicate that it is a ‘simplified accompanying document for the purposes of tax control (excise products)’.
The same rules on transport and acceptance of products put into free tax circulation in another Member State also apply in the Slovak Republic.
In those cases, the tax authorities transported the products put into free tax circulation with the accompanying transport document under the suspensive exemption scheme, the 3rd and 4th copy of which the recipient submitted to the tax administrator in the SR for verification.
The customs authorities in the SR registered these services in the transport database under the suspensive exemption scheme, as the accompanying documents did not state that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the database of transport of the Czech customs administration with the database of transport of the Slovak customs administration and found:
- in the databases the quantity of products transported was reported inconsistently, e.g. mineral oil was given in litres, in hectolitres or in kilograms; alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, making it more difficult to compare the quantity of goods transported,
- the amount of alcohol transported in the invoices did not coincide with the amount recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices listed in the databases,
- two transport of alcohol from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic were registered in the database of the Slovak customs administration carried out in November 2004 in a total volume of 47,237 litres of alcohol, which were not in the database of the Czech customs administration.
The Slovak side handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
The conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for excise duty management were governed by 30 June 2005 by Council Directive 77/799/EEC on mutual assistance between the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxes on insurance premiums.
On 1 July 2005, Regulation No 2073/2004, which lays down rules and procedures allowing the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties, entered into force.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office which shall ensure contacts with other Member States in the field of excise duty management and is responsible for exchanging information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, for securing the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union, a paper was set up at the DGC "Excise Liaison Office" (hereinafter referred to as "ELO ČR").
The safeguarding of tasks related to the management of systems for the control of the movement of excise goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information under mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the SR were carried out with effect from 1 May 2004 by the ELO at the Customs Office of Poprad.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of the ELO Office (based in Poprad) of the Excise Taxation Department of the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic (ELO SR) fulfil the tasks of the ELO.
Pursuant to the provisions of Article 3(3) of Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office is responsible, inter alia, for - the exchange of data held in the SEED electronic register, - the Early Warning System Excise (EWSE), - requests for verification of the movement of excise goods sent to or received by the Movement Verification System (MVS).
The content, scope and functions of SEED, EWSE and MVS are governed by Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - a system for the exchange of information on tax entities trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national registers of excise payers and allows tax administrations in the territory of the European Union to determine whether products subject to excise duty are traded by a person entitled to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States for excise purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information stored in that database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Act No 98/2004 Z. z., § 39 of Act No 104/2004 Z. z., with Section 46 of Act No 105/2004 Z. z., § 40 of Act No 106/2004 Z. z. and with § 39 of Act No 107/2004 Z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, authorised beneficiaries and tax warehouses - SEED database.
The customs authorities in the SR contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, a tax warehouse operator or an authorised recipient in the SysNed application software, which is automatically linked to the ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, an authorised recipient or a tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, they automatically transfer the related data to the SEED database.
The SAO of the SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the customs administration of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place in the audited period usually once a month, exceptionally several times a month.
SR Customs accepted 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
The data to the SEED database in the Czech Republic are transferred from the national register, in which all persons authorised to dispose of products subject to excise duty and issued authorizations to deal with these products are registered.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Applications by customs authorities to provide information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through the ELO CR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
A risk consignment is considered to be, on the one hand, the transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by the European Commission Regulation and, on the other hand, to transport assessed as risky by the tax administrator.
The exchange of information is realized in two forms:
- information - is sent when the limits are exceeded,
- alert message - is sent if the transport of goods is assessed as risky.
When assessing the level of risk of an ELO SR consignment, it uses the SEED database to send a warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
In the event that the SEED database does not agree with the data in the accompanying document (for example, it does not match the registration number of the recipient of the goods or the registered office of the consignee), the ELO SR shall draw up a warning report sent to the ELO of the Member State of the recipient of the goods.
In drawing up the reports, the ELO follows the regulations of the Tax and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457, which determine, among other things, the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measurement for the preparation of explanatory and warning reports.
In the audited period of ELO SR, the ELO sent one warning message to the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, information about started transport of products in quantities exceeding set limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving transport.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic evaluates the consignment as risky on the basis of its own analysis, it will prepare a so-called warning message, which it will send through the ELO ČR to the relevant Member State.
In 2005, the ELO CR sent two warning messages to the ELO SR.
The MVS - the system for controlling the movement of goods - makes it possible, through MVS requests, to control individual transport services of products subject to excise duty as well as the control of a specified route of transport between the entities listed in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information shall take place on the basis of a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system shall be used in particular in cases where the consignor takes receipt of the confirmed copy No 3 of the accompanying document and requires, for example, the refund of excise duty and in cases where the data contained in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
In the audited period ELO SR sent 33 MVS applications to the Czech Republic.
ELO ČR sent ELO SR 25 MVS applications.
Customs authorities in the Czech Republic most often examined the data contained in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantities of products received or dispatched or whether the consignor of the products listed in the accompanying document is entitled to dispose of the products subject to excise duty, unless this fact could be verified in the international SEED database.
The accepted MVS applications were forwarded in both countries to the customs offices locally competent for the recipients or consignors of products subject to excise duty.
The customs authorities examined the required data and reported the outcome of the investigation through the ELO to the other member country.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the SAO-ČR and the SAO SR made it possible to compare the basic legislation governing the area of excise duties in both states, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in initiating and terminating the transport of products under the conditional exemption regime between the two states, the registration of these services and further compare the exchange of information between customs authorities within the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 Compared to the legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, differences were found:
(a) in the procedure of tax entities and tax administrations in initiating the transport of products under the suspensive exemption scheme.
The transport of products under the suspensive exemption scheme can only be initiated by the taxpayer in the Czech Republic with the consent of the tax administrator, who authorises the commencement of transport on condition that the transported products were provided with a tax security equal to the tax attributable to them.
The start of the transport of products under the suspension exemption scheme in the SR is not subject to the authorisation of the tax administrator.
In the audited period, the taxpayer was obliged to notify the tax administrator of the start of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
He was able to commence the transport of mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax authorities of this fact.
In 2006, amendments to all laws on excise duties were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the conditional exemption procedure is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office, which is the locally competent consignor;
(b) within the time limits for dispatch of copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The beneficiary in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copy 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification at the latest on the following working day after the end of the transport.
The verified copy No 3 shall be sent to the consignor no later than the following working day after receiving it from the tax administrator.
The consignee in SR is obliged to send the consignor of the products copy No 3 confirmed by the tax authority and the recipient of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in both Slovakia and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of transport of products under the conditional exemption regime.
The content and method of keeping this register is not regulated by legislation in the Czech Republic or Slovakia.
Customs authorities in both countries shall enter into the register all data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which transport is carried out.
In order to monitor the transport of goods under a conditional tax exemption regime between Member States of the European Union, there is currently no single electronic system that allows excise tax administrations in individual Member States to obtain real-time information on the carriage of goods.
Pursuant to Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, an electronic system for monitoring the transport of products subject to excise duty is foreseen from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of the cooperation agreement in the control activities, the Czech side handed over to the Slovak side a database of transport of products under the conditional exemption regime initiated in Slovakia and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5 876 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak side forwarded to the Czech side a database of transport of products under the conditional exemption regime initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The database contained 3,319 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data on the traffic listed in the register of initiated traffic in the Czech Republic with the registration of traffic terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared the data on the transport of goods under the conditional exemption regime initiated in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of the data was made more difficult by the fact that the quantity of goods transported was not stated uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to clearly attribute the data on individual transports in the two registers, the accompanying documents was checked and the breach of the suspensive exemption scheme and cases of tax evasion were not found.
Based on the findings of parallel checks, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the register of transport to improve the management of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the transport and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council shall allow electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movements under the conditional exemption regime within the territory of the European Union.
Communications
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the chairman of Najýššie's Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic.
Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the follow-up
Introductory word
Taxes generally represent a key source of public revenue.
It is therefore self-evident that the supreme Audit Institutions (SAI) should concentrate their attention on this area.
Examples include value added tax fraud (VAT).
For their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated annually in the European Union (EU).
Already in 2005, the participants of the VI Congress of EUROSAI in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAI can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for control cooperation, as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also the SAO) and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, as well as theBRH) carried out the first parallel VAT control action in 2006.
The report was published in 2008.
As fraudulent VAT negotiations are not limited to a single country but is widespread across the EU, close cooperation between the SAI is needed to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the actions taken to address the problem.
The two SAI therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a subsequent parallel control.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (follow-up)
Objective of control:
(CZ) The aim of the audit was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the VAT administration, in particular to verify the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany") and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The audit action was proposed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
The intention was also to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were intended to compare with the proven practice found (if any).
The audited period covered the years 2006 to 2008, in case of factual context as well as the preceding and following periods, until the end of the inspection.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The subsequent inspection of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
During previous parallel inspections, suspicious cases of intracomonarian transactions were detected.
Some of them required further screening.
On the basis of the control findings, the two SAI formulated a VAT administration recommendation.
The follow-up control action carried out was used to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspicious cases.
The audit also focused, for example, on selected cases of high-risk intracomonality transactions, mutual assistance in debt recovery and the implementation of VAT controls for large tax entities.
When checking the VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors reached the following checks:
1. Recommendations from previous control
• Recommendation 1: Conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
In previous parallel checks, the comparison of VAT registration systems in both countries identified differences.
As different types of registration cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for registering payers within the EU.
This recommendation was made at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter referred to as "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003) called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including a database of tax identification numbers of VAT payers.
He also adjusted common standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
The SAI expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of that document, agreed by EU Member States under ECOFIN, does not already contain the issue.
Both SAI regret notes that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to see this intention as a relevant prevention tool in the fight against fraudulent VAT practices.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly submission of recapitulative statements
As part of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for submitting recapitulative statements, allowing for a more timely examination of the values of intracomonality transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat intra-Community tax evasion limits to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, implemented in Germany from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit recapitulative statements was not introduced monthly within the deadline, in accordance with the EU regulations in force, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve greater reliability of VIES data and consideration of linking the two VAT return systems and for recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, both SAI agreed that an effective risk management system could not be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, the perpetrators of fraudulent activity will be chosen by the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The check found that our two Member States use different risk management systems that have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO audited the EUROCANET system, which allows the exchange of information within the EU, while BRH concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected cases of intracomonality transactions
In the course of the previous audit, commercial transactions were jointly examined for which there were doubts about their execution or irregularities in the reporting of commercial transactions in tax returns or recapitulative statements by the tax payer from both countries.
Both SAI selected nine cases for subsequent inspection, which included the intracomonality movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Checks by the tax authorities of the countries concerned were not concluded at the date of completion of our previous joint control operation.
The subsequent inspection operation verified that most of the tax proceedings in connection with the mentioned selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany had been closed and that adequate measures had been taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT collection or the avoidance of input tax refund).
3. Checking selected cases of risky intracomonant transactions
High risk cases of intracomonality transactions carried out by EU payers that have been included in EUROCANET have been selected for inspection.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risky tax payers within the EU.
The participation of Member States in this system is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant in the scheme if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
Given the fact that the German tax authorities were not involved in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information on which suppliers with German VAT ID were assessed as risky.
As part of the audit, the SAO found both cases of normal commercial transactions and cases suspected of involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent VAT behaviour.
Tax administrators have limited opportunities to control risky transactions, especially as regards so-called missing traders, and mere physical examination of documents can hardly prove any fraudulent conduct to the taxpayer.
A similar situation for tax administrations occurs when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intracomonity carousel shops.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and irregularities in the transport documentation, as well as to monitor their physical movements within the EU towards the end consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to actively engage in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other tools are being used to detect risky tax payers, which until now have worked well for the German tax administration.
In this area, experience between EU Member States needs to be communicated and exchanged.
The Council of the EU has reached political agreement on the draft regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation lies in the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in the use of EUROCANET should be the basis for the creation of this new network to combat VAT fraud.
4. Mutual assistance in debt recovery
In the area of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling applications for international debt recovery assistance in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and BRH have compiled a comparison of the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not coincide.
Both SAIs consider useful to renegotiate the statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent mismatches.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the SAI agree that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission, on the basis of more detailed statistics, to produce an analysis to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the view of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with low recovery rates so that they can increase the recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The SAI analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control for large tax entities (hereinafter also "VDS") in both countries.
In addition, they collected, in the form of a questionnaire, information from tax authorities on areas considered essential by the SAI to manage this issue.
The responses received clearly show that the situation in both countries is developing differently.
The Czech Republic has a system to guide the selection of cases prone to risk, relying on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from tax inspections carried out, balance sheet data and profit and loss statements, etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
The establishment of a specialised tax office for the management of the VDS is planned in 2012.
There is no similar system in Germany yet, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT control in general.
So far, Germany has focused more on the choice of individual cases in question, mainly on the basis of VAT return data and recapitulative statements.
The analysis of these data is based on the different risk management components that will be strengthened.
3. The course of the inspection
3.1 The course of the control action in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by the Department II - the Department of State Budget Revenue and the Territorial Unions IX. Plzen, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited persons were: the Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also the "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 financial offices (hereinafter also "FÚ"): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ v Břeclav, FÚ v Domažlice, FÚ v Hodonín, FÚ v Hradec Králové, FÚ v Chebu, FÚ v Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ v Karlovy Vary, FÚ in Kralupy nad Vltavou, FÚ v Kraslice, FÚ Ostrava I, FÚ Ostrava I, FÚ in Písku, FÚ in Písku, FÚ
The audit conclusion of this audit was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 Progress of the control action in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the Audit Service for Indirect Taxation and Personnel Designated Regional Audit Offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
After selecting a sample of cases, a number of Länder were notified of the mission of the inspection.
In addition to interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, a control event took place in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hesse, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
Included were the tax files of the following tax authorities: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Financial Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, negotiations were held with the tax authorities Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-jih) and financial directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
A report on the audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
As part of the preparation of parallel control actions, a meeting of representatives of the two audit institutions to discuss and determine the control topics took place in September 2008.
Subsequently, in December 2008, the top officials of both SAI signed a cooperation agreement in the implementation of parallel controls.
At a meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the inspection teams informed each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the inspection, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on the way forward.
The second meeting took place in Prague on December 2 - 4, 2009.
The control teams exchanged hitherto accumulated findings together and agreed a timetable for drawing up a joint report.
Both SAI decided to focus on: • follow-up checks on the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report, • examining selected cases of intracomonality transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were not solved during the previous parallel control, • examining selected cases of intracomonant transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were classified as high-risk cases, • control of the process of tax administrations in the area of international VAT recovery assistance, • tax controls of large companies.
The report on the results of the parallel control actions was drawn up during the June 2010 working meeting.
4. Control of VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from previous control
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
Based on the results of the previous audit, the SAO recommended the modification of the VAT registration conditions and the introduction of a new rule for the abolition of registration in the Czech Republic.
Adjusted conditions should make it possible to reduce more effectively the risk of possible tax evasion on VAT collection.
In this context, it was found that the tax authorities in some cases did not use the authorisation to revoke the VAT registration on payers who did not comply with the obligations arising from Act No 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter the VAT Act).
An amendment to the provision consisting in introducing an obligation for tax authorities to abolish VAT registration for VAT payers on repeated non-submission of VAT returns has not yet been proposed by the Czech Ministry of Finance.
Under the VAT Act, the tax administrator may cancel the registration of the tax payer ‘ex offo’ in cases where: (a) the payer did not perform without notice of reason to the tax administrator for 12 consecutive months of performance, (b) the payer fails to comply with his obligations under this Act; (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous inspection, it was found that the legislation in force allowed the FC for Prague 1 to cancel the VAT registration on 31 January of the following calendar year to so-called non-established payers, who were not obliged to declare and pay the tax during the normal calendar year.
The FC for Prague 1 has often not abolished VAT registration for these payers, as the relevant provision has set an insufficient deadline for the deregistration.
This problem was removed by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the non-established tax payer if the taxpayer did not supply any goods or services subject to tax or exempt goods or services with a right to deduct VAT in the preceding calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of recapitulative reports
As part of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for submitting recapitulative statements.
The Council Directive shortens the periods for which recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions are submitted to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
There is also a new obligation to submit recapitulative statements in electronic form.
A summary report must be made to the payer even if the services in respect of which the place of performance is determined pursuant to Paragraph 9(1) of the VAT Act are made available to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State and if he is obliged to declare and pay the tax of the recipient of those services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration compares data on intracomonality transactions reported in VAT returns and recapitulative reports of Czech payers automated in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level
Proper VAT collection is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore among the areas of priority interest and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced, among other things, by the findings of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator attempted to determine the difference between a legitimate and actually collected amount of VAT in the 25 EU Member States (EU-25) during the period 2000-2006.
Based on the analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated amount of VAT loss for the period was between €90 and €113 billion, with an average of 12% of legitimate VAT not levied annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18%.
In the context of international cooperation, the previous control action stated that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by only one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO audited the EUROCANET system used to exchange information in the EU.
