For the inspection, cases of risky intracomonality transactions carried out by EU tax payers, included in the EUROCANET system have been selected (see chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and increasing the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved through the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should improve the cooperation of responsible authorities in a form enabling fraud to be detected in the bud.
This network should later become an important source of information in assessing risks for intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7 October 200812 while setting out the basic principles governing the network.
The preview of EUROFISC is an already functioning system of rapid and selective exchange of information EUROCANET developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky commercial transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations from the first report provided the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
The German tax administration has set up a well-functioning system for registering tax payers, which is based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance alerted the Commission to this system in October 2007.
Improvement of the system is carried out continuously.
Currently, data from the questionnaire are processed electronically and will then be used for exploration as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission has presented a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of the issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to safeguard the level of standards already reached in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of recapitulative reports
On 8 April 2010, a law was adopted on the transposition of EU directives into national law.
This Act contains provisions on the monthly submission of recapitulative statements on intracomonant supplies.
Those provisions entered into force on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative reports to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of linking the two VAT return systems and for recapitulative statements
A joint working group was set up, made up of workers from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance.
The group developed a strategy for automatically comparing data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy has so far been discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the Task Force dealt with a tool designed to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is a party to this exchange under the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of this platform and, following a written consultation of 18 October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 Action Plan.
Platform members are further divided into subgroups that deal with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • influence negotiations, • evaluation, • updates to the Risk Management Guide.
In early 2010, reports on the results of these subgroups were published.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and the cancellation of such registration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included the extension of existing databases within the EU, including a database of tax identification numbers of VAT payers.
He also adjusted common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
For the time being, the issue of registration and the cancellation of registration has been left to the national legislation of EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of the issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already reached in Germany does not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached political agreement on that draft regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States must implement national procedures and only have an obligation to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee about these procedures.
Both SAI regret that the Commission has failed to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome the Commission to make further efforts in this direction.
Monthly submission of recapitulative reports
As part of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for submitting recapitulative statements, allowing for a more timely examination of intracomonal transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat intra-Community tax evasion limits to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010, and took effect in Germany on 1 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced an obligation to submit summary reports monthly according to the set calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in accordance with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of linking the two VAT return systems and for recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of a risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO audited the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU (see cap. 4.3).
In this area, BRH concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected cases of intracomonality transactions
In the previous audit, the implementation of commercial transactions for which there were doubts about their implementation or irregularities in the way in which payers from both countries declared these commercial transactions in their VAT or recapitulative statements were jointly examined.
The two audit institutions selected nine cases for follow-up, including the intracomonality movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, the control of which carried out by the tax administrations of both countries was not completed during the previous joint control action.
1)
The Czech payer acquired goods worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer in the first quarter of 2005.
This acquisition of the goods was not awarded by the Czech payer in his VAT return because the German payer did not have a VAT ID allocated during that period, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that, under the German VAT Act, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States did not have to have a VAT ID allocated to the intracomonality supply of goods.
Subsequent inspection by the SAO found that, on the basis of an inspection carried out by the Czech tax administrator, the Czech taxpayer filed an additional VAT return in which he admitted the acquisition of the goods at that value and at the same time claimed the right to deduct VAT in the same amount in this tax return.
2)
The Czech payer was to acquire €12,561 worth of goods from a German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of these goods was denied by the Czech payer and did not state in his VAT return.
The German tax authorities refused to cooperate at the request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 as the turnover of transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence, he terminated the check without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed in the original amount.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had received two spontaneous information from Germany under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer had invoiced those goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer acquired the goods from the Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in a proper VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
The Czech payer was to acquire a passenger car worth €48,500 from a German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of the goods in question did not award the Czech taxpayer.
This payer has not filed VAT returns since August 2004, so the tax administrator assessed the VAT amount of CZK 0 for that quarter.
On the basis of information obtained in the context of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, in March 2007 the tax administrator invited the payer to file an additional VAT return but not submitted to the payer.
Subsequent inspection found that the tax administrator carried out further acts in the tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the passenger car in question had sold the Czech payer to a car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator issued a payment notice for the December 2004 tax year by which he additionally assessed VAT for the acquisition of goods from another Member State and its subsequent sale in the amount of CZK 295 379.
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was abolished with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of the execution of the liable assets of the tax debtor, this arrears appear to be irrecoverable.
4)
The Czech payer was to deliver new means of transport (personal cars) to Germany during the 4th quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005 with a total value of EUR 198 167.
The reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that there was an unfinished tax-criminal procedure against the German entity in Germany.
Upon subsequent inspection, BRH obtained information that after the conclusion of the tax proceedings in Germany, it was demonstrably established that the German tax payer had been integrated into fraudulent activities.
Intracomonarian acquisitions of goods were taxed at EUR 182 424 (in 2004) and EUR 369 690 (year 2005).
The SAO's follow-up inspection found that the Czech payer was involved in carousel trades with new means of transport.
On the basis of information provided by the German tax administration regarding the examination of the supply of goods, a VAT check was initiated at the Czech taxpayer for the tax years April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the control findings and information obtained in the context of the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally assessed VAT for the May 2005 period of CZK 703 031 and for the June 2005 period of CZK 726 551.
5)
In February 2005, Czech payer A was to acquire a machine worth a total of EUR 58 000 from a German payer.
This German payer was to deliver a machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech payer B in the 3rd quarter of 2004, but the payer B denied this acquisition of the goods.
Subsequent SAO inspection found that the payer B acquired the machine from a German company that had established an organizational unit in the Czech Republic.
Czech payer A did not show the acquisition of goods from a German payer in his VAT return.
The reply from the German tax administrator to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German payer did not make an intracomonial delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000, but the delivery of goods within the Czech Republic.
BRH's subsequent inspection found that after the tax inspection carried out, the intracomonality delivery of the machine was reclassified as the supply of the machine in the Czech Republic and the VAT exemption was abolished.
6)
The German tax payer was to deliver €11,600 worth of goods to the Czech taxpayer in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO's follow-up found that the Czech tax administrator had assessed the submitted additional VAT return, where the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State, including the acquisition of goods of that value, was improperly stated.
BRH found that after receiving a reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax administrator corrected the VAT return on the German payer and additionally charged VAT of EUR 1 600.
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany are subject to tax control.
The aggregate report of the German payer has not yet been corrected, as corrections to recapitulative statements in Germany can only be carried out by the payer who submitted the recapitulative statement.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 whether the Czech tax payer acquired a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German payer in February 2005.
The Czech tax administrator, after a tax procedure carried out for the February 2005 tax year, imposed a tax liability on the Czech taxpayer in the amount of CZK 0 and told the German tax administrator that he could not confirm the acquisition of the car by a Czech payer.
Subsequent SAO inspection found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was abolished in 2007 for non-compliance and the Czech tax administrator sent documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
Subsequent inspection by BRH found that the German payer had changed his seat and the new locally competent tax administrator had revoked the VAT exemption for the supply of the car to the Czech payer on the basis of the inspection carried out.
The German tax payer has not yet corrected the figures in the recapitulative statement and filed an appeal against the tax administrator's decision.
8)
According to data from the VIES system, the German payer supplied the Czech taxpayer with a total value of EUR 33 205 between the 3rd quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
Subsequent SAO audit found that the Czech tax administrator was attempting to determine the causes of the differences arising from the Czech tax payer in the purchase of goods between the 3rd quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax payer has repeatedly filed an additional VAT return for the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not clarify the difference in the value of the acquired goods in the amount of 134 273 CZK for the period 3rd quarter 2004 to Q1 2005, because according to the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture business transactions for individual quarters and therefore the tax administrator accepted the submitted additional tax returns.
9)
The German tax payer delivered €46,854 worth of goods to the Czech taxpayer in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
Over the same period, the Czech payer admitted the intracomonality acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of supplies made in the framework of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of the supply of goods EUR 31 998, a value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data contained in the VIES system.
Subsequent SAO audit found that the Czech payer filed an additional VAT return for the tax year July 2004 to January 2007 after many of the tax administrator's claims.
In that tax return, the taxpayer also exercised the right to deduct VAT, thereby remaining unchanged the tax liability for that tax period.
The follow-up verified that for selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most of the tax proceedings were completed and that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and Germany had taken an adequate measure (i.e. they additionally assessed VAT or prevented input tax refunds).
4.3 Control of selected cases of risky intracomonality transactions
4.3.1 Results of the control in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET may be an important source of information for the detection of risky entities within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with data on purchasers.
Starting on 1st quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic is sending data to EUROCANET on risky transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers.
As part of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for control.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
EUROCANET recorded relevant data from tax authorities from other Member States.
As the German tax authorities did not participate in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information to help determine whether suppliers with German VAT ID had been assessed by the German tax administration as risky entities.
The inspection revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases suspected of involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent VAT behaviour.
Where applicable, the tax authorities used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• Tax administrators did not reveal any suspicion of involvement in risky transactions when verifying the signal information.
The tax authorities shall continuously monitor such tax entities due to their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• During the verification of risky transactions, the tax authorities did not show deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax and VAT base in the submitted accounting, even though they found irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or revealed commercial relationships with suspected or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• The verification of commercial transactions was complicated, as some tax payers did not cooperate with tax administrators and could not be contacted.
Locally competent tax authorities have mostly examined risky tax entities and risky transactions listed in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax administrators in examining risky transactions, particularly in relation to the examination of so-called missing traders , have limited options and only from physical examination of documents makes it difficult to prove fraudulent conduct to the taxpayer.
Stricter requirements for VAT registration and more flexible registration cancellations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered in order to report fictitious supplies of goods within the EU or to issue formally correct tax documents to payers who improperly draw deductions of input VAT on their basis.
In cases where there is a suspicion of the involvement of tax entities in carousel transactions and other frauds and the import and export of goods from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help in identifying goods and irregularities in the transport documentation, as well as in monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that the work of EUROCANET was not attended by three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness of this system, which should be removed by setting up the EUROFISC mandatory network.
4.3.2 The results of the inspection in Germany
BRH analysed the information available at the Federal Central Financial Office, which contained data from EUROCANET.
These figures were the criterion for collecting the six files of the German tax payers for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, has refused to actively participate in EUROCANET.
Germany thus has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but is merely the recipient of the EUROCANET data.
The rationale for this position is contained in the following statement: according to the government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis that would make it possible to violate the provisions in force on the secrecy of tax information.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on how such EUROCANET data is used by other Member States."17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has been carrying out analyses of data from EUROCANET and shall proceed with the Länder's tax authorities in accordance with the agreed procedure.
German tax authorities receive control information on the direct trade relations of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in the EUROCANET system.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relations with traders from other Member States who also maintain business with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
As a result, the control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal large differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
Tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to create a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The Council of the EU has reached a political consensus on a draft regulation, the main contribution of which lies in the establishment of the EUROFISC network.
The envisaged network to combat VAT fraud should also include the experience gained in the use of EUROCANET data.
Member States should therefore communicate their experiences at European level.
On the other hand, cases brought before courts at national and European level show that discussions between Member States and the Commission on the terms of tax exemptions in intracomonality transactions seem necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for debt recovery
4.4.1 International debt recovery assistance in the Czech Republic
The basic regulation of international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU is in particular the following directives:
• Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from operations forming part of the system of financing of the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/EC amending Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from transactions forming part of the system of financing of the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive No. 76/308/EEC was implemented by Act No. 252/2000 Coll., on International Assistance in the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims.
After the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this directive into Czech law and at the same time to amend the mentioned Act No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No.119/2004 Coll., on International Assistance in the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims, was adopted.
The new regulation in the system for regulating international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU is Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28.11.2008.
The Annex to the Regulation sets out new templates of applications that apply from 1 January 2009, a new obligation for electronic communications and an obligation for the requesting authority to certify the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
Guiding principles for the provision of international cooperation in the recovery of claims:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance shall only be granted on the basis of an application containing the prescribed requirements;
3. the assistance shall not apply to financial claims which are in the nature of criminal penalties in the requested State;
4. the provision of international assistance in the recovery of claims shall be followed by the domestic legal order of the State that has been requested for assistance;
5. foreign claims do not take precedence in recovery;
6. assistance is granted only in the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting State, without success, used all applicable possibilities to recover the claim given by its legal order).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines the three forms by which assistance is carried out, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending claims for debt recovery to other EU Member States
The competent tax authority shall electronically send a request for information, a request for service or a request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance through the Financial Directorate.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will provide translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it, including annexes, and send it through the CCN/CSI network to the competent tax authority of the designated state.
There are two basic requirements for enforcement: the claim must be more than EUR 1 500 and must not be more than 5 years old.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receipt of claims recovery from other EU Member States
Upon receipt of a request from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the application as soon as possible within seven days at the latest.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it shall inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the rejection of the request and specifying the specific provisions of the directive it relies on.
This communication must be sent no later than three months after the date of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the application, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify that the application has all the formalities according to the law and should immediately forward the application through the Financial Directorate to the locally competent tax authority for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax administrator ascertains, among other things, the debtor's assets, e.g. by acquiring land registry statements, by ascertaining accounts in banks, by verifying vehicle registration at the DMV, etc.
After a period of six months from the date on which the receipt of the application was confirmed, the Czech Ministry of Finance should communicate to the applicant authority the outcome of the investigation carried out in order to obtain the required information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities where it is not possible to recover the claim, the requesting authority should also be informed of this fact.
Each amount recovered from the tax authority shall be transferred to the requesting authority within CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not impossible for the Czech tax administrator enforcing foreign claims to allow a wait to pay it or pay it in instalments if the state that requested enforcement agrees to do so.
During the period of recovery, the debtor is prescribed interest or penalty payments under Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
This interest or penalty payment belongs to the State that requested enforcement.
In the case of applications for recovery received, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for processing to the locally competent tax authorities in a timely manner, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the context of international debt recovery assistance in the case of applications received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The inspection operation revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with Act No 191/2004 Coll., because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State about the progress made in recovery within six months from the date when the receipt of the application was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistical data
In accordance with the provisions of Section 13(4) of Act No 191/2004 Coll., the Czech Ministry of Finance processes statistical data for the European Commission by 15 March each year, indicating the number of requests for information, delivery or recovery, sent or received in the past year, specifying the amount of claims to which the applications relate.
On the basis of the evidence provided from all EU Member States, the European Commission is preparing a report on the state of recovery, submitted to the Council of the EU and the European Parliament.
The audit found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistical data due to an error in the receivables item in 2008 by EUR 5 250 thousand, by indicating the incorrect value of the claimed VAT claim (this was a shift of the decimal point after converting the claim from Czech crowns to the value in euros).
The error subsequently translated into the statistics of the European Commission.
Mutual assistance information, including the amounts recovered, is provided in the table below.
4.4.2 International debt recovery assistance in Germany
The legal authorisation for international administrative assistance in tax matters is derived from the law of the European Communities, Council Directive 2008/55/EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Directive on debt recovery) and Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In the interests of more accessible formulation and better clarity, the EC Directive on the recovery of claims codifies Council Directive No 76/308/EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by the Law (EC) on the collection of State taxes of 3 May 2003.
The enforcement procedure in Germany is governed by the German fiscal code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities that are valid in national jurisdiction and under the EC Administrative Assistance Act.
Part of the Sixth German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) enshrines the statutory provisions governing the enforcement procedure.
The administrative acts of the tax authorities are governed in particular by enforcement instructions and enforcement instructions.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with representatives of the highest tax authorities of the Länder (Länder) on the principles of administrative assistance in tax assessment and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general prerequisites for filing claims for recovery are as follows:
• The legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic means of recovery have already been exhausted.
• Claims that are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be final.
• From the issue of the enforcement order or the date on which the claim becomes final (i.e. it is no longer the subject of an appeal), no more than 5 years must elapse by the date of submission of applications.
• The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending claims for debt recovery to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementing departments of the tax authorities to the relevant foreign authority, for example the Czech CLO, through the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The closer procedure is governed by the Methodological Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (recovery of claims) of 19 January 2004.25 The working group of the Federal Government and the Land Government is currently reviewing this methodological guideline to adapt it to the Recovery Directive.
The request, including annexes, shall be submitted by the Financial Conduct Authority electronically to the intermediate authority.
This office shall check the accuracy of the application in terms of content and form.
If the application is not correct, it shall be returned to the relevant tax authority.
If it fulfils all the formalities, it shall be referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Tax Office will then ensure the necessary communication with the relevant foreign authority and also ensure the translation of the application.
Procedure for receipt of claims recovery from other EU Member States
Claims for the recovery of claims received from other Member States shall be registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and shall send a certificate of receipt within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check that formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office shall submit these applications to the intermediate authority, which shall then proceed with the relevant tax authorities and monitor their handling.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
Where an application takes more than 6 months to process, the intermediary office shall invite the competent authority to submit a preliminary report which must be made pursuant to Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002/94/DG.
Following an inspection of the formal and factual elements of the application, the implementing services shall notify the method of recovery.
Any amounts recovered must be transferred to the bank account referred to in the application within one month of receipt.
Statistical data
Information on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims between Germany and the Czech Republic in 2006-2008 (as at 31.12.2008) is contained in the table below.
4.4.3 Recovery control, case studies
As part of international cooperation, 21 requests for international debt recovery assistance were selected for inspection between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Examination of the ten selected cases found, among other things:
1.
On 20 October 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received an application from Germany to recover the VAT claim for the years 2004 and 2005 totalling EUR 3 883, i.e. CZK 109 820, for the Czech taxpayer.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the tax administrator an application for recovery only on 26 February 2008.
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
As it was not even possible to pay the entire recovered claim by stopping the properties, a payment plan with instalments of min. CZK 2,000 per month was agreed with the Czech tax entity.
On 31 August 2009, information on the state of recovery was sent to the German tax authorities, with the claim being partially recovered on 25 August 2009 in instalments amounting to CZK 49 600.
This amount was sent to Germany and on 28 August 2009 a further instalment of CZK 3 000 was sent to Germany.
2.
On 7 January 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received an application to recover the tax arrears of the Czech tax entity, which owed EUR 180 869 in Germany, i.e. CZK 4 434 915, to VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the application to the tax administrator only on 27 November 2008.
By checking account ownership of banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movables, the tax administrator found that the debtor did not own any enforceable assets.
Furthermore, a local investigation found that the debtor had not been staying at his permanent address for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This Communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6 April 2009 and on 16 April 2009 the tax administrator's reply was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
On 21 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received an application from Germany for recovery in respect of tax arrears on turnover tax and accessories of the Czech taxpayer in the amount of EUR 3 139, i.e. CZK 84 846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this claim to the tax administrator on 6.8.2008, although already on 18 February 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
On 9 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance notified the tax administrator that the application for recovery was settled by the payment of a claim by a Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also paid in the context of enforcement in the Czech Republic and remitted to Germany on 27.10.2008.
Due to the long time limits in which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the authorized tax administrator, the claim was paid twice in this case - by the entity itself in Germany and the recovery of the claim by the Czech tax administrator.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been set off against the claim from a further recovery application amounting to EUR 6 649, which was to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance records only an application for recovery of a claim of EUR 3 139 for this company, the request for recovery of a claim of EUR 6 649 does not appear in the records of the Czech Ministry of Finance at the company in question.
4.
On 15 September 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received an application from Germany to recover the tax arrears of the Czech tax entity, which owed EUR 39 957 in Germany in income tax and VAT and accessories, i.e. CZK 956 654.
On 19 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax administrator.
On 1 June 2009, the recovery procedure was initiated, an execution was ordered to order a claim on accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and a deduction from wages (the deduction amounted to CZK 7,000).
At the hearing with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it to be questionable.
The Czech tax administrator found that the tax entity had been willing to repay EUR 250 per month in the past, which was not accepted by the German tax administrator.
The tax entity promised to discuss the application with the German tax administrator in order to obtain a change in the amount of its claim.
Recovery of the claim continued during the SAO's audit.
5.
On 19 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a recovery application from Germany concerning the Czech tax entity, which owed in income tax for 2005 and turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories a total of EUR 113 444, i.e. CZK 3 116 304.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent an application to the FÚ for Prague 1, which is entrusted with the administration of the tax on non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, until 14 November 2008, as it was not possible to determine the locally competent tax administrator on the basis of the said address of the tax entity.
In the investigation carried out, the FC obtained information that the debtor had an income of EUR 4 704 on 19 September 2008; however, the FC could no longer issue an execution order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance only forwarded the request for recovery of the claim after that date.
On 26 January 2009, the Czech tax administrator initiated the recovery of the claim and issued an enforcement order to order a claim on the debtor's funds in accounts held with banks and savings and credit unions.
Recovery of the claim continued during the SAO's audit.
6.
The Czech tax administrator applied for international cooperation in recovering the VAT claim and costs totalling CZK 146 223 742 on 3 October 2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for enforcement to the German tax administration until 13.5.2008.
On 8 September 2008, the German tax administrator transferred to the Czech authorities, through the Federal Bank, the amount obtained from the execution of funds in the debtor's account of EUR 17 700, i.e. CZK 439,226.
When verifying the amount of claims recovered, an error was found in the conversion of the amount recovered.
The amount recovered CZK 146 223 742 was converted at EUR 1 = 25,065 CZK erroneously to EUR 583 378.
The correct conversion of the amount recovered is EUR 5 833 781.83.
A claim for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1 March 2007, the Czech tax administrator sent an application to the Czech Ministry of Finance to recover the tax arrears from the Czech tax entity, which owed CZK 1 970 632 for VAT and accessories, i.e. EUR 79 847.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the application to the German tax administration only on 10 November 2008.
On 4. 2. 2009, the German tax administrator asked the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant declines in the company's turnover in the 2nd half of 2008 and in particular in the 1st half of 2009 and the associated liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to cover the arrears: on 8.4.2009, EUR 4 600, on 6.5.2009, EUR 3 000 and on 16 June 2009 EUR 2 500.
These payments were sent to the tax administrator's account in the Czech Republic.
On 23 June 2009, the German tax authority agreed with the debtor to pay a further instalment of EUR 2 500 by 30 June 2009.
8.
The application for recovery of the claim totalling EUR 398 653, i.e. CZK 9 832 779, including the claim for real estate transfer tax, was received from the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22 May 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for enforcement to the German tax administration on 2 October 2008.
On 3 April 2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a communication from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax authorities justified the repayment on the ground that the real estate transfer tax is not a tax within the meaning of Article 2(e), (f), (g) or point (h) of Council Directive 2008/55/EC.
The German tax authorities further stated that Article 2(g) concerns claims relating to income tax and property taxes.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008/55/EC applies to income and property taxes listed in Article 1(3) in conjunction with paragraph 4 of Council Directive 77/799/EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed to draw up and submit a new application for recovery, excluding the arrears of real estate transfer tax in the amount of CZK 61,759 and stating VAT arrears, corporate income tax and personal income tax, which will be again sent to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a new application by the Czech tax administrator for the recovery of tax arrears relating to the same tax entity, which owes CZK 7 079 735 in income and VAT tax.
9.
On 6 February 2006, the Czech tax administrator sent an application to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of the tax arrears of the Czech taxpayer, which owed in personal income tax and VAT amounting to CZK 3 445 782, i.e. EUR 123 328.
Of this amount, the VAT amounted to CZK 1 133 967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the application to the German tax administration only on 18 April 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded the German tax administration's response from the German tax administration dated 9 July 2007 to 11 November 2008.
The reply stated that the German tax administrator had issued an execution order for a bank account with the bank on 11 June 2007, which, however, stated that it had no commercial relations with the tax entity.
By doing so, the German tax administration considered the application to be settled.
10.
On 26 September 2005, the Czech tax administrator sent an application to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT arrears totalling CZK 1 296 845, i.e. EUR 43 591.
The application from the Czech tax administrator was received from the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10 October 2005.
On 15 December 2005, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent the application to the German tax administration.
Before sending the request for enforcement, the Czech tax administrator carried out an execution on the debtor's funds in bank accounts and a deduction from wages and established a lien on immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authority on 16.3.2005.
The reply to a request for information received by the Czech tax administrator on 16 September 2005 showed that the Czech tax entity was staying in Germany and had an income of EUR 8 437 from the non-business activity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20. 4. 2006, but forwarded it to the Czech tax administrator only on 12.2.2008.
The reply stated that no enforcement proceedings could be initiated in Germany because of the insolvency of the debtor - no assets were found on him and his non-business income was already subject to other enforcement proceedings.
In doing so, the German tax administration considered the application for enforcement to be settled.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the area of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling applications for international debt recovery assistance in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and BRH have compiled a comparison of the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not coincide.
In a 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay particular attention to keeping their statistics.
In the 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of non-compliance in the statistics had decreased even though the number of applications had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important that the issues of statistics are renegotiated at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent mismatches, otherwise the data reported by individual EU states in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the two SAIs agree that reliable statistics are intended to show an annual number of applications as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amounts of claims recovered by individual Member States.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by Member States, as this may help Member States to assess their own effectiveness in combating VAT fraud.
The fact that it is possible to calculate the rate of recovery of claims broken down into individual Member States is considered by both SAIs to be useful for Member States with a lower recovery rate to intensify their efforts and to try to improve the recovery rate at least to the level of the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
Especially in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for debt recovery to the locally competent tax authorities on time.
A similar situation was found in applications for international assistance received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The inspection operation revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with Act No.119/2004 Coll., on international debt recovery assistance, because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in recovery within six months of the date when the receipt of the request was confirmed.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for checking VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons who were established or set up for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax year specified in the personal/legal income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion or more.
The inclusion of the taxpayer among the VDS took place after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax year, for the first time for 2003.
The taxpayer ceased to be referred to as the VDS if, in three consecutive tax years, from the end of the period on which he filed the tax return on the basis of which he was included in the VDS, his net turnover for the tax year fell below that threshold.
The taxpayer was not allowed to be removed from the VDS register without carrying out a tax audit of at least one tax per tax period.
All VDS had been checked in at least five years of periodicity until the end of 2009.
From 2010 a written evaluation of the taxpayer must be carried out at least every 2 years and the chosen follow-up must eliminate the tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The audit of the FC is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administrator generally chooses several tax periods at once.
The VDS was audited by departments of specialised controls, which are set up in a total of 13 FCs, or by the staff of the control departments of locally competent FCs.
The Department of Specialised Controls carries out tax inspections within the scope set by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• Tax entities operating in unusual and specific fields of business;
• entities where carrying out tax control is technically and time-consuming;
• entities with a sprawling territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• entities linked in chains and networks suspected of large-scale tax evasion and unauthorised avoidance of excess deductions.
The number of tax checks carried out by the departments of the FCA and the results of these checks are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No. 531/1990 Coll., on Territorial Financial Authorities, which consists of establishing a dedicated FC with a nationwide competence for selected tax entities (i.a. for legal entities established for business purposes, which achieved a turnover of more than 2 billion CZK).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls for large companies are governed by the same rules as tax controls in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • the German fiscal code (AO), • the Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • Tax Controls (BpO) regulations.
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions on control are enshrined in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - Tax On-the-spot checks. In particular, those articles enshrine the rules on the admissibility of on-the-spot tax control (i.e. at the premises of the undertaking), their scope in terms of subject-matter, rules on the division of responsibilities, the form and content of the inspection notice, the principles of control, the obligations of the taxpayer to cooperate and the preconditions for the implementation of the final consultation and the communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax inspections are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Administration Act According to Article 5.1, point 1, in connection with Article 19 of the Act, participation in tax controls on the spot by the tax authorities is mandatory for the Federal Central Financial Office.
The participating authorities shall agree on the spot the nature and extent of the Federal Central Tax Office's participation in tax inspections.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the specific undertakings it collects are subject to scrutiny at the time it determines.
In such a case, it may declare rules for the implementation and content of the inspection at the premises of these companies.
Tax control regulations According to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the regulations on tax inspections (German abbreviation BpO 2000) were agreed by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper house of the German parliament, in which the governments of the Länder are represented).
These administrative rules apply to on-the-spot checks carried out by the tax authorities of the Länder as well as by the Federal Central Tax Office.
Businesses shall be classified by size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BpO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to follow-up (Article 4.2 BpO).
Under Article 33.1 BpO 2000, each informed tax office must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in BpO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the additional methodology for tax administration sets out the following guidelines:
• Single manual for special VAT checks in Germany ;
• the USLO Manual, which sets out a methodology for the use of data on intracomonant trade relations conducted in VIES;
• ZAUBER manual setting out the methodology for using the ZAUBER database;
• work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits according to the type of business.
The figures are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to control - not just large businesses - must be set at regular check intervals.
As a general rule, checks on large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually declared including VAT checks.
This means that during the course of the inspection, checks will be definitively carried out primarily on income tax, excise duty and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks can be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisational arrangements of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by controls is usually between three and five years.
BpO 2000 foresee a three-year control period.
The subject of the screening is all the taxes of the company.
4.5.3 Management of control of large tax entities
Both SAI decided not to examine individual cases of VDS controls carried out, but focused on management issues to get an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VAT controls at VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax administrations about the areas they consider essential for the management of the issue.
• What statistical records and analyses relating to VAT control of VDS have at its disposal to the management of tax administrations?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or records of rates in which there is a distinction between the fight against VAT fraud and, more generally, VAT control?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system at the current data version does not allow such a resolution.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between the control proposed to combat VAT fraud and the general VAT control.
• Are there any statistics or records of the timeliness of VAT controls (in relation to the time period of transactions checked)?
Czech Republic: Registration of timeliness of questioning with relevance to intracomonality acquisition of goods for selected VAT payers is reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, data such as how long it took to inquire are part of the information recorded in the ADIS system.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors contain only information on the average recent check (information on the year).
This figure does not provide an overview of selected control periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the latest period of tax assessment; they also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, the statistics produced at the Federal level for the units of special VAT controls do not provide information regarding the classification of tax entities.
• There are some statistics or records of the nature of the additional tax revenue generated, broken down, for example, according to the following criteria:
i. net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where the taxpayer improperly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only a nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. the transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax year);
iii. additional collection of tax revenue (payment of additional tax due due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the amounts of the additional tax assessed by the type of tax, the number of tax entities audited and the number of tax years checked.
Other tax procedures (local investigations, complaint procedure) are monitored in the same way.
As a separate task, time figures and amounts of additional taxes are recorded.
Statistics of general debts broken down by type of tax are also kept, but not according to the declared tax or tax determined by the tax authorities.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and for the units of special VAT checks do not distinguish between the above criteria.
Moreover, these differences are not distinguished by the majority of tax administrations visited.
• Are control areas registered that generate high additional returns?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to collect the tax payer for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in the special ADIS sections.
Germany: There are no regulations at the federal level.
It then follows that uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and for specialised VAT control services do not provide such data.
Nevertheless, there is one coordinated approach by the finance ministers of the Länder and the Federal Government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must write down an obligation imposed by them on the increased tax (VAT) basis if they exceed a certain amount.
In such a case, they must specify, for example, the nature of the assessed increase in tax liability.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- VDS exercise an unjustified right to deduct input tax for supplies and services:
• which were not used to carry out any economic activity under Section 72(1) of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation pursuant to Section 75(3) of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents which did not meet the requirements set out in Section 73(1) of the VAT Act;
- VDS did not declare output VAT under Section 21(1) of the VAT Act.
Germany: It was said that there were no regulations at the federal level.
It then follows that uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and for specialised VAT control services do not provide such data.
VAT findings are not separately registered by the Länder if they result from VDS tax inspections.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must write down their assessed increased tax (VAT) obligation if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration carry out analyses of the areas of control from which there is a high "return" and draws the consequences for the management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching nationwide audits focused on risky commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at the federal level.
Uniform statistics at the Federal level for tax inspectors and for special VAT control services do not provide data on audit areas that generate high "revenue".
There are different views on the analysis process, as well as on the management of cases in terms of relevance.
Some regional tax authorities provide special information, but their use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
Differences in the replies of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects the amount of data from the tax inspections carried out, as well as data from financial statements - balance sheets and profit and loss statements.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to channel the selection of cases prone to risk.
The same is true of the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, the establishment of a specialised tax office for the administration of VDS is planned in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
It follows, then, that it is more difficult to carry out those tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places greater emphasis on the choice of individual cases based on data from submitted tax returns.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAI agree that Member States should be able to provide adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce shortfalls in VAT revenues.
As a result, the return on VAT collection will increase and the level of risk detection for unreliable entrepreneurs will also improve.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of the two SAI on parallel checks of the VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and BRH.
The two SAI have better recognised each other's applicable systems in the following areas: • intracomonality transactions, • VAT risk management, particularly in terms of risk collection of transactions, • assistance in the recovery of VAT receivables and • VAT control for large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud detection strategies as well as differences in the above mentioned areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany were revealed.
The control findings were compared and proven practices were identified on the basis of them.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to launch a debate on approaches and strategies within, including at European Commission level.
Extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT administration.
6. Communications
The report was drawn up in the Czech, English and German languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and by the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Ediency deadline: June 2010.
